Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Anti 'Alayya Haram Ka-Zahri Ummi'
Presenting the dispute among Hanafi imams on the meaning of the ambiguous phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the phrase 'Anti 'alayya haram ka-zahri ummi' and explain the Hanafi proof that the explicit (sarih) term overrides the ambiguous (muhtamil).

Core Idea
When an explicit phrase for zihar is used, intention cannot change it to divorce or ila'.

In this passage from the Hidayah commentary, we encounter a classic intra-Hanafi debate: does the husband's intention matter when he says 'You are forbidden to me like my mother's back'? Abu Hanifa insists the explicit phrase controls, while the two companions give weight to intention. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the underlying usul principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance and the parties
The utterance is 'Anti 'alayya haram ka-zahri ummi'. The scholars involved are Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Note that the Sahibayn disagree with Abu Hanifa and also differ among themselves.
Also note that Imam Ahmad agrees with Abu Hanifa.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: only zihar (regardless of intention). Abu Yusuf: both zihar and divorce occur if divorce intended. Muhammad: only divorce occurs if divorce intended (zihar invalidated by baynunah).
If ila' intended, similar logic applies.
3
Analyze the proofs of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn argue that 'anti 'alayya haram' is ambiguous and can mean zihar, divorce, or ila'. Therefore intention should determine the ruling. Muhammad adds that after a ba'in divorce, zihar is invalid. Abu Yusuf says both parts operate independently.
Muhammad's proof relies on the condition of validity of zihar after baynunah.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that 'ka-zahri ummi' is sarih (explicit) for zihar and is muhkam (unambiguous). Therefore it cannot bear any other meaning. The ambiguous part is turned towards the explicit part by the rule 'al-muhtamil yuhmal 'ala al-muhkam'.
This is a fundamental usul principle applied here.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view. The practical consequence: if a husband says this, he must perform zihar expiation; he cannot claim a different intention to avoid it.
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah.

Chapter of Zihar. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume five. Near that it will be nothing except zihar. And the two companions (Sahibayn) said: whatever he intends, that will be. Because making haram (tahrim) has probability for every matter, as we have already explained. Except that according to Imam Muhammad, when he intended divorce, then it will not be zihar; and according to Abu Yusuf, it will be both divorce and zihar, and this is mentioned in its place. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that this speech is explicit (sarih) in the meaning of zihar, so it cannot have any other probability. Then it is muhkam (authoritative), so this making haram (tahrim) will be turned towards the prohibition of zihar. Explanation of the case: A man said to his wife: "Anti 'alayya haram ka-zahri ummi" (You are forbidden to me like the back of my mother). And he intended divorce or ila' by this speech. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this speech is only zihar, and Imam Ahmad agrees with him. According to the two companions, it will be whatever he intended: if he intended zihar, it is zihar; if he intended divorce, it is divorce; if he intended ila', it is ila'. The proof of the two companions is that his speech "Anti 'alayya haram" has probability for each of the mentioned matters, and intention is valid due to probability, therefore the ruling will be according to his intention. But there is also a difference between the statements of the two companions: According to Imam Muhammad, if he intended divorce by this speech, then only divorce will occur, and this speech will not be zihar. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, this speech will be both divorce and zihar. Imam Muhammad's proof is that when the husband said "Anti 'alayya haram" to his wife and intended divorce, then a ba'in divorce occurs; after that, with "ka-zahri ummi" zihar will not occur because after severance (baynunah) zihar is not valid. And Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that divorce will occur due to his intention, and "ka-zahri ummi" is explicit in the meaning of zihar. Therefore this person will also be counted as one who does zihar, and he will not be believed in turning the speech from its apparent meaning. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the word "ka-zahri ummi" is explicit in the meaning of zihar. This is why this word does not need intention to indicate zihar. So in this word there cannot be any probability of divorce and ila' besides zihar. Then the word "ka-zahri ummi" is muhkam (authoritative) in the meaning of zihar due to the absence of probability of other meanings, and "Anti 'alayya haram" has the probability of many meanings, and the rule is that the probable (muhtamil) is turned towards the muhkam. Therefore "Anti 'alayya haram" is also turned towards zihar.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the interpretation of the statement 'Anti 'alayya haram ka-zahri ummi' (You are forbidden to me like the back of my mother). The issue is whether this utterance constitutes zihar (a form of unlawful speech that requires expiation), divorce (talaq), or an oath of abstention (ila'). The passage presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with their respective proofs. Abu Hanifa holds that the phrase 'ka-zahri ummi' is explicit for zihar, making the entire utterance a clear case of zihar regardless of intention. He is supported by Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. The two companions (Sahibayn) argue that the earlier part 'anti 'alayya haram' is ambiguous and can refer to zihar, divorce, or ila', so the husband's intention determines the ruling. Within Sahibayn, there is further disagreement: Imam Muhammad says that if divorce was intended, only divorce occurs and zihar does not follow because after a ba'in divorce zihar is invalid; Imam Abu Yusuf says both divorce and zihar occur because the two parts can operate independently. Abu Hanifa's reasoning relies on the principle that the explicit (sarih/muhkam) term overrides the ambiguous (muhtamil) term, so the entire speech is interpreted as zihar.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A form of divorce-like speech where a husband compares his wife to a mahram relative, making her temporarily forbidden until expiation.
محکم (muhkam): A speech that is unambiguous and cannot bear multiple interpretations, as applied to 'ka-zahri ummi' in this context.
صریح (sarih): Explicit or clear in its meaning, not requiring intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is both zihar and divorce.
D) It is ila'.

Key Takeaway
The explicit phrase 'ka-zahri ummi' makes the utterance solely zihar, and the husband's contrary intention is irrelevant in Hanafi law.

Zihar with a Slave-Girl is Invalid
Ruling that zihar with a slave-girl is invalid, with three proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zihar with a slave-girl and explain the three proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Zihar with a slave-girl is invalid because a slave-girl is not a wife, and zihar is linked to divorce.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: that performing zihar with one's own female slave has no legal effect. The passage provides three distinct proofs — from the Quran, from legal analogy, and from the historical nature of zihar — to establish that a slave-girl cannot be the subject of zihar. Understanding these proofs will sharpen your ability to assess how the Hanafi school interprets textual and rational evidence.

Guided Path
1
Quranic Proof
Identify the key phrase from Surah al-Mujadilah (58:2): 'min nisa'ikum' (from your wives). Explain that the word 'nisa'' in this context is restricted to wives, not including slave-girls, because the verse was revealed about wives.
The general linguistic meaning of 'nisa'' may include women, but the occasion of revelation restricts it to wives.
2
Status-Based Proof
Explain that a slave-girl's legal status is defined by ownership, not marriage. She is not a 'wife' (zawja) in Islamic law. Therefore, she cannot be analogized to a wife for the purpose of zihar.
A slave-girl may be a concubine, but she is not a wife unless explicitly married.
3
Historical Proof
Trace the origin of zihar as a form of divorce in pre-Islamic Arabia. In Islam, zihar became a temporary prohibition requiring expiation, but its link to divorce remains. Since a slave-girl cannot be divorced (her relationship is severed by freeing or sale, not divorce), zihar cannot apply.
This proof connects zihar to the concept of divorce, which requires a valid marriage.
4
Synthesize the Ruling
Combine the three proofs to confirm that zihar with a slave-girl is batil (void). The man is not a muzahir, no expiation is due, and the slave-girl remains unaffected.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس نے اپنی باندی سے ظہار کیا تو یہ شخص ظہار کرنے والا شمار نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے من نسائکم [؟] اور لفظ (نساء) بیویوں کے لئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے اور مملوکہ باندی بیوی نہیں کہلاتی لہذا اس سے ظہار بھی [؟] نہیں ہوگا۔ یہ بات واضح رہے کہ یہاں [؟] کی تغیر [؟] زوجات اور بیویوں کے ساتھ مقصد آیت کو سامنے رکھتے ہوئے کی گئی ہے ورنہ نساء امراۃ کی [؟] جمع ہے جو بیوی اور غیر بیوئی سب کو شامل ہے۔ (عینی شرح ہدایہ) دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندی کی حالت اس کے مملوک ہونے کے تابع ہے لہذا اس کو منکوحہ کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کر سکتے۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ظہار زمانہ جاہلیت میں طلاق تھا پھر اس کو ظہار کے موجودہ حکم یعنی تحریم موقت بالکفارہ کی طرف نقل کر لیا گیا۔ لہذا جس کو طلاق دی جا سکتی ہے اسی سے ظہار بھی کیا جا سکتا ہے اور چونکہ مملوکہ باندی کے حق میں طلاق نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے اس سے ظہار بھی نہیں ہو سکتا۔
If someone performed zihar with his slave-girl, then this person will not be considered one who performed zihar. The proof is that Allah Almighty said 'min nisa'ikum' and the word 'nisa' is used for wives, and a female slave owned is not called a wife, therefore zihar will not occur with her. It should be clear that here the [؟] of the verse is done keeping in view the wives as the purpose of the verse, otherwise the word 'nisa' is a plural of 'imra'a' and includes both wives and non-wives. (Ayni Sharh al-Hidayah) The second proof is that the condition of the slave-girl is subject to her being owned, so she cannot be attached to [the category of] wife. The third proof is that zihar was divorce in the time of ignorance, then it was transferred to its current ruling, i.e., temporary prohibition with expiation. Therefore, zihar can only be done with someone who can be divorced, and since there is no divorce regarding a female slave, zihar cannot be done with her.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its evidences. The ruling is that zihar with a female slave is invalid. The author provides three proofs: (1) Quranic: Allah says 'from your wives' (min nisa'ikum) in the verse on zihar, and a slave-girl is not called a 'wife' in Islamic law. The author notes that although the word 'nisa'' can include non-wives, the context of the verse specifically addresses wives. (2) The slave-girl's legal status is defined by her being owned, not by marriage, so she cannot be analogized to a wife. (3) Zihar originated as a form of divorce in pre-Islamic times, and in Islam it continues to be linked to divorce (only those who can be divorced can make zihar). Since a female slave cannot be divorced (her relationship ends by dissolution of ownership, not talaq), zihar is not valid with her. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' which in Islam becomes a temporary prohibition requiring expiation.
باندی (bāndi): A female slave owned by a person.
نساء (nisa'): Plural of imra'a; in the context of zihar verse, it specifically means 'wives' as per the purpose of the verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the primary Quranic evidence that zihar with a slave-girl is invalid?
A) The verse says 'from your wives' (min nisa'ikum), and a slave-girl is not a wife.
B) The verse prohibits all forms of zihar.
C) The verse requires the woman to be free.
D) The verse mentions expiation, which a slave cannot perform.

Key Takeaway
Zihar with a slave-girl is legally void because the Quranic restriction 'from your wives' excludes slave-girls, a status-based analogy confirms it, and the historical link to divorce limits zihar to women who can be divorced.

Zihar Void in Marriage Without Wife's Consent
Ruling that zihar is void if wife later approves a marriage contracted without her consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zihar made in a marriage contracted without the wife's consent and explain why subsequent approval does not validate it.

Core Idea
Zihar is void if marriage was invalid at the time; later approval does not retroactively validate it.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a man marries a woman through an unauthorized third party (fudūlī) without her consent, then makes a zihar statement (comparing her to his mother). Later, the woman approves the marriage. Does the zihar become effective? The Hanafi school rules it is void ab initio. The key lies in the definition of zihar as 'ugly and false speech'—truthfulness negates it. The lesson also explores an objection based on qiyas with freeing a slave bought from a usurper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A man marries a woman through a fudūlī (unauthorized agent) without her permission, then makes a zihar statement. Later, the woman approves the marriage. What is the ruling on the zihar?
The marriage was suspended (mawqūf) at the time of the zihar.
2
State the Ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that the zihar is void (bāṭil). Even after the wife's approval, it does not become valid.
The text explicitly says 'faz-zihar bāṭil'.
3
Understand the Reason
Zihar is defined in Quran (58:2) as 'munkar min al-qawl wa zūr' (ugly and false speech). At the time of the statement, the woman was not his wife (since the marriage was not yet binding), so the comparison to a mahram was truthful—she was actually a stranger. Truthfulness negates the essence of zihar.
The rukn (pillar) of zihar—falsely comparing a wife to a mahram—was missing.
4
Address the Objection via Qiyas
An objector might argue by analogy: when a person buys a slave from a usurper and frees him, and later the owner approves the sale, the freeing becomes valid. Similarly, approval of the marriage should make the zihar valid.
This is the counterargument considered in the text.
5
Distinguish Based on Rights
The Hanafi response: freeing a slave is a right of ownership (ḥuqūq al-milk), which is lawful. Zihar is not a right of marriage; marriage is lawful, but zihar is unlawful. Therefore, the analogy fails because the 'illa (effective cause) differs.
The distinction is between rights arising from lawful ownership versus an unlawful act.

Source Text

(If he married a woman without her command, then he made zihar with her, then the woman accepted the marriage, the zihar is void. For if he married a woman without her order, then made zihar with her, then she accepted the marriage, the zihar is void because he was truthful in the analogy at the time of the action, so he was not one who said ugly and false speech. And zihar is not a right from his rights such that it should be suspended. Contrary to the freeing of the purchased slave from a usurper, because freeing is from the rights of ownership.) Commentary
This passage deals with a specific case: a man marries a woman through a third party (fuduli contract) without her consent, then makes zihar with her, and later she approves the marriage. The ruling is that the zihar is void. The reason given is that at the time of the zihar statement, he was truthful in comparing her to a mahram because she was not legally his wife (the marriage was not yet binding). Since the essence of zihar is 'ugly and false speech' (munkar min al-qawl wa zura), truthfulness negates it. The text then addresses an objection: why doesn't the zihar become valid upon subsequent approval, like the freeing of a slave by a buyer from a usurper becomes valid upon the owner's approval of the sale? The answer is that zihar is not a right arising from marriage; marriage is a lawful (mashru') act, while zihar is unlawful (ghayr mashru'). Rights come from lawful acts. Freeing a slave, however, is a right arising from ownership, which is a lawful right. Therefore, the analogy fails. This shows the Hanafi method of distinguishing between qiyas cases based on the nature of the rights involved.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): An unauthorized third party who contracts on behalf of another without permission.
منكر من القول وزورا (munkar min al-qawl wa zura): Ugly and false speech; the Quranic description of zihar (Surah 58:2). If the statement is truthful, it is not considered zihar.
حقوق الملك (huquq al-milk): Rights arising from ownership, such as the right to free a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the woman's approval only affects the marriage, not the zihar.
B) Because zihar is an ugly and false speech, and it was truthful at the time.
C) Because zihar is not a right of marriage, unlike freeing which is a right of ownership.
D) Because the husband must repeat the zihar after approval.

Key Takeaway
A zihar statement made before a marriage becomes valid is void, and subsequent approval does not revive it because it was truthful at the time and is not a right of marriage.

Zihar to Multiple Wives: One Statement, Multiple Expiation
Ruling that one zihar statement to all wives requires separate expiation for each

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that one zihar statement to multiple wives requires separate expiation for each wife and evaluate the Maliki/Hanbali counter-argument.

Core Idea
Each wife becomes individually prohibited (hurmat) — so the expiation multiplies with the number of wives.

When a husband says to his wives collectively, 'You are all to me like the back of my mother,' the ruling on expiation (kaffarah) becomes disputed. While some schools see a single expiation sufficient by analogy with ila', the Hanafis insist on separate expiation for each wife. This lesson examines the reasoning behind each view and the crucial distinction between zihar and ila'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act of zihar? What does the Hanafi school hold when a man addresses all his wives with one zihar statement?
The man becomes a muzahir to all wives by consensus.
2
Locate the opponent's dalil
Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad analogize to ila' – in ila', one kaffarah suffices for multiple wives. Identify their qiyas.
Their evidence: the ila' scenario requires only one expiation even for multiple wives.
3
Trace the Hanafi response
Why does the analogy to ila' fail? The kaffarah in zihar is to remove the individual prohibition of each wife; in ila', it is for violating Allah's name.
The effective cause (illah) differs: in zihar it is personal hurmah; in ila' it is oath violation.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under Hanafi, separate expiations must be performed before each wife can be approached. Under Maliki/Hanbali, one suffices.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is multiple expiations.
5
Confirm the tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position relied upon? The text states the Hanafi proof is based on the nature of hurmah, a stronger ta'lil.
None.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ومن قال لنسائه انتن على كظهر امي كان مظاهرا منهن جميعا لانه اضاف الظهار اليهن فصار كما اذا اضاف الطلاق و عليه لكل واحدة كفارة لان الحرمة تثبت في حق كل واحدة والكفارة لانهاء الحرمة فيتعدد بتعددها بخلاف الايلاء منهن لان الكفارة فيه لصيانة حرمة الاسم و لم يتعدد ذكر الاسم

(And whoever said to his women: 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' he becomes a muzahir to all of them because he attributed the zihar to them, so it is as if he attributed divorce to them. And upon him is a kaffarah for each one, because the prohibition is established for each one, and the kaffarah is to remove the prohibition, so it multiplies according to their number. Unlike ila' with them, because the kaffarah in ila' is for protecting the honor of the name (of Allah) and the mention of the name is not multiplied. Then the commentary: ...
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a man who has multiple wives and says to them collectively: 'You are all to me like the back of my mother.' The unanimous ruling is that he becomes a muzahir (one who has made zihar) to all of them. The reason is attribution: he directed the statement to all, similar to saying 'you are all divorced' (antunna tawaliq). Then the issue of kaffarah arises: does he owe one kaffarah for all or separate kaffarah for each wife? The Hanafi and Shafi'i positions, along with scholars like Hasan al-Basri, al-Awza'i, al-Zuhri, and al-Thawri, hold that he owes a separate kaffarah for each wife. Their evidence is that each wife individually becomes haram to him (hurmah), and the kaffarah is designed to remove that specific prohibition. Since the prohibitions are multiple, the expiations are multiple. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad argue that one kaffarah suffices, drawing an analogy with ila' (swearing to abstain from intercourse). In ila', if a man says 'La aqrabu bikhunna' (I will not approach you all) and then breaks his oath within four months, he owes only one kaffarah for all. They analogize zihar to ila'. The Hanafis distinguish: in ila', the kaffarah is for violating the oath, which involves the name of Allah (one swear word), not for removing women's prohibition. In zihar, the kaffarah is to lift the prohibition from each wife individually. Thus multiple expiations are required. The practical consequence: the man must expiate separately before resuming intercourse with each wife.

Key Terms
حرمت (hurmat): The marital prohibition that is established for each wife individually by the zihar statement.
ایلاء (ila'): A husband's oath to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for four months or more.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required to remove the prohibition caused by zihar; options: freeing a slave, fasting two months, feeding sixty poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why, according to the Hanafi madhhab, does a man who makes zihar to all his wives owe a separate expiation for each wife?
A) Because he used the plural form, so each wife is addressed separately.
B) Because the prohibition (hurmah) is established for each wife individually and the kaffarah removes that prohibition.
C) Because the Quran commands multiple expiations for multiple wives.
D) Because the man intended multiple zihars.

Key Takeaway
Each wife becomes individually prohibited; therefore, the expiation must be performed separately for each wife.

Kaffarah of Zihar: Sequence and Timing Before Intercourse
States sequential kaffarah options and their timing before intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sequential options for kaffarah of zihar and explain why all must be performed before intercourse.

Core Idea
The kaffarah of zihar follows a fixed sequence: free a slave, fast, or feed — all before intercourse.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic form of divorce that Islam regulated by requiring expiation (kaffarah) before the husband can resume relations. The Quran provides a clear sequence of options. This lesson examines the obligatory order and the timing requirement, based on the verse's wording and Hanafi interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its sequence
Read the passage to find the three options for kaffarah: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, and feeding sixty poor persons. Note that they are presented in a fixed order.
The order is not optional; each subsequent option only applies if the previous is impossible.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse (Surah al-Mujadilah 3-4) cited in the passage. Note that the phrase 'min qabli an yatamassa' (before they touch) appears for both freeing and fasting.
The verse uses the particle 'fa' to connect each option, indicating sequence not choice.
3
Analyze the linguistic indicator for sequence
Focus on the word 'fa' in the Arabic text. In usul al-fiqh, 'fa' denotes tartib (order) unless there is evidence to the contrary. This establishes that the kaffarah must follow the given sequence.
This is a key point of Hanafi reasoning: the literal meaning of 'fa' is sequence.
4
Apply the timing requirement to all options
The text explicitly states for freeing and fasting that they must be 'before intercourse'. By analogy (qiyas), the same applies to feeding, since the purpose of kaffarah is to remove the prohibition before resuming relations.
The commentator argues that feeding also must precede intercourse because the effective cause (illa) is the removal of prohibition.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on the cause of kaffarah
The passage mentions that the majority hold the cause is zihar plus return (ruju), while some say it is only return. Understand that this difference affects when kaffarah becomes obligatory but not the sequence or timing.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

باب الظهار
کفارہ ظہار کب ادا کرے
قال وكل ذالك قبل المسيس و هذافي الاعتاق والصوم ظاهر للتنصيص عليه و كذافي الاطعام لان الكفارة فيه منهية للحرمة فلابد من تقديمها على الوطى ليكون الوطى حلالاً
ترجمہ کہا اور ہر ایک امر اس کے وطی کرنے سے پہلے ہے اور وطی سے پہلے ہونا آزاد کرنے اور روزہ رکھنے میں ظاہر ہے کیونکہ اس پر صریح نص ہے اور یہی حکم کھانا دینے میں ہے اس لئے کہ ظہار میں کفارہ دینا حرمت کو ختم کرنے والا ہے تو اس کا ولی سے مقدم کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ ولی حلال واقع ہو۔
تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ ظہار کا کفارہ خواہ بالا عتاق ہو یا بالصیام یا بالا طعام ہر ایک کا وطی سے پہلے ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اعتناق اور صیام میں تو صراحہ نص ( من قبل ان تما سا) موجود ہے اور رہا اطعام تو اس کا بھی قبل الوطی ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ کفارہ ظہار حرمت کو ختم کرنے والا ہے اس لئے ضروری ہوا کہ کفارہ ولی پر مقدم ہوتا کہ ولی حلال واقع ہو۔
Chapter of Zihar. It is wajib and since from all women in one ila, the name of Allah is not multiplied [؟] so one kaffarah is wajib, not multiple. Section on Kaffarah. Translation: This section is on the rulings of kaffarah. Explanation: Previously the author mentioned the ruling of zihar, i.e., prohibition of intercourse and prohibition of its continuation. Therefore in this section we will mention that which removes this prohibition, i.e., kaffarah. Scholars differed about its cause. According to the majority of mashayikh, the cause of kaffarah is zihar and returning to the wife. Because in the Quranic verse 'Those who declare zihar from their women then return to what they said, then freeing a slave' Allah connected 'return' (awd) to zihar with 'thumma', then attached the ruling with 'fa'. The rule is that when a ruling is mentioned after a conjunction, it belongs to both conjuncts. So the combination of zihar and return is the cause. In Minni Sharh Hidayah it is mentioned that the cause is only return. And Allah knows best. Kaffarah of Zihar. He said: 'And the kaffarah of zihar is freeing a slave, then if he does not find, fasting two consecutive months, then if he cannot, feeding sixty poor persons, due to the text that came for it; indeed it informs the kaffarah on this order.' Translation: He said: The kaffarah of zihar is freeing a slave, then if he does not get a slave, he should fast two consecutive months, then if he has no capability, he should feed sixty poor persons, because of the text that came in the chapter of zihar, for that text informs the kaffarah with this order. Explanation: Imam Quduri stated the order of kaffarah for zihar: free a slave; if unable, fast sixty consecutive days; if unable, feed sixty poor persons. The proof is the Quranic text: 'Freeing a slave before they touch...' This text indicates order because Allah used the word 'fa' which comes for sequence, not choice. Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah volume 5, page 117, Chapter of Zihar. When to perform kaffarah of zihar. He said: 'And everything of that is before intercourse. And this in emancipation and fasting is apparent due to the explicit text, and likewise in feeding because the kaffarah in it terminates prohibition, so it is necessary to precede it over intercourse so that intercourse becomes lawful.' Translation: He said: Every matter is before intercourse, and being before intercourse is apparent in freeing and fasting because there is explicit text on it, and the same ruling applies to feeding because in zihar, giving kaffarah removes prohibition, so it is necessary for it to precede intercourse so that intercourse becomes lawful. Explanation: He says that the kaffarah of zihar, whether by emancipation, fasting, or feeding, each must be before intercourse, because in emancipation and fasting there is explicit text 'before they touch', and as for feeding, it also must be before intercourse because the kaffarah of zihar removes prohibition, so it became necessary that kaffarah precedes intercourse so that intercourse becomes lawful.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage states the sequential kaffarah for zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor persons. It emphasizes that kaffarah must be performed before intercourse, as the Quranic verse indicates 'before they touch'. The author, al-Quduri, outlines this sequence, and the commentator explains that the word 'fa' in the verse indicates order (tartib) not choice (takhyir). The timing before intercourse is established by explicit text for freeing and fasting, and by analogy for feeding, since the purpose is to remove the prohibition.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujūʿ): Returning to the wife after zihar, i.e., resuming marital relations, which is the cause of kaffarah according to the majority.
مسيس (masīs): Sexual intercourse between spouses; kaffarah must be performed before this occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fasting two consecutive months
B) Feeding sixty poor persons
C) Freeing a slave
D) Giving charity

Key Takeaway
The kaffarah of zihar must follow a fixed sequence and be completed before intercourse, as commanded in the Quran.

Freeing a Non-Muslim Slave for Zihar Kaffarah: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Rebuttal
Ruling on which slaves suffice and rebuttal of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which slaves suffice for zihar kaffarah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the absolute nature of the Quranic command.

Core Idea
The Quranic command 'raqabah' is absolute — any slave suffices, regardless of religion.

This passage addresses a critical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a non-Muslim slave be freed for the expiation (kaffarah) of zihar? The Hanafi school, relying on the unqualified term 'raqabah' in the Quran, permits freeing any slave. The Shafi'i school, drawing an analogy to zakat, restricts it to Muslim slaves. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how each school approaches textual interpretation and the role of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the types of slaves acceptable for kaffarah of zihar. Note that it includes non-Muslim, Muslim, male, female, young, and old.
The key term is 'raqabah' without qualification.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i, along with Malik and Ahmad, restricts it to Muslim slaves only.
Their proof is based on qiyas with zakat.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i analogy: kaffarah is a right of Allah, so it cannot be given to an enemy of Allah, just as zakat cannot be given to non-Muslims.
This is a qiyas based on the underlying rationale (sarf ila 'aduww Allah).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: the Quranic text is absolute ('raqabah'), and the intention of freeing a slave is to enable obedience; the slave's own sin does not invalidate the act.
The Hanafis argue that the analogy fails because the text is clear and does not allow restriction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: a Hanafi may free a non-Muslim slave, while a Shafi'i must free a Muslim slave.
This difference affects accessibility and cost of expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کون سے رقبہ کو آزاد کرنا کفایت کرے گا
قال وتجزى فى العتق الرقبة الكافرة والمسلمة والذكر والانثى والصغير والكبير لان اسم الرقبة يطلق على هولاء اذهى عبارة عن الذات المرقوق المملوك من كل وجه والشافعي يخالفنا في الكافرة ويقول الكفارة حق الله تعالى فلايجوز صرفه الى عدو الله كالزكواة و نحن نقول المنصوص عليه اعتاق الرقبة وقد تحقق وقصده من الاعتاق التمكن من الطاعة ثم مقارنة المعصية يحال به الى سوء اختياره
ترجمہ فرمایا: اور آزاد گرنے میں کافی ہے رقبہ کا آزاد کرنا ( خواہ) کا فر ہو یا مسلمان نہ ہو یا مادہ اور ( خواہ) نابالغ ہو یا بالغ ۔ کیونکہ رقبہ کا لفظ ان سب پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ رقبہ نام ہے اس ذات کا جو من کل وجہ مرفوق اور مملوک ہواور امام شافعی رقبہ کافرہ کی صورت میں ہماری مخالفت کرتے ہیں اور کہتے ہیں کہ کفارہ دینا اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے تو اس کو دشمن خدا کی طرف صرف کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ جیسے ( کافرکو ) زکوۃ دینا ( نا جائز ہے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جس چیز پر نص وارد ہے، وہ ایک رقبہ آزاد کرنا ہے اور وہ ( کافر کے آزاد کرنے سے ) متحقق ہو گیا اور کفارہ دینے والے کا قصد آزاد کرنے سے خالق عز و جل کی طاعت پر قدرت دینا ہے پھر معصیت سے ملا رہنا اس رقبہ کافرہ کے بدراہ اختیار کرنے پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح قدروی نے فرمایا کہ کفارہ ظہار میں مطلقا رقبہ کو آزاد کرنا کافی ہے خواہ وہ کا فر ہو یا مسلمان مذکر ہو یا مونث ، نابالغ ہو یا بالغ ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ رقبہ ان سب پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ کسی صفت کے ساتھ مقید نہیں۔ کیونکہ رقبہ کہتے ہیں اس ذات کو جو مملوک ہو اور من کل وجہ مرقوق ہو حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ظہار میں رقبہ کا فرہ کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور یہی قول ہے امام مالک اور امام احمد کا اور دلیل میں فرماتے ہیں کہ کفارہ خدا تعالیٰ کا حق ہے لہذا اس کو خدا کے دشمن کافر کی طرف صرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ جیسے کافرکو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے ہماری دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں مطلقا رقبہ کے آزاد کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور رقبہ کا فرہ کو آزاد کرنے سے مطلقا رقبہ کا آزاد کرنا متحقق ہو گیا ہے اس وجہ سے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کفارہ ظہار میں رقبہ کا فرہ کو آزاد کرنا بھی کافی ہوگا۔
Which slave suffices to free? He said: 'And it suffices in emancipation the non-Muslim and Muslim slave, male and female, young and old, because the name 'raqabah' applies to all of them, for it is an expression for the essence that is owned and possessed from every aspect. Al-Shafi'i opposes us regarding the non-Muslim and says: Kaffarah is a right of Allah, so it is not permissible to give it to an enemy of Allah, like zakat. We say: The text stipulates freeing a slave, and that is realized. And the intention of emancipation is to enable obedience; then association with sin is attributed to his own bad choice.' Translation: He said: It suffices in emancipation to free a slave, whether non-Muslim or Muslim, male or female, young or old, because the word 'raqabah' is applied to all these. Because 'raqabah' is the name for the essence that is possessed from every aspect. Imam Shafi'i opposes us in the case of a non-Muslim slave and says: Giving kaffarah is a right of Allah, so it is not permissible to give it to an enemy of Allah, like giving zakat to a non-Muslim. We say: The thing on which the text came is freeing a slave, and that is realized by freeing a non-Muslim, and the intention of the one giving kaffarah is to enable obedience to the Creator; then remaining with sin is attributed to the non-Muslim slave's own choice. Explanation: Quduri said: In kaffarah of zihar, absolutely freeing a slave suffices, whether non-Muslim or Muslim, male or female, young or old. The proof is that the word 'raqabah' is applied to all these, not restricted to any description. Because 'raqabah' is said for the essence that is owned and possessed from every aspect. Imam Shafi'i says: It is not permissible to free a non-Muslim slave in zihar, and this is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Their proof: Kaffarah is a right of Allah, so it is not permissible to give it to an enemy of Allah, like giving zakat to a non-Muslim. Our proof in summary: The Quran commands freeing a slave absolutely, and by freeing a non-Muslim slave, absolute freeing is realized. Therefore we say: In kaffarah of zihar, freeing a non-Muslim slave also suffices.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage addresses the type of slave that suffices for zihar kaffarah. The Hanafi position, based on the general term 'raqabah' in the Quran, allows freeing any slave—Muslim or non-Muslim, male or female, adult or child. Imam Shafi'i, along with Malik and Ahmad, restricts it to Muslim slaves, analogizing to zakat which cannot be given to non-Muslims. The Hanafi rebuttal argues that the Quranic command is absolute ('raqabah'), and the intention is to enable the slave to perform acts of obedience; any sinfulness on the part of the slave is their own choice, not affecting the validity of the kaffarah.

Key Terms
رقبہ (raqabah): A slave; literally 'neck', used metonymically for a person in bondage. Here it refers to any human being who is legally owned and possessed from every aspect.
عتق (ʿitq): Emancipation or freeing a slave, which is the first option in kaffarah of zihar.
کافرہ (kāfirah): A female slave who is a non-Muslim (unbeliever).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following slaves is acceptable for kaffarah of zihar?
A) Only a male Muslim slave
B) Only a female Muslim slave
C) Any slave, regardless of religion, gender, or age
D) Only a non-Muslim slave

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Quranic command to free a 'raqabah' is absolute, allowing any slave to be freed for zihar kaffarah, even a non-Muslim, unlike the Shafi'i school which restricts it to Muslim slaves.

Timing of Zihar Expiation Must Precede Intercourse
Ruling with proof from Quran and rational extension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive and apply the Hanafi rule that all forms of kaffarah for zihar must be performed before intercourse, using both explicit text and qiyas.

Core Idea
Expiation for zihar must precede intercourse; without it, intercourse remains prohibited.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the timing of kaffarah for zihar. The Quran explicitly commands expiation 'before they touch' (Quran 58:3-4). The commentary extends this ruling to all three forms of expiation, not just freeing and fasting. We will see how the Hanafi school uses both explicit text and logical reasoning to derive a unified rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Zihar creates a prohibition against intercourse; expiation removes it. The passage rules that expiation must occur before intercourse.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 58:3-4, specifically the phrase 'min qabli an yatamassa' (before they touch), provides the primary evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative to perform expiation 'before they touch' indicates that precedence is obligatory.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While explicit for freeing and fasting, feeding is not explicitly mentioned; the Hanafi school extends the rule via qiyas: expiation removes prohibition, so it must precede.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
This is the mufta bihi position; other schools may not require strict precedence, but Hanafi insists based on text and reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وكل ذالك قبل المسيس و هذافي الاعتاق والصوم ظاهر للتنصيص عليه و كذافي الاطعام لان الكفارة فيه منهية للحرمة فلابد من تقديمها على الوطى ليكون الوطى حلالاً
ترجمہ کہا اور ہر ایک امر اس کے وطی کرنے سے پہلے ہے اور وطی سے پہلے ہونا آزاد کرنے اور روزہ رکھنے میں ظاہر ہے کیونکہ اس پر صریح نص ہے اور یہی حکم کھانا دینے میں ہے اس لئے کہ ظہار میں کفارہ دینا حرمت کو ختم کرنے والا ہے تو اس کا ولی سے مقدم کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ ولی حلال واقع ہو۔
تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ ظہار کا کفارہ خواہ بالا عتاق ہو یا بالصیام یا بالا طعام ہر ایک کا وطی سے پہلے ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اعتناق اور صیام میں تو صراحہ نص ( من قبل ان تما سا) موجود ہے اور رہا اطعام تو اس کا بھی قبل الوطی ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ کفارہ ظہار حرمت کو ختم کرنے والا ہے اس لئے ضروری ہوا کہ کفارہ ولی پر مقدم ہوتا کہ ولی حلال واقع ہو۔
He said: And all that is before intercourse. And this (the requirement of being before intercourse) is apparent in freeing and fasting due to explicit textual evidence (from the Quran), and similarly in feeding because the expiation in it is a remover of prohibition, so it must be preceded before intercourse so that intercourse becomes lawful. Urdu translation: He said: Every act of expiation is before intercourse. That it is before intercourse is apparent in freeing and fasting because there is explicit text on it (the Quranic verse 'before they touch each other'), and the same ruling applies to feeding because the expiation for zihar removes prohibition, so it is necessary to precede the expiation before intercourse so that the intercourse becomes lawful. Commentary: It is stated that the expiation for zihar, whether by freeing, fasting, or feeding, each must be before intercourse because in freeing and fasting there is explicit text (the verse 'before they touch'), and as for feeding, it is also necessary before intercourse because the expiation removes prohibition, therefore it is necessary that expiation precede intercourse so that intercourse becomes lawful.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah stating that the expiation for zihar must be performed before the husband has intercourse with his wife. The comment explains that this requirement is clear for the options of freeing a slave and fasting, as the Quran explicitly says 'before they touch each other' (Quran 58:3-4). For the option of feeding, there is no explicit text, but the same rule applies by reasoning: the expiation is what removes the prohibition (hurmah) created by the zihar pronouncement. Therefore, the expiation must precede the intercourse to make it lawful. This is a Hanafi position rooted in the literal and rational interpretation of the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A form of divorce where a husband likens his wife to his mother's back, requiring expiation before intercourse.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for zihar, which consists of freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for requiring feeding (it'am) to precede intercourse?
A) Explicit Quranic text
B) Qiyas on freeing and fasting because the illa (removing prohibition) is the same
C) Consensus of the Sahaba
D) It is not required; only freeing and fasting require precedence

Key Takeaway
All forms of zihar expiation must precede intercourse; the rule is derived from explicit text for freeing/fasting and by qiyas for feeding.

Any Slave Suffices for Zihar Expiation: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the permissibility of freeing a disbelieving slave for zihar expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on freeing a disbelieving slave for zihar expiation and explain the madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response.

Core Idea
For zihar expiation, the Hanafi school holds that any slave suffices; the absolute term 'raqabah' in the Quran is not restricted by faith.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and the Shafi'is (along with Malik and Ahmad) regarding the validity of freeing a disbelieving slave for zihar expiation. The Hanafi position is that the Quranic command to free a 'raqabah' is absolute and applies to any slave, while the opposing school argues that expiation, being a right of Allah, cannot be directed to an enemy of Allah. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafis prioritize literal textual interpretation over analogical reasoning (qiyas) when the text is clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling in the matn
Read the source passage and note that the matn states: 'it suffices to free the disbelieving and believing slave, male and female, young and old.' This is the Hanafi ruling that any slave, regardless of faith, is valid for zihar expiation.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proof
The passage then presents the Shafi'i objection: expiation is a right of Allah, so it is not permitted to be spent on an enemy of Allah. They draw an analogy (qiyas) to zakat, which cannot be given to a disbeliever. Recognize the analogical reasoning here.
This objection is also held by Malik and Ahmad.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The Quranic command 'free a slave' is absolute ('mutlaq') and not restricted by any condition of faith. (2) The intention of freeing a slave is to enable obedience to Allah; if the freed slave remains a disbeliever, that is his own choice, not a defect in the expiation. Distinguish between the text and the analogy.
The Hanafi position relies on the principle that 'al-mutlaq yajri ala itlaqihi' (the absolute remains absolute) unless there is evidence to restrict it.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: Under the Hanafi school, if a man frees a disbelieving slave for zihar, his expiation is valid and he need not repeat it. Under the Shafi'i school, the expiation is invalid and he must free a believing slave or choose another option (fasting or feeding).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح قدروی نے فرمایا کہ کفارہ ظہار میں مطلقا رقبہ کو آزاد کرنا کافی ہے خواہ وہ کا فر ہو یا مسلمان مذکر ہو یا مونث ، نابالغ ہو یا بالغ ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ رقبہ ان سب پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ کسی صفت کے ساتھ مقید نہیں۔ کیونکہ رقبہ کہتے ہیں اس ذات کو جو مملوک ہو اور من کل وجہ مرقوق ہو حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ظہار میں رقبہ کا فرہ کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور یہی قول ہے امام مالک اور امام احمد کا اور دلیل میں فرماتے ہیں کہ کفارہ خدا تعالیٰ کا حق ہے لہذا اس کو خدا کے دشمن کافر کی طرف صرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ جیسے کافرکو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے ہماری دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں مطلقا رقبہ کے آزاد کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور رقبہ کا فرہ کو آزاد کرنے سے مطلقا رقبہ کا آزاد کرنا متحقق ہو گیا ہے اس وجہ سے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کفارہ ظہار میں رقبہ کا فرہ کو آزاد کرنا بھی کافی ہوگا۔
He said: And it suffices in freeing the believing and disbelieving slave, male and female, young and old, because the term 'raqabah' (slave) applies to all these, as it is an expression for the essence that is owned and completely enslaved. Our proof is that the Quran commands absolutely freeing a slave, and freeing a disbelieving slave achieves that absolute freeing, therefore we say that in zihar expiation, freeing a disbelieving slave is sufficient.

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school (along with Malik and Ahmad) regarding the validity of freeing a disbelieving slave for zihar expiation. The matn states that any slave (disbeliever, Muslim, male, female, young, old) suffices, citing the absolute term 'raqabah' used in the Quran. The Shafi'i objection analogizes to zakat, which cannot be given to a disbeliever. The Hanafi response argues that the Quranic command is unconditional; the intention is to free a human being to enable obedience to Allah. If the freed slave remains a disbeliever, that is his own bad choice, not the fault of the one performing expiation. The commentary by Qadrawi further explains and reinforces this Hanafi position.

Key Terms
رقبہ (raqabah): A slave, male or female, who is completely owned and enslaved.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for zihar, which is a right of Allah requiring freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding.

Ruling on Defective Slaves for Zihar Expiation
Ruling on defective slaves for zihar expiation with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of 'jins al-manfa'ah' to determine whether a slave with a physical defect is valid for zihar expiation.

Core Idea
Only complete loss of an entire category of benefit makes a slave invalid; partial impairment is acceptable.

Zihar expiation requires freeing a slave, but not every slave qualifies. The Hanafi school draws a precise line using the concept of 'jins al-manfa'ah' (category of benefit). If the slave has lost an entire genus of benefit—sight, grip, or walking—the expiation is invalid. A mere reduction, like being one-eyed or missing one limb, is acceptable. The case of a deaf slave is especially instructive: it shows how istihsan can override strict qiyas to preserve the purpose of expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative principle
Recognize that the key concept is 'jins al-manfa'ah' (category of benefit). Validity depends on whether the slave retains the full category or has it completely lost, not merely impaired.
The text explicitly mentions sight, grip, and walking as the essential categories.
2
Apply to obvious cases: complete loss
Blindness (loss of sight), missing both hands (loss of grip), or missing both feet (loss of walking) result in total loss of a category, making the slave invalid.
These are straightforward applications of the principle.
3
Apply to borderline cases: partial loss
One-eyed (partial sight), missing one hand and one foot from opposite sides (partial grip and walking) are mere impairments—the category is not entirely lost, so valid. However, missing one hand and one foot from the same side invalidates because walking becomes impossible, losing that category.
The distinction between 'opposite sides' and 'same side' hinges on whether walking is still possible.
4
Handle the exceptional case: deaf slave
By strict qiyas, deafness (loss of hearing) would invalidate, as per a nawadir narration. But the Hanafi school adopts istihsan: since the slave can hear when called loudly, the original benefit remains, so the slave is valid.
This shows that istihsan can override qiyas when the underlying rationale (remaining benefit) differs.
5
Summarize the rule
A slave is valid for expiation if at least some of each essential benefit category remains. Complete loss of any one category (sight, grip, walking, or hearing in extreme cases) invalidates. The principle applies to all physical defects.
The author of al-Inayah adds that the slave must be fully owned, the freeing must be connected to expiation intention, and the freeing must be without compensation (like a mudabbar is invalid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تجزى العمياء ولا المقطوعة اليدين او الرجلين لان الفائت جنس المنفعة وهي البصر او البطش يجوز العوراء ومقطوعة احدى اليدين واحدى او المشى وهو المانع اما اذا اختلت المنفعة فهو غیر مانع قلت بخلاف ما اذا كانتا مقطوعتين من - الرجلين من خلاف لانه مافات جنس المنفعة بل ال واحد حيث لايجوز لفوات جنس منفعة المشى اذهو عليه متعذر ويجوز الاصم والقياس ان لايجوز وهو روايت النوادر لان الفائت جنس المنفعة الا انا استحسنا الجوازلان اصل المنفعة باق فانه اذاصيح عليه ليسمع حتى لو كان بحال لايسمع اصلا بان ولداصم وهو الاخرس لايجزيه
ترجمہ اور ایسا رقبہ آزاد کرنا کافی نہیں ہے جو اندھا ہو، یا جس کے دونوں ہاتھ دونوں پاؤں کئے ہوں ۔ کیونکہ (اس رقبہ میں ) منفعت کی جنس فوت ہے اور وہ بینائی یا گرفت یا چالی ہے اور یہی (ادائے کفارہ سے ) مانع ہے اور اگر اس کی منفعت میں خلل ہو تو مانع نہیں ہے حتی کہ کانا، یا جس کا ایک ہاتھ اور دوسری طرف کا ایک پاؤں کٹا ہو تو جائز ہے کیونکہ جنس منفعت زائل نہیں ہوئی بلکہ مختل ہوگئی ہے بر خلاف اس کے کہ جب ایک ہاتھ اور ایک پاؤں دونوں ایک طرف سے کئے ہوئے تو ( یہ ) جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ چلنے کی جنس منفعت فوت ہو گئی اس لئے کہ اس پر چلنا ستعد رہے اور بہرہ غلام آزاد کرنا جائز ہے اور قیاس یہ تھا کہ جائز نہ ہو اور یہی نوادر کی روایت ہے کیوں کہ جنس منفعت فوت ہو گئی مگر ہم نے استحسانا جائز قرار دیا۔ کیوں کہ اصل منفعت باقی ہے۔ چنانچہ جب چلا کر بات کی جائے تو سن لیتا ہے۔ حتی اکہ اگر اس کی حالت ایسی ہو کہ بالکل نہیں سنتا بایں طور کو مادر زاد بہرہ ہے اور وہی گونگا ہے تو اس کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ کفارہ ظہار میں نا بینا غلام یا باندی کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ اس کا آزاد کرنا درست ہے ۔ جس کے دونوں ہاتھ گئے ہوں یا دونوں پاؤں کئے ہوں صاحب عنایہ نے ایک ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے ایسا رقبہ آزاد کیا جو کامل الرق ہے اور آزاد کرنے والے کی ملک میں ہے اور یہ آزاد کرنا کفارہ کی نیت کے ساتھ متصل ہے اور اس کی جنس منفعت جس پر وہ قائم ہے باقی ہے اور یہ آزاد کرنا بلا بدل ہے تو یہ آزاد کرنا جائز ہوگا اور اگر ایسا نہیں ہے تو نا جائز ہے چنانچہ مدبر کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہ
And a blind slave does not suffice, nor one with both hands or both feet cut off, because the entire category of benefit is lost - that benefit being sight, grip, or walking - which is the preventative. But if there is only impairment of benefit, it is not preventative. So a one-eyed slave, or one with one hand and the opposite foot cut off, is permissible, because the category of benefit is not lost, only impaired. In contrast, if one hand and one foot are cut off from the same side, it is not permissible because the category of walking is lost as walking becomes impossible. A deaf slave is permissible, and by qiyas it would not be permissible, and this is the narration of al-Nawadir, because the category of benefit is lost, but we have permitted it by istihsan, because the original benefit remains; when called out to, he hears. Until if he is in a condition of not hearing at all, like one born deaf and also mute, then freeing him does not suffice. Urdu translation: And such a slave does not suffice who is blind, or whose both hands or both feet are cut off, because the category of benefit is lost - that benefit being sight, grip, or walking - and this prevents validity. If there is only impairment of benefit, it is not preventative. So a one-eyed slave, or one with one hand and one foot from opposite sides cut off, is permissible because the category of benefit is not lost but only impaired. Unlike if one hand and one foot are cut off from the same side, which is not permissible because the category of walking is lost, as walking becomes impossible. A deaf slave is permissible, and by qiyas it would not be permissible, and this is the narration of al-Nawadir, because the category of benefit is lost, but we have permitted it by istihsan because the original benefit remains. So if he is called out to, he hears. However, if he is in a state of not hearing at all, such as one born deaf and also mute, then freeing him does not suffice. Commentary: The ruling is that in zihar expiation, freeing a blind slave or a slave with both hands or both feet cut off is not permissible. The author of al-Inayah has stated a principle: if a person frees a slave who is perfect in slavery, owned by him, and the freeing is connected to the intention of expiation, and the category of benefit upon which the slave depends remains, and the freeing is without compensation, then it is valid. If not, then it is invalid. Thus, freeing a mudabbar is not valid.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on which physical defects disqualify a slave for zihar expiation and which are acceptable. The key principle is that the loss of an entire genus (jins) of benefit (sight, grip, or walking) renders the slave invalid. Mere impairment (ikhtilal) does not. For example, a one-eyed slave is valid because the genus of sight is still present, just reduced. Similarly, a slave with one hand and one foot from opposite sides is valid because both the functions of grip and walking are partially retained. However, if one hand and one foot are from the same side, walking becomes impossible, so the genus of walking is lost, making the slave invalid. A deaf slave is considered valid by istihsan, even though qiyas would suggest invalidity (as in a narration from al-Nawadir), because the original benefit of hearing remains when called loudly. However, if the slave is born deaf and mute, he is invalid. The commentator then quotes a principle from al-Inayah summarizing the conditions for a valid expiatory freeing: the slave must be fully owned, the freeing must be connected to the expiation intention, the genus of benefit must remain, and the freeing must be without compensation (not like freeing a mudabbar).

Key Terms
جنس منفعت (jins al-manfa'ah): The category of benefit (e.g., sight, grip, walking) that is essential for the slave's functionality.
استحسان (istihsan): Legal preference over qiyas based on broader principles of benefit and ease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following slaves is valid for zihar expiation according to the text?
A) A blind slave.
B) A slave with both hands cut off.
C) A one-eyed slave.
D) A slave with one hand and one foot from the same side cut off.

Key Takeaway
A slave is invalid for expiation only if an entire category of benefit (sight, grip, walking, hearing in extremes) is completely lost; mere impairment is acceptable.

Conditions for a Valid Slave in Zihar Kafarah: The Principle of Jins al-Manfa'ah
Explains which defective slaves are valid or invalid for zihar expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between complete loss (fawt) and impairment (ikhtilal) of benefit in a slave, and apply this to determine the validity of freeing a slave for zihar kafarah.

Core Idea
Complete loss of benefit type invalidates; mere impairment does not.

In the expiation for zihar, freeing a slave is one option. But not every slave qualifies. The Hanafi school sets a precise condition: the slave must be complete in slavery and retain the full type of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah). This lesson unpacks that condition using examples like one-eyed, thumbless, and insane slaves, and contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam Shafi'i. You will learn to identify which defects are fatal and which are not, based on the underlying legal rationale (ta'lil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is freeing a slave as kafarah for zihar. The overall hukm: it is valid only if the slave is 'kamil al-raq' (complete in slavery) and retains the full type of benefit. Otherwise, the kafarah is not discharged.
2
Classify slave defects into fawt or ikhtilal
Read the text and list the defects given. For each, determine whether the text says the jins al-manfa'ah is completely lost (fawt) or merely impaired (ikhtilal). Fawt examples: both hands gone, both feet cut, blindness, both thumbs cut, permanent insanity. Ikhtilal examples: one-eyed, one hand and one foot on opposite sides, intermittent insanity, deafness (by istihsan).
Remember: fawt = type of benefit is gone; ikhtilal = benefit is present but imperfect.
3
Apply the classification to derive the ruling
If fawt → invalid. If ikhtilal → valid. Note the exception of the mudabbar and umm walad: even if physically complete, they are not valid because their slavery is incomplete (they have a right to future freedom).
The rationale for fawt: the slave becomes like a dead person in terms of benefit.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position on the one-eyed slave
Imam Shafi'i holds that any permanent defect (like one-eyed) invalidates, based on the principle 'ayb fahish. The Hanafi response distinguishes between loss and impairment. Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Note the istihsan exception for the deaf slave
By qiyas, a deaf slave would be invalid because hearing is a type of benefit lost. But by istihsan, it is valid if the slave can hear when spoken loudly. If the slave is born deaf and mute, then the benefit is completely lost and freeing is invalid.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here because the original benefit of hearing remains to some degree.

Chapter of Zihar. Commentary of Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh Hidayah Volume Five. Because he is not complete in slavery. If he freed without intention of expiation or intended expiation after freeing, it is still not valid. If he freed a slave whose type of benefit is lost, e.g., both hands are gone, both feet cut, or blind, then freeing such a slave is not valid. However, if the type of benefit is not lost but impaired, then freeing that slave does not prevent expiation. For example, if a one-eyed slave is freed, or one hand on one side and one foot on the other side, then freeing him for zihar expiation is valid because his type of benefit is not lost but impaired. If one hand and one foot are both on the same side, then freeing him is not valid because the type of benefit of walking is lost due to impossibility of walking. Regarding the one-eyed, Imam Shafi'i's madhhab is that freeing a one-eyed slave for zihar expiation is not valid. His proof: this slave is so defective that the defect is not expected to disappear, so it resembles the blind. According to Imam Shafi'i, the principle is: any defect that is not expected to disappear prevents the validity of expiation, called 'ayb fahish; if the defect is expected to disappear, it does not prevent, called 'ayb yasir, like fever or wound. The rule mentioned by Sahib al-Inayah had an additional condition: the freeing must be without substitute. So if someone freed his slave with a substitute, expiation is not paid. Regarding a deaf slave, Sahib al-Hidayah says: by qiyas, freeing him is not valid, and this is the narration in Nawadir, because the type of benefit is lost with deafness, but by istihsan it is declared valid because the original benefit remains, because if addressed loudly he hears. If he cannot hear at all because he is born deaf and mute, then freeing such a slave is insufficient. As for why freeing a slave whose type of benefit is lost prevents expiation, the proof is that by losing the type of benefit, this person becomes like a dead person, since a person's existence is connected to his benefits. The one with both thumbs cut is not sufficient. And it is not permissible to free one whose both thumbs are cut, because the power of grip is with them; with their loss, the type of benefit is lost. And it is not permissible to free an insane person who does not possess reason, because benefit from limbs is only possible with reason, so he is one who has lost benefits. One who becomes insane intermittently and recovers, his freeing is valid because impairment is not a preventive. And the freeing of a mudabbar and umm walad is not sufficient because they have become deserving of freedom from one aspect, so slavery in them is incomplete. Explanation: If a slave or slave-girl has both thumbs cut, then freeing him for zihar expiation is not valid. Proof: due to the loss of both thumbs, the power of grip is lost; thus the type of benefit is lost, and it is established that loss of type of benefit prevents expiation. An insane slave or slave-girl who lacks reason, freeing him is also not valid. Proof: benefit from limbs is not possible without reason, so he too is one who has lost benefits. A slave who becomes insane intermittently and sometimes recovers, if freed during a lucid interval, expiation is paid because the impairment is not preventive. Freeing a mudabbar and umm walad is not sufficient for expiation. Proof: In the Qur'an, 'tahrir raqabah' (freeing a neck) is mentioned, and 'raqabah' is absolute, and when an absolute term is used, it refers to a perfect individual. Mudabbar and umm walad are not perfect slaves because a mudabbar deserves freedom due to tadbir, and umm walad deserves freedom due to istilad, so the meaning of slavery is incomplete in both.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof segment from the commentary on Bab al-Zihar in Ashraf al-Hidayah. It explains the conditions for a slave being valid for expiation (kafarah) in zihar. The key ruling: the slave must be 'kamil al-raq' (complete in slavery) and must have the full type of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah). If the slave's primary benefit is completely lost (like both hands, both feet, blindness, both thumbs cut, permanent insanity), then freeing him is invalid. If the benefit is merely impaired (like one-eyed, one hand and one foot on opposite sides, intermittent insanity, deafness when not completely deaf-mute), then freeing is valid. The passage also discusses mudabbar and umm walad: they are not valid because their slavery is incomplete—they have a right to freedom. The basis for the ruling is rational: a person's existence is tied to his benefits; loss of benefit makes him like a dead person. The text includes an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i regarding the one-eyed slave: Shafi'i considers any permanent defect as preventive, while the Hanafi position distinguishes between loss (fawt) and impairment (ikhtilal) of benefit. The Hanafi school uses istihsan for the case of deafness, contravening qiyas. The passage also notes that freeing with a substitute (badal) invalidates expiation, and that a slave who is both deaf and mute from birth is invalid.

Key Terms
جنس منفعت (jins al-manfa'ah): The type or category of benefit that a slave provides, such as the ability to grip, walk, see, hear. If this is completely lost, the slave is considered 'fā'it al-manāfi'.
مقطوع ابهامى اليدين (maqtū' ibhāmay al-yadayn): A slave whose both thumbs are cut off, causing loss of gripping power.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death (tadbir).
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master.
فوت المنفعة (fawt al-manfa'ah): Complete loss of the type of benefit, rendering the slave invalid for kafarah.
اختلال المنفعة (ikhtilal al-manfa'ah): Impairment of the benefit but not complete loss; does not prevent validity in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is freeing a one-eyed slave valid for zihar kafarah?
A) Yes, because the benefit of sight is impaired but not lost
B) No, because he is defective like a blind person
C) Yes, but only if the other eye is healthy
D) No, because any permanent defect invalidates

Key Takeaway
For zihar kafarah, a slave is valid only if he is kamil al-raq and retains the full type of benefit; complete loss invalidates, but mere impairment does not.

Ruling on Freeing a Mukatab Slave for Zihar Kafarah
Discusses validity of freeing a mukatab for zihar expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on freeing a mukatab for zihar kafarah and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding its validity.

Core Idea
Freeing a mukatab for kafarah is invalid in Zāhir al-Riwāyah because the substitute (badal) negates devotion.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a mukatab (a slave with a kitabah contract) who has paid part of his purchase price be freed to fulfill the expiation for zihar? The relied-upon position holds it invalid due to the transactional element, while a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa considers it valid based on the hadith 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham'. Understanding this dispute requires grasping how the presence of 'badal' affects acts of devotion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The issue is whether freeing a mukatab who has paid some kitabah is valid for zihar kafarah. The Zahir al-Riwayah position (relied upon) says no; a narration from Abu Hanifa says yes.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, not inter-madhhab.
2
Analyze the proof for Zahir al-Riwayah
The basis is logical: freeing such a mukatab involves a substitute (badal) because of the kitabah contract, contradicting the pure devotion (qurbah) required for kafarah. This view is also supported by Imam Zufar, Shafi‘i, Malik, and Ahmad.
No direct textual proof is cited; it's primarily a conceptual argument.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham' (the mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains) and argues that since the mukatab is a full slave from every aspect, his freeing is akin to freeing any other slave.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and others.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The response to Abu Hanifa is that while the hadith indicates general slavery, for kafarah the specific element of badal overrides general status. The presence of payment removes the act from pure devotion.
This is a case of takhsīs (specification) of a general text by qiyas.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah position: freeing such a mukatab is invalid. In practice, one must free a fully owned slave with no kitabah to fulfill zihar expiation.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: validity vs invalidity.

Source Text

وكذا المكاتب الذي أدى بعض المال لأن اعتاقه يكون ببدل وعن ابي حنيفة يجزيه لقيام الرق من كل وجه
ولهذا تقبل الكتابة الانفساخ بخلاف امومية
الولد والتدبير لانها لا يحتملان الانفساخ
ترجمہ اور یہی حکم ہے اس مکاتب کا جس نے کچھ مال ادا کیا کیونکہ اس کا آزاد کرنا بدل کے ساتھ ہو جائے گا اور ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ ایسے مکاتب کو آزاد کرنا کافی ہے اس لئے کہ رقیت من کل وجہ موجود ہے اور اسی وجہ سے کتابت مسخ ہونے کو قبول کر لیتی ہے برخلاف ام ولد اور مد بر ہونے کے کیونکہ یہ دونوں فسخ کا احتمال نہیں رکھتے ۔
تشریح مصنف نے فرمایا کہ وہ مکاتب جس نے کچھ بدل کتابت ادا کر دیا ہے کفارہ ظہار میں اس کا آزاد کرنا بھی کافی نہیں ہو گا دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کا آزاد کرنا بالعوض ہوگا اور عوض قربت اور عبادت کے معنی کو باطل کر دیتا ہے یہی حکم ظاہر الروایتہ میں ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام زفر، امام شافعی اور امام مالک اور ایک روایت میں امام احمد ہیں ۔
اور حسن نے امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ کی ہے کہ ایسے مکاتب کا آزاد کرنا بھی کافی ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتب جب تک پورا بدل کتابت ادا نہ کرے اس وقت تک وہ من کل وجہ رفیق اور غلام رہتا ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے المكاتب عبد مابقی علیه در هم یعنی مکاتب غلام ہی رہتا ہے جب تک اس پر ایک درہم بھی باقی ہے اور چونکہ مکاتب من کل وجہ رقیق ہے اسی وجہ سے کتابت فسخ ہونے کو قبول کر لیتی ہے۔ خواہ یہ نسخ کرنا کچھ بدل کتابت وصول کرنے سے پہلے ہو یا بعد میں ۔ اس کے برخلاف ام ولد ہونا
Freeing a mukatab for zihar kafarah is not sufficient. And likewise the mukatab who has paid some of the money, because his freeing is with a substitute. And from Abu Hanifa: it suffices because the slavery exists from every aspect. For this reason, kitabah accepts annulment, unlike umm walad and tadbir, because they do not admit annulment. Translation: The same ruling applies to a mukatab who has paid some money, because his freeing is with a substitute. And from Abu Hanifa: freeing such a mukatab is sufficient because slavery exists from every aspect. For this reason, kitabah accepts annulment, unlike umm walad and tadbir, because they do not admit annulment. Explanation: The author said that the mukatab who has paid some of the kitabah money, freeing him is not sufficient for zihar kafarah. Proof: his freeing is with a substitute, and a substitute invalidates the meaning of devotion and worship. This is the ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is the view of Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and in one narration Imam Ahmad. And Hasan narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that freeing such a mukatab is sufficient. Proof: the mukatab remains a full slave until he pays the entire kitabah money, because the Prophet (SAW) said: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And since the mukatab is a slave from every aspect, kitabah accepts annulment, whether this dissolution occurs before receiving some of the kitabah money or after. Unlike umm walad...
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of freeing a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to buy his freedom) for zihar kafarah. The mukatab has paid some of the kitabah price. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that his freeing is not valid because it is with a substitute (badal), which negates the devotional aspect. This view is shared by Imam Zufar, Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad. However, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad records Abu Hanifa's view that it is valid, because the mukatab remains a full slave until the entire price is paid, as per the hadith 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham'. Abu Hanifa argues that since the mukatab is a slave from every aspect, the kitabah can be annulled, unlike umm walad or mudabbar, whose status is irreversible. The practical consequence: in fatwa, the Zahir al-Riwayah position is followed (not valid), but Abu Hanifa's view is recorded as a weaker opinion.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
بدل (badal): Substitute, here referring to the money paid by the mukatab for his freedom.
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books, considered the primary authoritative source in the Hanafi school.

A) It is valid because he is still a slave.
B) It is not valid because his freeing involves a substitute.
C) It is valid only if he has paid more than half.
D) It is not valid because he is already free.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi is that freeing a mukatab who has paid any part of his kitabah is invalid for zihar kafarah due to the presence of a substitute (badal).

Freeing a Mukatab in Zihar Kaffarah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute over validity of freeing a mukatab with no payment in zihar kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on freeing a mukatab with no payment for zihar kaffarah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith and the concept of kitabah.

Core Idea
A mukatab is a full slave until the last dirham is paid, making his freeing valid for kaffarah.

The Hanafi school permits freeing a mukatab who has not yet paid any portion of his kitabah as expiation for zihar. The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that the mukatab's right to freedom resembles that of a mudabbar. This lesson dissects the proofs and responses of both schools, highlighting the Hanafi reliance on a prophetic hadith and the nature of the kitabah contract.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to the Hanafi school: freeing a mukatab with no payment is valid for zihar kaffarah.
This is the mufta bihi position, supported by Abu Hanifa and one narration of Imam Muhammad.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
The Shafi'i school (and Zufar, Malik, one narration of Ahmad) holds it invalid. Their proof: the mukatab has become deserving of freedom through the kitabah, resembling a mudabbar (which Hanafis reject for kaffarah).
The analogy with mudabbar is central to their argument.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi dalil is the hadith: 'المكاتب عبد ما بقى عليه درهم' (The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him). This establishes full slave status until full payment.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but its meaning is clear.
4
Address the Hanafi rebuttals
The Hanafis respond that kitabah is merely a removal of restrictions (like permission to trade), not a removal of slavery. The analogy with mudabbar fails because mudabbar's freedom is contingent on death, while mukatab's is conditional on payment.
Also, if kitabah were a preventer, the act of freeing would annul it first, making the slave a non-mukatab.
5
Determine the practical difference
Thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis allow the mukatab for kaffarah; Shafi'is require a slave with no claim to freedom.
The Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa.
