دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں کتابت کا فسخ ہونا صحت اعتاق کی وجہ سے ضرورۃ ثابت ہے اور جو چیز ضرورۃ ثابت ہو وہ بند ر ضرورت ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا کفارہ میں آزادی کے جائز ہونے کے حق میں کتابت کا فسخ ہونا ظاہر ہوگا اس کی اولاد اور کمائی کے سامان کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں ہوگا پس جب مکاتب کی اولاد اور اس کی کمائی کے سامان کے حق میں کتابت فسخ نہیں ہوئی تو اس کی اولاد اور کمائی اسی کے لئے ہوگی نہ کہ مولی کے لئے ۔
Chapter of Zihar. If he frees a mukatab who has not paid anything, it is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His proof: he has become deserving of freedom by virtue of the kitabah, so he resembles a mudabbar. Our proof: slavery remains fully as we have explained, and by his statement (peace be upon him): 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And kitabah does not contradict it, because it is the removal of a restriction, like permission to trade, except that it is for a consideration, so it becomes binding on his part. And if it were a preventer, it would be annulled by virtue of the freeing, because it can bear annulment, except that his earnings and children are surrendered to him, because the freeing in this case is by virtue of kitabah, or because the annulment is necessary and does not appear in the case of the child and earnings. (The Urdu commentary explains the dispute: Hanafis hold it valid; Shafi'i, Zufar, Malik, and a narration of Ahmad hold it invalid. The Hanafi proof is the hadith and that slavery remains fully. Kitabah is like permission to trade, not a removal of slavery. The objection about the master's inability to annul kitabah alone is answered by noting kitabah is for consideration, thus binding. Another answer: if kitabah were a hindrance, freeing would annul it first, making it a free person, not a mukatab. The question about earnings and children going to the master is answered: freedom is due to kitabah, so they remain with the mukatab; or the annulment is necessary only for the validity of freeing, not for other rights.)
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of freeing a mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) who has not yet paid any portion of the kitabah (the agreed price) as expiation (kaffarah) for zihar. The Hanafi position, based on the matn of al-Hidayah, states that it is valid. The text presents the Shafi'i objection: since the mukatab has earned the right to freedom through the contract, he is like a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death), which the Hanafis themselves do not accept for zihar kaffarah. The Hanafi response rests on two main arguments: first, the hadith 'المكاتب عبد ما بقى عليه درهم' (the mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him) proves that slavery is fully intact until full payment; second, the contract of kitabah is merely a removal of restriction (fakk al-hajr) similar to permission to trade (idhn fi al-tijarah) and does not negate the underlying slavery. The text then addresses two potential objections: (1) why can't the master annul the kitabah unilaterally if it's like permission to trade? The answer: kitabah is for consideration (bi 'iwad), so it becomes binding on the master, unlike permission to trade. (2) If the freeing annuls the kitabah, why don't the mukatab's earnings and children go to the master? The answer: either because the freeing is by virtue of kitabah (so the rights remain with the mukatab) or because the annulment is necessary (daruri) only to validate the freeing, not to affect property rights. The text also clarifies that if the mukatab has paid any portion, freeing him is not valid because the kaffarah becomes mixed with trade. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position, though Imam Zufar and others disagree.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum.
ظهار (ẓihār): A form of divorce where a husband compares his wife to his mother or another mahram, making her prohibited until expiation is performed.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death, effective after the master's demise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is freeing a mukatab with no payment valid for zihar kaffarah?
A) Because the mukatab has earned the right to freedom through kitabah.
B) Because the master can annul the kitabah at any time.
C) Because the hadith states the mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.
D) Because the mukatab is considered a mudabbar.

Key Takeaway
Freeing a mukatab with no payment is valid for zihar kaffarah in the Hanafi school because the hadith and legal reasoning affirm his full slave status until the debt is cleared.

Freeing a Shared Slave as Kaffarah for Zihar: Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn
Explains ruling on freeing half a jointly-owned slave as kaffarah for zihar and internal Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on freeing half a jointly-owned slave as kaffarah for zihar and explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Freeing half then the other half of a jointly-owned slave is valid for kaffarah, but the reasoning differs: istihsan for Abu Hanifa, indivisibility for the Sahibayn.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of freeing a half-owned slave as expiation (kaffarah) for zihar. While the ruling is ultimately valid, the legal reasoning differs between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). Understanding this dispute illuminates key Hanafi principles on the divisibility of emancipation and the role of istihsan.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the overall ruling: freeing half a jointly-owned slave and then later freeing the other half is valid (jā'iz) for kaffarah according to the relied-upon view.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the internal dispute
Clarify that both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree on the validity but differ in their legal reasoning. The dispute centers on whether emancipation can be partial (tajazzu').
Abu Hanifa allows partial emancipation; the Sahibayn hold that it is indivisible.
3
Follow each imam's proof
Analyze the dalil for each view: Abu Hanifa uses istihsan analogizing to a sacrificial sheep; the Sahibayn argue that freeing half frees the whole because 'itq does not divide.
Istihsan overrides qiyas for Abu Hanifa in this case.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in this specific scenario, both views lead to the same outcome (valid kaffarah). However, in other scenarios (e.g., freeing half then intercourse before freeing the other half), the difference may lead to different rulings.
The key distinction is whether the deficiency occurs in one's own ownership or the partner's.
5
Note the mufta bihi
Confirm that the valid ruling (jā'iz) is the operative one for fatwa, as presented in the matn and supported by istihsan.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah endorses this view.

اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتناق متجری ( ٹکڑے ٹکڑے) ہوتاہے ہیں جس پر کفارہ واجب تھا جب اس نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کیا تو اس سے کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوا۔ کیونکہ نصف رقبہ رقبہ نہیں ہوتا اور ر ہا نصف آخر تو اس میں نقصان واقع ہو گیا ہے اس وجہ سے کہ اس میں رقیت کا باقی رکھنا محال ہے اور یہ نقصان اس کے شریک کی ملک میں واقع ہوا ہے پس جب آزاد کرنے والا ضمان دے کر اس نصف آخر کا مالک ہوا تو وہ اس ناقص کا مالک ہوا۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا اس نے کچھ کم پورا غلام آزاد کیا ہے اور ایسے غلام کا آزاد کرنا ادائے کفارہ کے لئے مانع ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کفارہ ادا نہیں ہو گا۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنا نصف غلام اپنے کفارہ میں آزاد کیا پھر باقی غلام کو بھی آزاد کر دیا تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی کفار واوا ہو جائے گا۔ یہ جواز استحسانا ہے ورنہ قیاس کے مطابق امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ عبد مشترک میں عدم جواز کا حکم ہے اس لئے کہ نصف آخر میں نقصان پایا گیا ہے اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے دو دفعہ کلام کر کے غلام آزاد کیا ہے اور جو نقصان نصف آخر میں واقع ہوا ہے وہ اس ملک میں رہتے ہوئے کفارہ میں آزاد کرنے کی وجہ سے پیدا ہوا ہے اور اس قسم کا نقصان ادائے کفارہ کیلئے مانع نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسے ایک شخص نے قربانی کیلئے بکری زمین پر گرائی پس بکری کی آنکھ میں چھری لگ گئی تو یہ نقصان قربانی سے مانع نہیں ہے۔
اس کے برخلاف وہ مسئلہ جو پہلے گزر چکا کیونکہ وہ نقصان تو شریک کی ملک میں پیدا ہوا ہے، لہذا اس نقصان کو جو نصف آخر میں پیدا ہوا ہے ، کفارہ کی طرف پھیر ناممکن نہیں ۔ اس لئے کہ یہ شخص آزاد کرتے وقت اس نقصان کا مالک نہیں تھا۔ یہ تقریر حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے اصول پر تھی ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ آزاد کرنا منتجومی (ٹکڑے) نہیں ہوتا ، اس لئے جب آدھا غلام آزاد کیا تو اسی وقت پورا غلام آزاد ہو گیا ۔ لہذا صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ آزاد کرنا دو دفعہ کلام کر کے آزاد کرنا نہیں ہو گا۔ بلکہ ایک ہی کلام کے ساتھ پورا کر غلام آزاد ہو گیا۔
A person must first know that according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), emancipation cannot be partial, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it can be partial. So if a slave is freed little by little, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, only the part freed becomes free; but according to the Sahibayn, if half or more is freed, the entire slave becomes free. Then the proof of the Sahibayn is that the person who frees half gives compensation to the partner for the other half and becomes owner of it, thus he frees the whole slave which is in his ownership, so kaffarah is fulfilled. But if the person freeing is insolvent, the kaffarah is not fulfilled by consensus because the slave must work to pay the partner's share, so the freeing is for compensation, which is not valid for kaffarah. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that emancipation can be partial; the person had an obligation to free a slave, but freeing half does not count because half of a person is not a complete person. When he later acquires the other half, a deficiency occurs in the partner's ownership, so he becomes owner of a defective slave. This is like freeing a defective slave, which prevents kaffarah. Then the matn says: If he frees half his slave as kaffarah, then frees the remaining half, it is valid because he freed it with two utterances, and the deficiency occurred in his own ownership, which is not a barrier, like a sheep for sacrifice that gets its eye cut. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa's principle. According to the Sahibayn, since emancipation is not partial, freeing half is freeing the whole, so it is not with two utterances. Then the commentary explains that this validity is by istihsan; by qiyas it would be invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, like the case of a jointly-owned slave. The reason for istihsan is that the deficiency occurred in his own ownership due to the act of freeing, and such deficiency is not a barrier. The case is different from the earlier one where the deficiency occurred in the partner's ownership. According to the Sahibayn, since emancipation does not divide, freeing half frees the whole immediately, so it is not considered freeing with two utterances.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of freeing a jointly-owned slave as expiation (kaffarah) for zihar. The text first clarifies the fundamental dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether emancipation can be partial (tajazzu'). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it can be partial, meaning only the portion freed becomes free. The Sahibayn hold that emancipation is indivisible: if any part is freed, the entire slave becomes free. Based on this, the passage then discusses two scenarios. The first scenario is where a person owns half a slave (the other half is owned by a partner). He frees his half as kaffarah and later acquires the other half and frees it as well. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, is this valid? The matn states that it is valid (jā'iz). The reasoning is that the slave was freed with two utterances, and the deficiency that occurred in the second half (due to the obligation to work or compensation) is within the person's own ownership, and such deficiency does not prevent the kaffarah. He gives an analogy: if a person lays down a sheep for sacrifice and accidentally cuts its eye, the sacrifice is still valid. Similarly, here the deficiency is not a barrier. However, according to the Sahibayn, since emancipation is indivisible, freeing the first half already freed the entire slave, so the second freeing is not needed; thus it is not considered 'freeing with two utterances.' But the result is the same: the kaffarah is valid. The commentary then explains that this validity is by istihsan (juristic preference). By qiyas (analogy), it would be invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, like the case of a jointly-owned slave where the deficiency occurs in the partner's ownership. The key distinction is whether the deficiency occurs in one's own ownership or in another's. If in one's own, it is not a barrier; if in another's, it is. This is the foundation of Imam Abu Hanifa's approach. The Sahibayn's approach is based on the indivisibility of emancipation, so the issue of deficiency does not arise because the whole slave is considered freed from the start.

Key Terms
اعتاق (ʻitāq): Emancipation of a slave; the act of freeing.
تجزي (tajazzu'): Partiality; the quality of being divisible into parts.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is freeing half a slave and then later freeing the other half valid as kaffarah for zihar?
A) Because the slave is wholly owned at the time of the second freeing.
B) Because the deficiency occurred in the person's own ownership, which does not prevent kaffarah.
C) Because the person freed the entire slave with one utterance.
D) Because the partner's consent is obtained.

Key Takeaway
Freeing half a jointly-owned slave and later the other half is valid for kaffarah by istihsan when the deficiency arises in one's own ownership.

Freeing Half a Slave in Zihar Kaffarah: The Tajazzu' Dispute
Ruling on kaffarah with half-freed before intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of kaffarah when freeing half a slave before intercourse and the other half after, and identify the underlying usul principle that drives the difference.

Core Idea
Whether freeing half frees the whole determines if the Quranic condition is met.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in zihar kaffarah: a person frees half his slave, then has intercourse with his wife, then frees the other half. Does this fulfill the Quranic requirement? The Hanafi school splits on the answer based on whether emancipation can be partial (tajazzu') or is indivisible. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in applying textual conditions and recognizing the role of usul principles in generating rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the issue
Clearly describe what the person did: freed half the slave, then had intercourse, then freed the other half. The issue: does this satisfy the Quranic condition that the freeing be before intercourse?
The Quranic text (58:3-4) says 'min qabli an yatamāssā' – before they touch.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his premise
Abu Hanifa rules that the kaffarah is invalid. His premise: emancipation can be partial (tajazzu'), so freeing half is not freeing the whole. Thus only half was freed before intercourse; the other half was after.
This is because 'al-i'tāq yatajazzā'' according to him.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their premise
The Sahibayn rule that the kaffarah is valid. Their premise: emancipation is indivisible, so freeing half immediately frees the entire slave. Thus the whole freeing occurred before intercourse.
They hold 'al-i'tāq lā yatajazzā'' – emancipation does not divide.
4
Apply each premise to the Quranic condition
Both sides agree the condition is that freeing must be before intercourse. The disagreement is on what constitutes 'freeing the slave'. For Abu Hanifa, the act of freeing is not complete until the whole slave is free; for the Sahibayn, it is complete immediately upon any part.
This is a direct application of the usul principle of tajazzu' al-‘itq.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A person following Abu Hanifa must free the entire slave before intercourse (or choose fasting/feeding). One following the Sahibayn may free half before and the rest after, and it still counts.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi tradition is often the view of the Sahibayn.

وان اعتق نصف عبده عن كفارته ثم جامع التى ظاهر منها ثم اعتق با قيه لم يجز عند ابي حنيفة لان الا عتاق يتجزى عنده و شرط الاعتاق ان يكون قبل المسيس بالنص واعتاق النصف حصل بعده وعندهما اعتاق النصف اعتاق الكل فحصل الكل قبل المسيس
ترجمہ اور اگر اپنا آدھا غلام اپنے کفارہ سے آزاد کیا پھر اس عورت سے جماع کر لیا جس کے ساتھ ظہار کیا تھا، پھر باقی غلام آزاد کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتناق متجری ہوتا ہے۔ اور اعتناق کی شرط بنص قرآنی یہ ہے کہ جماع سے پہلے ہو، حالانکہ آدھا غلام آزاد کرنا جماع کے بعد ہوا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک آدھا آزاد کرنے سے پورا آزاد ہو جاتا ہے۔ لہذا پورا آزاد کرنا جماع سے پہلے پایا گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنے کفارہ میں آدھا کلام آزاد کیا پھر اس عورت سے ولی کر لی جس کے ساتھ ظہار کیا تھا۔ پھر باقی غلام کو آزاد کر دیا تو یہ آزاد کرنا حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک کافی نہیں ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک کافی ہو جائے گا۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک آزاد کرنا ٹکڑے ہو سکتا ہے۔ لہذا امام صاحب کے نزدیک آدھے غلام کو آزاد کرنا کل کو آزاد کرنا نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اعتاق کی شرط یہ ہے کہ غلام کا آزاد کرنا جماع سے پہلے ہو ۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالی نے فرمایا ہے فتحرير رقبة من قبل ان يتما سال ور یہاں نصف کا آزاد کرنا جماع کے بعد پایا گیا اس وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ اعتاق منجر می نہیں ہوتا اس لئے آدھے غلام کو آزاد کرنا پورے کو آزاد کرنا ہے۔ لہذا صاحبین کے نزدیک پورے غلام کی آزادی جماع سے پہلے پائی گئی ، اس وجہ سے جائز
And if he frees half his slave as his kaffarah, then has intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar, then frees the remaining half, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa because emancipation can be partial according to him, and the condition for emancipation (as kaffarah) is that it be before intercourse by the text (of the Quran), and freeing half occurred after intercourse. But according to the Sahibayn, freeing half is freeing all, so the whole freeing occurred before intercourse. Translation: And if he frees half his slave from his kaffarah, then has intercourse with the woman with whom he made zihar, then frees the remaining slave, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is not valid. Because according to Imam, emancipation can be partial. And the condition for emancipation by the Quranic text is that it be before intercourse, whereas freeing half occurred after intercourse. And according to the Sahibayn, freeing half frees the whole, so the whole freeing was found before intercourse. Commentary: The explanation of the issue is that a person freed half a slave from his kaffarah, then had intercourse with the woman with whom he made zihar, then freed the remaining slave. This freeing is not sufficient according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but it is sufficient according to the Sahibayn. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that according to him, freeing can be partial. Therefore, according to Imam, freeing half is not freeing the whole. And the condition of freeing is that the freeing of the slave be before intercourse, because Allah Almighty said: 'But the freeing of a slave before they touch one another.' Here, freeing half occurred after intercourse, for this reason it is not valid. And according to the Sahibayn, since emancipation is not partial, freeing half is freeing the whole. Therefore, according to the Sahibayn, the freeing of the whole slave was found before intercourse, for this reason it is valid.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage addresses a second scenario concerning the validity of kaffarah for zihar. The issue is: a person frees half of his own slave as kaffarah, then he has intercourse with his wife from whom he had made zihar, and then later he frees the other half of the slave. Is this kaffarah valid? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not valid. His reasoning is based on two premises: (1) emancipation can be partial (tajazzu'), so freeing half does not constitute freeing the whole slave; (2) the Quranic condition for kaffarah when freeing a slave is that it must be done before the spouses touch each other (Quran 58:3-4: 'min qabli an yatamāssā'). Since only half was freed before intercourse, and the second half was freed after, the condition is not met. Therefore, the kaffarah is not fulfilled. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), however, it is valid. Their reasoning is that emancipation is indivisible: freeing half immediately frees the entire slave. Thus, the whole slave is considered freed at the first act, which occurred before intercourse. Hence, the Quranic condition is satisfied. The commentary emphasizes that this difference stems directly from the fundamental disagreement on tajazzu' al-‘itq. The practical consequence is clear: Abu Hanifa requires the entire slave to be freed before intercourse, while the Sahibayn consider the entire slave freed upon freeing any part.

Key Terms
مسيس (masīs): Touching; here it refers to sexual intercourse between the spouses after zihar.
شرط (shart): Condition; here it means the legal requirement that the freeing of the slave must be before intercourse.
تجزؤ (tajazzu'): Divisibility; the principle that an act or contract can be done in parts. Here, applied to emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the underlying usul principle that causes the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in the scenario where half the slave is freed before intercourse?
A) Whether the Quranic condition is mandatory or recommended.
B) Whether emancipation can be partial (tajazzu') or is indivisible.
C) Whether the slave must be of sound health.
D) Whether the freeing must be done with a single utterance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of zihar kaffarah when freeing a slave in installments depends on whether emancipation is considered divisible (tajazzu') or indivisible; the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn's view that freeing any part frees the whole slave before intercourse.

Divisibility of Emancipation in Zihar Expiation: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zihar expiation with partial emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the divisibility of emancipation and apply the mufta bihi position to a zihar expiation scenario.

Core Idea
Freeing half a slave is freeing the whole according to Sahibayn, but not for Abu Hanifa – affecting zihar expiation.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of zihar expiation when a man frees half his slave, then has intercourse, then frees the other half. The disagreement centers on the principle of tajazzi al-‘itq – whether emancipation is divisible. You will learn both positions, their proofs, and the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position of Sahibayn
Identify that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the expiation is valid because freeing half a slave is considered freeing the whole slave immediately.
2
State Abu Hanifa's opposing view
Abu Hanifa rules the expiation invalid because he holds emancipation is divisible; complete emancipation occurs only when the second half is freed, which happens after intercourse, violating the condition.
3
Examine the proof of Sahibayn
Their proof: emancipation is not divisible (la yatajazza), thus freeing half equals freeing the whole, analogously to cases like mudabbar and umm walad where partial manumission results in full freedom.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that emancipation can be divisible (tajazzi), as seen in contracts like kitabah where partial freedom is possible; therefore the condition of complete emancipation before intercourse is not met.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: if a man frees half, has intercourse, then frees the rest, the expiation is valid (Sahibayn) or invalid (Abu Hanifa). The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view for ease in fulfilling expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اعتق نصف عبده عن كفارته ثم جامع التي ظاهر منها ثم اعتق باقيه لم يجز عند ابي حنيفة لأن الإعتاق يتجزى عنده و شرط الإعتاق ان يكون قبل المسيس بالنص واعتاق النصف حصل بعده وعندهما اعتاق النصف اعتاق الكل فحصل الكل قبل المسيس
And if he freed half his slave for his kaffarah, then he had intercourse with the one from whom he made zihar, then he freed the remainder, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa because emancipation is divisible according to him, and the condition of emancipation is that it be before intercourse by the text, and the freeing of half occurred after it. And according to the two (Sahibayn), freeing half is freeing the whole, so the whole occurred before intercourse.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of expiation when the sequence of freeing a slave and intercourse is altered. The issue: a man frees half his slave for zihar expiation, then has intercourse with his wife, then frees the remaining half. Imam Abu Hanifa rules this invalid because he holds that emancipation is divisible (tajazzi al-‘itq). Therefore, freeing half does not constitute freeing the entire slave until the second half is freed. Since the Qur’anic condition requires the emancipation to occur before intercourse (Quran 58:3: min qabli an yatamassa), and the complete emancipation (freeing of the second half) happened after intercourse, the kaffarah is not valid. In contrast, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that emancipation is not divisible; freeing half is equivalent to freeing the whole slave. Consequently, the entire slave is considered freed at the moment of the first half, which occurred before intercourse, so the expiation is valid. This difference stems from the principle of tajazzi al-‘itq (divisibility of emancipation). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position according to later scholars is that of the Sahibayn, as it facilitates the fulfillment of expiation.

Key Terms
اعتاق (i‘taq): Emancipation of a slave; the act of freeing.
تجزى (tajazzi): Divisibility; that a legal action can be partial and only complete upon full performance.
مظاهر (muzahir): A person who performs zihar (a pre-Islamic form of divorce declaring his wife like his mother's back).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is the expiation valid when a man frees half his slave, then has intercourse, then frees the other half?
A) Because the condition of emancipation before intercourse is waived for expiation.
B) Because freeing half is considered freeing the whole slave immediately.
C) Because the second half is freed before intercourse in intention.
D) Because the man can combine both halves as one act.

Key Takeaway
The validity of zihar expiation when freeing a slave in parts depends on whether emancipation is divisible—the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view that it is not, so freeing half suffices.

Ruling on Zihar and Kaffarah of a Slave
Explains that a slave's kaffarah for zihar is only fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's kaffarah for zihar and explain why the master's payment is invalid, referencing the principle of ownership capacity.

Core Idea
A slave's zihar kaffarah is only fasting because he cannot own property; even his master's payment is invalid.

After understanding the general rules of zihar, this passage addresses the specific case of a slave. The key point is that a slave lacks legal capacity to own property, which directly impacts how he can expiate his zihar. Let's examine the text to see the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Who is performing zihar in this passage? A male slave (ghulam). Recognize that the ruling is specific to a slave, not a free person.
The slave is owned by a master (mawla).
2
Identify the ruling
What is the required kaffarah for this slave? Only fasting (sawm). No other option is permitted.
The general options for zihar kaffarah are freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor.
3
Identify the reason
Why is wealth-based kaffarah not allowed? Because the slave has no ownership (la malk lahu). He is not qualified (ahl) to give kaffarah with wealth.
Ownership (milk) is a prerequisite for financial expiation.
4
Examine the edge case
What if the master tries to pay on his behalf by freeing a slave or feeding the poor? This is invalid (la yajuz) because the slave cannot become an owner through the master's act of giving.
The master cannot transfer ownership capacity to the slave.
5
Note an exception
The master may prevent the slave from fasting for other kaffarahs, but not for zihar. Why? Because the wife's right (haqq al-zawja) is attached to the zihar kaffarah.
This highlights the protection of the wife's right in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ظاهر العبد لم يجز فى الكفارة الا الصوم لانه لا ملك له فلم يكن من اهل التكفير بالمال وان اعتق المولى او اطعم عنه لم يجزه لانه ليس من اهل الملك فلا یصیر مالكابتملیكه ترجمہ اور اگر غلام نے اپنی بیوی سے ظہار کیا تو (اس کو ) کفارہ میں ( کوئی چیز ) جائز نہیں سوائے روزہ رکھنے کے، کیونکہ غلام کی کچھ ملک نہیں ہے، تو مال سے کفارہ دینے کی لیاقت ہی نہیں رکھتا ہے اور اگر غلام کی طرف سے اس کے مولیٰ نے رقبہ آزاد کر دیا یا اس کی طرف سے کھانا دے دیا تو بھی کافی نہیں ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہ غلام مالک ہونے کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا مولی کے مالک کرنے سے مالک نہیں ہو گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی غلام نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ ظہار کیا تو اس کا کفارہ صرف روزوں کے ذریعہ سے ادا ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ غلام کی ملک میں کوئی چیز نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے وہ مال سے کفارہ ادا کرنے کا اہل نہیں ہوگا اور اگر اس کے مولیٰ نے اس کی طرف سے غلام آزاد کیا یا کھانا دید یا تو بھی کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ یہ غلام مالک ہونے کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا مولی کے مالک کرنے سے مالک نہیں ہوگا ۔ واضح ہو کہ مولی اگر اپنے غلام کو کفارات کے روزں سے منع کرنا چاہے تو منع کر سکتا ہے سوائے کفارہ ظہار کے کیونکہ کفارہ ظہار کے ساتھ بیوی کا حق متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ (فتح القدير )
And if a slave performed zihar, he is not permitted in the kaffarah except fasting because he has no ownership, so he is not qualified for kaffarah with wealth. And if the master freed [a slave] or fed on his behalf, it is not valid for him because he is not capable of ownership, so he does not become an owner by the master's act of making him own. Translation: And if a slave performed zihar with his wife, he is not permitted in kaffarah except fasting, because the slave has no property, so he is not qualified to give kaffarah with wealth. And if the master freed a slave on his behalf or fed on his behalf, it is not sufficient, because the slave is not qualified to be an owner. Therefore, he does not become an owner by the master's act of making him own. Commentary: If a slave performed zihar with his wife, his kaffarah will be fulfilled only through fasting, because the slave does not own anything. Therefore, he will not be qualified to give kaffarah with wealth. And if his master freed a slave on his behalf or fed on his behalf, it is not sufficient, because the slave is not qualified to be an owner. So he does not become an owner by the master's making him owner. It is clear that if the master wants to prevent his slave from fasting for other kaffarahs, he can prevent him, except for kaffarah of zihar, because with kaffarah of zihar the wife's right is attached. (Fath al-Qadir)
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of a slave who performs zihar. The slave's kaffarah is restricted to fasting because he possesses no property. Therefore, freeing a slave or feeding the poor is not valid from him. If his master performs these acts on his behalf, they are also not accepted because the slave cannot become an owner through the master's giving. The master may prevent the slave from fasting for other kaffarahs, but not for zihar kaffarah because the wife's right is attached to it. This is from Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A form of divorce where a husband says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back' or similar, requiring kaffarah to resume marital relations.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for certain actions, here for zihar: either freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor.
غلام (ghulam): A male slave who is owned by another person and possesses no property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because slaves are not obligated to pay kaffarah
B) Because a slave has no property and cannot pay with wealth
C) Because fasting is the only option in the Quran
D) Because the master is responsible for the slave's kaffarah

Key Takeaway
A slave's zihar kaffarah is exclusively fasting because the slave cannot own property, and neither the slave nor his master can substitute it with financial expiation.

Feeding Sixty Poor for Zihar Kaffarah: The Third Option
Details of feeding sixty poor for zihar kaffarah with prescribed amounts and permissibility of value payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed amounts for feeding sixty poor in zihar kaffarah and explain the Hanafi permissibility of paying value instead of food.

Core Idea
Zihar kaffarah: feed sixty poor half sa' wheat each, or one sa' dates/barley, or pay their value – Hanafis permit qimah.

When a person who has performed zihar cannot fast the two consecutive months, the Quran and Sunnah prescribe feeding sixty poor. This lesson unpacks the specific measures, the proof from hadith, and the Hanafi allowance to pay the monetary value instead of food. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the analogy with sadaqat al-fitr and the conditions for value substitution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic command
Locate the verse (Surah al-Mujadilah 58:4) that orders feeding sixty poor when unable to fast. Note that the imperative 'at'im' indicates obligation.
2
Specify the quantity from hadith
Find the hadith of Aws ibn al-Samit and Sahl ibn Sakhr that defines the amount: half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley per poor person.
The hadith is ahad, so its dalala is zanni, but it establishes the wajib amount.
3
Understand the analogy to sadaqat al-fitr
The author compares this kaffarah to sadaqat al-fitr, which uses the same measures. The consideration is to fulfill a day's need for each poor person.
4
Note the Hanafi permission for value payment
The Hanafi school allows paying the monetary value (qimah) of the food instead of giving it in kind. This is based on the principle that the purpose is to relieve need, which can be achieved by money.
This is a point of ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school.
5
Recognize the restriction on substituting specified items
The text clarifies that one specified item (e.g., half sa' wheat) cannot be replaced by another specified item in a different quantity (e.g., half sa' dates) even if equal in value. Each item must follow its own prescribed measure.
This is a nuance of the commentary, not the matn itself.

کسی شخص نے عمدہ قسم کی نصف صاع کھجوریں دیں درانحالیکہ یہ کھجور میں نصف صاع گندم کی قیمت کے برابر ہیں یا زائد تو جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ نص ایک صاع کھجور پر وارد ہوتی ہے اسی طرح اگر نصف صاع گندم سے کم کا بدل واقع نہیں ہوسکتی اگر چہ قیمت میں زائد ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ (الکفایہ ، عنایہ ) صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل میں اوس بن صامت اور سہل بن مصعتر کی حدیث کا حوالہ دیا ہے۔ پس ہم آپ کی معلومات میں اضافہ کے لئے اوس بن صامت کی پوری حدیث نقل کرتے ہیں۔ ان خولة بنت ثعلبة قالت كنت تحت اوس بن الصامت و قد ساء خُلقه، لكبر سنه فراجعته في بعض ما امرنی به فقال انت على كظهر امى ثم خرج فجلس فى نادى قومه ثم رجع الى فراودنى عن النفس فقلتُ والذى نفس خولة بيده لا تصل الى و قد قلت ما قلت حتى يقضى الله و رسوله في ذالک فوقع على فدفعته بما تدفع به المرأة الشيخ الكبير و خرجت الى بعض جيراني فاخذت ثياباً فلبستها واتيت رسول الله فاخبرته بذالک فجعل يقول لى زوجک و ابن عمک و قد کبر فاحسنى اليه فجعلت اشكو الى الله ما ارى من سوء خلقه فتغشى رسول الله ما كان يتغشاه عند نزول الوحى فلما سرى عنه قال انزل الله فیک وفی زوجک بیانا و تلا قوله تعالى قد سمع الله قول التي تجادلك في زوجها و تشتکی الی الله الى اخر ايات الظهار ثم قال مر به فليعتق رقبة فقلت لا يجد ذالک یا رسول الله ثم قال مر به ان يصوم شهرين متتابعين فقلت هو شيخ كبير لا يطيق الصوم فقال مر به فليطعم ستين مسكينا فقلت ما عنده شيء يا رسول الله فقال انا سنعينه بعرق فقلت
When the one who performed zihar is unable to fast, he feeds sixty poor people, due to the saying of Allah: 'But if he is unable, then feed sixty poor people.' And he feeds every poor person half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley or its value, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Aws ibn al-Samit and Sahl ibn Sakhr: 'For every poor person half a sa' of wheat.' And because the consideration is to fulfill the need of the day for each poor person, so it is analogized to sadaqat al-fitr. And his (the author's) saying 'or its value' is our madhhab, and we have mentioned it in the book of zakat. Translation: And if the one who performed zihar does not have the ability to fast, he should feed sixty poor people. Because Allah said: 'But if he is unable, then feed sixty poor people.' And he should give each poor person half a sa' of wheat, or a sa' of dates or barley, or its value. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in the hadith of Aws ibn al-Samit and the hadith of Sahl ibn Sakhr: 'For each poor person half a sa' of wheat.' And because the consideration is to fulfill the need of a day for each poor person, so it is analogized to sadaqat al-fitr. And the author's statement 'or its value' is our madhhab, and he has mentioned it in the book of zakat. Commentary: ... (followed by details on substitution and the hadith of Khawlah)
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage explains the third option for zihar kaffarah: feeding sixty poor when unable to fast. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Mujadilah 58:4) and hadith of Aws ibn al-Samit and Sahl ibn Sakhr set the quantity: half a sa' of wheat per poor person. The author notes the analogy to sadaqat al-fitr which also uses these quantities. The Hanafi madhhab permits paying the value instead of the food. The commentary elaborates that value payment is allowed only for items not explicitly mentioned in the nass; for specified items like dates or barley, one must give the exact specified amount. For example, half a sa' of dates cannot replace half a sa' of wheat because the nass specifies a full sa' of dates. The hadith of Khawlah bint Tha'labah is quoted as the background for the revelation of the zihar verses, showing the progression: freeing a slave, fasting two months, feeding sixty poor.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume used for zakat and kaffarah; approximately 2.5 kg for wheat, 3 kg for dates/barley.
مسکین (miskin): A poor person who possesses less than the basic needs; eligible zakat and kaffarah recipients.
قیمت (qimah): Monetary value or equivalent of the prescribed food item, allowed by Hanafis for kaffarah.
صدقۃ الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan; its measurement is analogized to here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling if a person unable to fast gives half a sa' of dates instead of half a sa' of wheat for kaffarah?
A) It is valid because they are equal in value
B) It is not valid because the nass specifies one sa' of dates
C) It is valid because dates are better than wheat
D) It is not valid because dates are not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Feeding sixty poor for zihar must follow the prescribed measures; Hanafis permit paying value, but substitution between specified items is restricted.

The Hadith of Aus bin al-Samit as Proof for Zihar Kaffarah
Narrates the full hadith of Aus bin al-Samit as proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of zihar kaffarah as derived from the hadith of Aus bin al-Samit and explain how the Prophet's commands prove each step.

Core Idea
The Prophet's step-by-step commands establish the wajib sequence of zihar kaffarah: free a slave, fast, or feed sixty poor.

This lesson presents the full hadith of Aus bin al-Samit, the primary proof for the ruling of zihar expiation. By examining this hadith, you will see how the Prophet (peace be upon him) laid out the three options in order: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, and feeding sixty poor. The hadith also demonstrates the principle of helping those unable to fulfill the kaffarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Zihar is a forbidden form of divorce that makes kaffarah wajib. The hadith provides the specific expiation sequence.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the dalil is ahad hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Aus bin al-Samit is the proof. Read the full narration to understand the context and commands.
This is a sahih hadith narrated by Abu Dawud and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Each command (مر به) is an imperative, indicating obligation. The order shows sequential options: slave, fasting, feeding.
The Prophet's response to Khawla's objections supports the order.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
A minor difference exists about the meaning of 'araq' (container of food), but no dispute on the sequence itself.
Imam Abu Dawud preferred the view that an 'araq' holds two sa'.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school accepts this hadith as the basis for the sequence, and it is the mufta bihi position without intra-madhhab conflict.
The ruling is consistent across the school.

صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل میں اوس بن صامت اور سہل بن مصعتر کی حدیث کا حوالہ دیا ہے۔ پس ہم آپ کی معلومات میں اضافہ کے لئے اوس بن صامت کی پوری حدیث نقل کرتے ہیں۔

ان خولة بنت ثعلبة قالت كنت تحت اوس بن الصامت و قد ساء خُلقه، لكبر سنه فراجعته في بعض ما امرنی به فقال انت على كظهر امى ثم خرج فجلس فى نادى قومه ثم رجع الى فراودني عن النفس فقلتُ والذى نفس خولة بيده لا تصل الى و قد قلت ما قلت حتى يقضى الله و رسوله في ذالک فوقع على فدفعته بما تدفع به المرأة الشيخ الكبير و خرجت الى بعض جيراني فاخذت ثياباً فلبستها واتيت رسول الله فاخبرته بذالک فجعل يقول لى زوجک و ابن عمک و قد کبر فاحسنى اليه فجعلت اشكو الى الله ما ارى من سوء خلقه فتغشى رسول الله ما كان يتغشاه عند نزول الوحى فلما سرى عنه قال انزل الله فیک وفی زوجک بیانا و تلا قوله تعالى قد سمع الله قول التي تجادلك في زوجها و تشتکی الی الله الى اخر ايات الظهار ثم قال مر به فليعتق رقبة فقلت لا يجد ذالک یا رسول الله ثم قال مر به ان يصوم شهرين متتابعين فقلت هو شيخ كبير لا يطيق الصوم فقال مر به فليطعم ستين مسكينا فقلت ما عنده شيء يا رسول الله فقال انا سنعينه بعرق فقلت و انا اعينه بعرق ايضاً فقال افعلی و استوصی به خیراً

[؟فہرست؟] خولہ بنت ثعلبہ نے کہا کہ میں اوس بن صامت کے نکاح میں تھی اور وہ اپنے بڑھاپے کی وجہ سے بدمزاج سا ہو گیا تھا پس میں نے اس سے ایک ایسے کام میں مراجعت کی جس کا اس نے مجھے کو حکم دیا تھا تو اس نے انت علی کظہر امی کہا پھر وہ نکل کر اپنی برادری کی مجلس میں بیٹھ گیا پھر لوٹ کر میرے پاس آیا اور مجھ کو منانے لگا تو میں نے کہا اس ذات کی قسم جس کے قبضہ میں خولہ کی جان ہے مجھ کو ہاتھ نہ لگانا اور جو میرے منہ میں آیا میں نے کہہ ڈالا یہاں تک کہ اس بارے میں اللہ اور اس کا رسول کوئی فیصلہ کرے پس وہ میرے اوپر گر پڑا تو میں نے اس کو اس طرح دور کیا جس طرح عورت بوڑھے آدمی کو دور کرتی ہے اور میں نکل کر اپنے پڑوسی کے یہاں چلی گئی پھر میں کپڑے پہن کر حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس آئی اور یہ پورا واقعہ سنایا۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم فرمانے لگے تمھارا شوہر ہے اور تمھارا چا زاد بھائی ہے، بیچارا بوڑھا ہو نہیں رکھتا پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ اچھا اس کو حکم دو کہ وہ ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا دے میں نے کہا اللہ کے رسول اس کے پاس تو کچھ بھی نہیں ہے۔ (یہ سن کر) آپ نے فرمایا کہ میں کے مدد کہ اس کی ایک عرق کے ساتھ مدد کر دوں گا، میں نے کہا کہ میں بھی ایک عرق سے مدد کر دوں گی آپ نے فرمایا کہ دے اور اس کو خیرات کر دینے کا حکم دے۔ (عنایہ ) حدیث میں لفظ عرق آیا ہے امام ابو داؤد نے روایت کیا ہے کہ ایک عرق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوتا ہے اور بعض حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ عرق ایسا ظرف ہے جس میں تمہیں صاع کی گنجائش ہو امام ابوداؤد نے فرمایا کہ یہ زیادہ صحیح ہے اور عقل بھی اس کی مقتضی ہے کہ یہی زیادہ صحیح ہو کیونکہ اگر ایک عرق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوتا تو پھر دوسرے کی کیا ضرورت تھی کفارہ میں وہی کافی ہو جا تا واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
The author of Hidayah has cited as proof the hadith of Aus bin al-Samit and the hadith of Sahl bin Mus’tar. So we narrate the complete hadith of Aus bin al-Samit for your added knowledge. Indeed, Khawla bint Tha'laba said: I was under (married to) Aus bin al-Samit, and his character had become bad due to old age. I argued with him about something he commanded me, and he said, 'You are to me like my mother's back.' Then he went out and sat in the gathering of his people. Then he returned to me and tried to seduce me. I said, 'By the One in whose hand is the soul of Khawla, you will not reach me; you have said what you said until Allah and His Messenger decide regarding this.' So he fell upon me, and I pushed him away as a woman pushes away an old man. I went to some of my neighbors, took clothes, wore them, and came to the Messenger of Allah and informed him of this. He kept saying to me, 'He is your husband and your cousin, and he has grown old, so treat him well.' I started complaining to Allah about what I saw of his bad character. Then the Messenger of Allah was covered with what used to cover him at the time of revelation. When it cleared from him, he said, 'Allah has revealed concerning you and your husband a detailed statement.' And he recited the verse: 'Indeed Allah has heard the statement of her who argues with you concerning her husband and complains to Allah...' up to the end of the verses of zihar. Then he said, 'Command him to free a slave.' I said, 'He cannot find that, O Messenger of Allah.' Then he said, 'Command him to fast two consecutive months.' I said, 'He is an old man, he cannot bear fasting.' Then he said, 'Command him to feed sixty poor people.' I said, 'He does not have anything, O Messenger of Allah.' He said, 'I will help him with an 'araq.' I said, 'And I will also help him with an 'araq.' He said, 'Do so, and recommend good treatment to her.' (Inayah) The word 'araq' appears in the hadith. Imam Abu Dawud narrated that one 'araq is sixty sa'. Some scholars are of the opinion that 'araq is a container that holds two sa'. Imam Abu Dawud said this is more correct, and reason also requires that this is more correct, because if one 'araq were sixty sa', then there would be no need for another (help) as that would be sufficient for the kaffarah. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage provides the full hadith of Aus bin al-Samit, which serves as a primary proof for the ruling of zihar kaffarah. The hadith recounts the story of Khawla bint Tha'laba and shows the sequence of expiation: first freeing a slave, then fasting two months consecutively, then feeding sixty poor. The hadith also mentions the Prophet's (peace be upon him) guidance and the word 'araq'. A point of clarification is offered regarding the meaning of 'araq': according to Imam Abu Dawud, it is a container that holds two sa', not sixty sa', as some thought. This explanation ensures that the hadith is understood correctly. The commentator includes this hadith to reinforce the divine legislation and the mercy shown to those unable to perform the earlier options.

Key Terms
رقبہ (raqabah): A slave, the first option in zihar kaffarah.
شہرین متتابعین (shahrayn mutatabi'ayn): Two consecutive months of fasting as the second option in kaffarah.
عرق (araq): A container of food; according to the authentic opinion, it holds two sa'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) To give charity
D) To divorce his wife

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Aus bin al-Samit is the foundational proof for the wajib sequence of zihar kaffarah: freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding the poor.

The Kaffarah of Zihar: Sequential Obligations
Narrating the story of Khawla and deriving the sequential kaffarah ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sequential options for kaffarah of zihar and explain the Hanafi position on feeding (it'am) versus the Shafi'i requirement of tamlik.

Core Idea
Kaffarah of zihar must follow a strict sequence: free a slave, or fast two months, or feed sixty poor.

The passage opens with the story of Khawla bint Tha'labah, which is the sabab (occasion) for the revelation of Surah al-Mujadilah. From this incident, the Prophet ﷺ established a sequential kaffarah for zihar. This lesson unpacks that ruling, the proof from hadith, and the Hanafi analogy to sadaqat al-fitr for the feeding option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab and the ruling
Read the story of Khawla bint Tha'labah. Note that the Prophet ﷺ commanded a slave to be freed, then fasting, then feeding. This sequence is the central ruling.
The sabab al-nuzul provides context but the ruling is general.
2
Extract the three options
From the hadith, list: 1) freeing a slave, 2) fasting two consecutive months, 3) feeding sixty poor persons. Note the order is strict (tartib).
The imperative form (أمر) indicates obligation (wujub).
3
Understand the sequential condition
The next option is only allowed if the previous is impossible. This is derived from the Prophet’s acceptance of Khawla’s excuses.
Hanafis: must follow order; Shafi'is: order is recommended but not compulsory.
4
Analyze the qiyas for feeding
The feeding amount is analogized to sadaqat al-fitr: each poor gets half a sa' of wheat (or equivalent). However, in zihar the number (60) is fixed, unlike zakat fitr.
This qiyas is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) supporting the hadith.
5
Cross-madhhab difference: tamlik vs it'am
The Hanafi school considers feeding (it'am) sufficient – enabling the poor to eat. The Shafi'i school requires transfer of ownership (tamlik). This affects whether you can invite them to a meal or must give the food in hand.
The difference arises from interpretation of 'feeding' in the verse.

باب الظهار و انا اعينه بعرق ايضاً فقال افعلی و استوصی به خیراً یعنی خولہ بنت ثعلبہ نے کہا کہ میں اوس بن صامت کے نکاح میں تھی اور وہ اپنے بڑھاپے کی وجہ سے بدمزاج سا ہو گیا تھا پس میں نے اس سے ایک ایسے کام میں مراجعت کی جس کا اس نے مجھے کو حکم دیا تھا تو اس نے انت علی کظہر امی کہا پھر وہ نکل کر اپنی برادری کی مجلس میں بیٹھ گیا پھر لوٹ کر میرے پاس آیا اور مجھ کو منانے لگا تو میں نے کہا اس ذات کی قسم جس کے قبضہ میں خولہ کی جان ہے مجھ کو ہاتھ نہ لگانا اور جو میرے منہ میں آیا میں نے کہہ ڈالا یہاں تک کہ اس بارے میں اللہ اور اس کا رسول کوئی فیصلہ کرے پس وہ میرے اوپر گر پڑا تو میں نے اس کو اس طرح دور کیا جس طرح عورت بوڑھے آدمی کو دور کرتی ہے اور میں نکل کر اپنے پڑوسی کے یہاں چلی گئی پھر میں کپڑے پہن کر حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس آئی اور یہ پورا واقعہ سنایا۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم فرمانے لگے تمھارا شوہر ہے اور تمھارا چا زاد بھائی ہے، بیچارا بوڑھا ہو گیا۔ تم اس کے ساتھ حسن سلوک ہی کروپس میں اس کی بدمزاجی کا شکوہ اللہ سے کرنے لگی ۔ پس رسول اللہ گو اس چیز نے ڈھانپ لیا جو نزول وحی کے وقت آپ کو ڈھانپا کرتی تھی (یعنی آپ پر نزول وحی کی کیفیت طاری ہو گئی ) پس جب آپ سے وہ کیفیت کھول دی گئی تو فرمایا کہ اللہ نے تیرے اور تیرے شوہر کے بارے میں ایک تفصیلی بیان نازل کیا ہے اور پھر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قد سمع الله قول التي تجاد لک فی زوجها الآية تلاوت فرمائی پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس کو ایک رقبہ آزاد کرنے کا حکم دو میں نے کہا یہ اس کے پاس نہیں ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ اچھا پے در پے دو ماہ کے روزے رکھنے کا حکم دو میں نے کہا وہ تو بہت بوڑھا ہے روزے کی طاقت نہیں رکھتا پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ اچھا اس کو حکم دو کہ وہ ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا دے میں نے کہا اللہ کے رسول اس کے پاس تو کچھ بھی نہیں ہے۔ (یہ سن کر) آپ نے فرمایا کہ میں کے مدد کہ اس کی ایک عرق کے ساتھ مدد کر دوں گا، میں نے کہا کہ میں بھی ایک عرق سے مدد کر دوں گی آپ نے فرمایا کہ دے اور اس کو خیرات کر دینے کا حکم دے۔ (عنایہ ) حدیث میں لفظ عرق آیا ہے امام ابو داؤد نے روایت کیا ہے کہ ایک عرق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوتا ہے اور بعض حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ عرق ایسا ظرف ہے جس میں تمہیں صاع کی گنجائش ہو امام ابوداؤد نے فرمایا کہ یہ زیادہ صحیح ہے اور عقل بھی اس کی مقتضی ہے کہ یہی زیادہ صحیح ہو کیونکہ اگر ایک عرق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوتا تو پھر دوسرے کی کیا ضرورت تھی کفارہ میں وہی کافی ہو جا تا واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
دوسری حدیث سہل بن مسفر کے حوالہ سے اسی حدیث کے ہم معنی ہے مگر یہ صاحب ہدایہ کا سہو ہے کیوں کہ سہل بن مطر لیشی صحابہ میں سے ہیں مگر سہل بن صحر سے ظہار کے متعلق کوئی حدیث مروی نہیں ہے اور مبسوط میں سلمہ بن صحر مذکور ہے بہر حال ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر ظہار کرنے والے کو رقبہ آزاد کرنے پر قدرت نہ ہو تو دو ماہ کے روزے رکھے اور اگر اس پر بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو ساتھ مساکین کو
کھانا دے۔
دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معتبر ہر مسکین کی ایک دن کی ضرورت پوری کرنا ہے۔ لہذا اس کو مقدار میں صدقۃ الفطر پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ مگر تھوڑے سے فرق کے ساتھ وہ یہ کہ ظہار میں عدد اور مقدار دو معتبر ہیں یعنی ایک مسکین کو نصف صاع گندم سے کم نہیں دیا جائے گا اور نہ زیادہ دیا جائے گا کیوں کہ ساٹھ کا عدد ضروری ہے اور صدقۃ الفطر میں مقدار معتبر ہے نہ کہ عدد پس ایک فطرہ کئی مساکین کو اور کئی فطرے ایک مسکین کو دیئے جاسکتے ہیں صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کا قول قیمتہ ذالک احناف کا مذہب ہے اور ہم اس کو کتاب الزکوۃ میں
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, Volume 5. Chapter of Zihar: And I will help him with an 'araq as well, so he said 'do so' and 'treat her well'. i.e., Khawla bint Tha'labah said: I was married to Aws ibn Samit, and due to his old age he had become somewhat ill-tempered. So I returned to him regarding a matter he had commanded me, and he said: 'You are to me like the back of my mother.' Then he went out and sat in the gathering of his clan, then returned to me and tried to appease me. So I said: 'By the One in Whose hand is the soul of Khawla, do not touch me,' and I said whatever came to my mouth until Allah and His Messenger decide about this matter. Then he fell upon me, so I pushed him away as a woman pushes away an old man, and I went out to my neighbor's house. Then I dressed and came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and narrated the entire incident. He (peace be upon him) said: 'He is your husband and your cousin brother; the poor man has become old. You should treat him kindly.' Then I began to complain about his ill-temper to Allah. Then the Messenger of Allah was overcome by what used to overcome him at the time of revelation. When the state left him, he said: 'Allah has revealed a detailed statement concerning you and your husband,' and then he recited the verse: 'Indeed Allah has heard the speech of her who disputes with you concerning her husband...' Then he said: 'Command him to free a slave.' I said: 'He does not have that.' He said: 'Then command him to fast two consecutive months.' I said: 'He is very old; he cannot fast.' He said: 'Then command him to feed sixty poor persons.' I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, he does not have anything.' Upon hearing this, he said: 'I will help him with an 'araq (of dates).' I said: 'And I will also help with an 'araq.' He said: 'Give it and command him to give it in charity.' (al-'Inayah) In the hadith, the word 'araq appears. Imam Abu Dawud narrated that one 'araq is sixty sa'. Some scholars opine that 'araq is a container that holds one sa'. Imam Abu Dawud said this is more correct, and reason also necessitates this, because if one 'araq were sixty sa', then there would be no need for another; that would suffice for the kaffarah. And Allah knows best what is correct. The second hadith from Sahl ibn Musaffir is similar in meaning, but this is a slip of the author of al-Hidayah, because Sahl ibn Muttar al-Laysi is among the Companions, but no hadith regarding zihar is narrated from Sahl ibn Sahar. In al-Mabsut, Salamah ibn Sahar is mentioned. However, from these ahadith, it is learned that if the one who performs zihar is unable to free a slave, he should fast two months, and if he is unable to do that, he should feed sixty poor persons. Second rational evidence: The objective is to satisfy each poor person for one day. Therefore, it is analogized to sadaqat al-fitr in quantity, with a slight difference: in zihar, both number and quantity are considered, i.e., each poor person should be given no less than half a sa' of wheat and no more, because the number sixty is necessary. In sadaqat al-fitr, quantity is considered, not number; thus one fitrah can be given to several poor persons, and several fitrahs can be given to one poor person. The author of al-Hidayah says: 'Al-Quduri's statement about its value is the madhhab of the Hanafis, and we have mentioned it in detail in the Book of Zakat.'
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) for the kaffarah of zihar. It opens with the story of Khawla bint Tha'labah, which is the sabab (occasion) for the revelation of the initial verses of Surah al-Mujadilah. The hadith establishes the sequential order of kaffarah: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, feeding sixty poor persons. The text then discusses the measurement of 'araq (a container for dates), clarifying that the sounder opinion is that it holds one sa', not sixty. A note corrects an error in al-Hidayah regarding the narrator Sahl ibn Musaffir. Finally, a rational proof (qiyas) is given: the feeding of sixty poor is analogized to sadaqat al-fitr, but with the distinction that in zihar, each poor must receive at least half a sa' of wheat, and the number sixty is fixed. The author references al-Quduri's position that giving the value in cash is also valid, as will be explained in Kitab al-Zakah.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' which makes her unlawful to him until kaffarah is performed.
عرق ('araq): A container for dates; according to the preferred opinion, it holds one sa', not sixty.
صدقۃ الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, typically half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates or barley per person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first option for kaffarah in zihar according to the hadith?
A) Fasting two months
B) Feeding sixty poor persons
C) Freeing a slave
D) Giving charity in cash

Key Takeaway
The kaffarah of zihar must follow a strict sequence: free a slave, then fast two consecutive months, then feed sixty poor persons, with the option of cash value when all are impossible.

Combining Grains in Zihar Kaffarah: The Principle of Unified Jins
Ruling on giving one mann wheat and two mann dates or barley together

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mixing wheat and dates/barley for zihar kaffarah and explain why it is permissible.

Core Idea
Mixing wheat and dates in kaffarah is valid because both serve the same purpose of feeding — the type (jins) is unified.

This lesson examines a specific case from the chapter of zihar: a person gives one mann of wheat and two mann of dates to a poor person. Is this acceptable? The answer hinges on understanding the legal concept of jins (type) and the objective (maqsud) of kaffarah. Let's break down the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving a combination of wheat and dates as kaffarah for zihar. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Understand the measurements
One mann = 1/4 sa'. So 1 mann wheat = 1/4 sa' wheat, 2 mann dates = 1/2 sa' dates. The required amount per poor person is half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley.
1 sa' = 4 mann
3
Identify the principle
The text states that the mixture is permissible because the jins is unified (al-jins muttahid). Both wheat and dates are considered the same type for the purpose of kaffarah because they both serve as food.
Jins refers to the category of food grains.
4
Apply the principle
Since the objective is to provide food, and both grains serve that purpose, the combination achieves the required quantity. The mixture satisfies the maqsud, so the kaffarah is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الظهار
فان اعطى منا من برومنوين من تمر او شعير جاز لحصول المقصود اذ الجنس متحد ترجمہ . پس اگر من گیہوں دیا اور دو من کھجور یا جو دیئے تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ مقصود حاصل ہو گیا ہے کیونکہ جنس متحد ہے۔ تشریح ایک صاع میں چارمن ہوتے ہیں پس ایک من چوتھائی صاع کا ہوگا۔ اب مسئلہ یہ ہوگا کہ کفارہ دینے والے نے ایک مسکین کو ایک من گندم (چوتھائی صاع) اور دو من (نصف صاع کھجوریں یا جو دیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ مقصود یعنی کھانا دینا پایا گیا اس لئے کہ دونوں کی جنس ایک ہے اس طرح پر کہ دونوں چیزوں سے مقصود کھانا دینا اور بھوک دور کرنا ہے، لہذا ایک کو دوسرے سے مکمل کرنا جائز ہے۔
Chapter of Zihar. If he gives one mann of wheat and two mann of dates or barley, it is permissible because the objective is achieved, since the type is unified. Translation: So if he gave one mann of wheat and two mann of dates or barley, it is permissible, because the objective is achieved since the type is unified. Explanation: One sa' contains four mann, so one mann is a quarter sa'. Now the ruling is: if the one giving kaffarah gives one poor person one mann of wheat (quarter sa') and two mann (half sa') of dates or barley, it is permissible. Because the objective, i.e., giving food, is attained, since both are of the same type, in that both items are meant to give food and satisfy hunger. Therefore, it is permissible to complete one with the other.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (mas'alah) from the chapter of zihar. It addresses the case where a person gives a combination of grains to a poor person for the kaffarah. The author clarifies that if one gives one mann of wheat (which is half the required half sa') and two mann of dates or barley (which is a full half sa'), the total quantity satisfies the requirement. The key principle is that both wheat and dates/barley are considered the same 'jins' (type) for the purpose of feeding, as they both serve the same objective of providing nourishment. The measurement: 1 sa' = 4 mann, so 1 mann = 1/4 sa', 2 mann = 1/2 sa'. Since the required amount per poor person is half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley, combining them in this manner achieves the goal.

Key Terms
من (mann): A unit of weight; in this context, 1 mann = 1/4 sa' (approximately 0.75 kg but used as a measure of volume).
صاع (sa'): A standard measure of volume; in Hanafi law, 1 sa' is approximately 3.2 liters or 2.5 kg of wheat.
جنس (jins): Type or category; here, wheat, dates, and barley are considered the same jins for the purpose of kaffarah because they all serve as food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1 mann total
B) 2 mann total
C) 3 mann total
D) 4 mann total

Key Takeaway
Combining wheat and dates in zihar kaffarah is valid because both are considered the same type (jins) when the objective is to feed.

Delegating Zihar Kaffarah Feeding
Ruling on delegating the feeding of kaffarah to someone else

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that delegating the feeding of zihar kaffarah to another person is valid and explain the legal reasoning (istiqrad analogy) that supports it.

Core Idea
Delegating zihar feeding is valid because the command is treated as a loan, establishing the zihar-doer's ownership before transfer.

This lesson examines a specific ruling regarding zihar (a form of divorce). The question is whether a person who must feed the poor as expiation can authorize someone else to give the food on his behalf. The Hanafi text rules that such delegation is valid, and the reasoning provides insight into how ownership transfers in such transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and state the ruling: if the zihar-doer orders another to feed on his behalf and he does so, it suffices (اجزاه).
The ruling is that delegation is valid.
2
Analyze the legal reasoning (talil)
The text says 'because it is in the sense of a loan (istiqrad)'. Understand that the command to give food is treated as a request for a loan from the agent to the zihar-doer.
Analogy: the agent lends the food to the zihar-doer, who then gives it to the poor.
3
Understand the dual possession (qabd)
The poor person first takes possession as a deputy of the zihar-doer, then takes possession for himself. This ensures the zihar-doer becomes owner first, then transfers ownership to the poor.
The sequence: zihar-doer's ownership → transfer to poor.
4
Conclude the validity
Because the poor person's first possession is on behalf of the zihar-doer, the zihar-doer effectively owns the food at the moment of giving. Thus the delegation is valid.
Without this reasoning, the delegation might be invalid due to lack of ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان امر غيره ان يطعم عنه من ظهاره ففعل اجزاه لانه استقراض معنى والفقير قابض له اولا ثم لنفسه فتحقق تملكه ثم تمليكه ترجمہ اور اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے دوسرے شخص کو حکم دیا کہ میرے کفارہ ظہار میں میری طرف سے کھانا دیدے اور اس نے دید یا تو کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ قرض لینے کے معنی میں ہے اور فقیر نے پہلے اس کے واسطے قبضہ کر لیا پھر اپنے واسطے (قبضہ کر لیا ) تو اپنی ملک میں لینا پھر فقیر کو مالک بنانا متحقق ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے کسی دوسرے شخص کو حکم دیا کہ میرے کفارہ ظہار میں میری طرف سے کھانا دیدے، اس نے دید یا تو یہ کافی ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ ظہار کرنے والے کا اپنی طرف سے کھانا دینے کا حکم دینا معنی اس سے قرض طلب کرنا ہے اور . رہا فقیر تو وہ اولا ظہار کرنے والے کی طرف سے نائب بن کر اس کے واسطے قبضہ کرے گا پھر اپنے واسطے قبضہ کرے گا۔ پس ظہار کرنے والے کا پہلے خود مالک ہونا پھر فقیر کو مالک بنانا متفق ہو گیا ہے۔
And if he orders another to feed on his behalf for his zihar, and he does so, it suffices, because it is in the sense of a loan. The poor person first takes possession on his behalf, then for himself; thus his own ownership and then transferring ownership to the poor person are realized. Translation: And if the one who performed zihar orders another person to give food on his behalf for his zihar kaffarah, and he gives it, then the kaffarah is discharged. Because this is in the sense of borrowing, and the poor person first takes possession on his behalf, then for himself. So the zihar-doer first becomes owner himself and then makes the poor person owner. Explanation of the ruling: If the zihar-doer orders some other person: 'Give food on my behalf for my zihar kaffarah,' and he gives it, then it is sufficient. Because the zihar-doer's ordering to give food on his behalf means he is asking for a loan from that person. As for the poor person, he first takes possession as a representative on behalf of the zihar-doer, then takes possession for himself. Thus the zihar-doer first becomes the owner himself and then makes the poor person the owner; this is effective.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with a legal reasoning (talil) explaining the validity of delegation in zihar kaffarah. The issue: A person liable for zihar kaffarah tells someone else to give food to the poor on his behalf. The text rules that this is valid. The reasoning is that the order constitutes an istiqrad (request for a loan) in meaning: the zihar-doer effectively borrows the food from the agent, then the agent gives it to the poor. Technically, the poor person first takes possession as a deputy (na'ib) of the zihar-doer, and then takes possession for himself, thereby completing the transfer of ownership from the zihar-doer to the poor. This ensures that the zihar-doer's ownership is established before the gift is made.

Key Terms
استقراض (istiqrad): Requesting a loan; here, the zihar-doer's command is treated as asking for a loan of food from the agent.
قبض (qabd): Possession or taking hold; the poor person first takes possession on behalf of the zihar-doer, then for himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because it is a gift from the agent

Key Takeaway
Delegating the feeding of zihar kaffarah is valid because the command is legally treated as a loan, establishing the zihar-doer's ownership before the food reaches the poor.

Feeding vs. Tamlik in Zihar Kaffarah: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on it'am vs. tamlik in zihar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on feeding (it'am) in zihar kaffarah, explain the proof from the Quranic text, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position based on tamlik.

Core Idea
In zihar, 'it'am' means enabling to eat, not necessarily ownership transfer.

The Quran commands feeding the poor as expiation for zihar. But does 'feeding' require giving ownership of the food, or does inviting to eat suffice? Imam al-Shafi'i insists on ownership transfer (tamlik), analogizing to zakah. The Hanafi school, however, holds that the literal meaning of 'it'am' is broader and that ibahah (permission to eat) is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The matn affirms that feeding morning and evening (ghadāhā wa ashshā) is valid, whether the poor ate little or much.
The ruling applies to the kaffarah of zihar.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only tamlik (transfer of ownership) is valid, not merely ibahah.
He draws an analogy with zakah and sadaqat al-fitr.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues by qiyas: zakah and sadaqat al-fitr require tamlik because the poor's need is best met by ownership. Zihar kaffarah should follow suit.
The Quran for zakah uses 'ita' (giving), which implies tamlik.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response (lana) is that the Quran uses 'it'am' for zihar, which literally means enabling to eat (tamkin min al-ta'am). Both ibahah and tamlik achieve that. Zakah uses different words ('ita', 'ada') that connote tamlik, so qiyas is invalid.
Hanafi usul: haqiqah takes precedence over qiyas when the text is clear.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: inviting the poor to a meal suffices for Hanafis; Shafi'is require giving ownership (e.g., handing over the food as a gift).
Both schools consider the kaffarah valid within their own framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان غداهم و عشاهم جاز قليلا كان ما اكلوا او كثيرا وقال الشافعى لا يجزيه الا التمليك اعتبارا بالزكوة وصدقة الفطر وهذا لان التمليك ادفع للحاجة فلاينوب منابه الاباحة ولنا ان المنصوص عليه هو الاطعام وهو حقيقة في التمكين من الطعم وفى الاباحة ذالک کمافی التمليك اما الواجب في الزكوة الايتاء و في صدقة الفطر الاداء وهما للتمليك حقيقة ترجمہ پس اگر (ظہار کرنے والے نے ) ساٹھ فقیروں کو صبح میں کھانا دید یا پھر شام ا کھانا دید یا تو جائز ہوگیا خواہ انھوں نے کم کھایا ہو یا زیادہ کھایا ہو اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ مگر مالک کر دینا ، زکوۃ اور صدقۃ الفطر پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ مالک کر دینا ضرورت کو زیادہ دور کرتا ہے۔ لہذا مباح کرنا اس کے قائم مقام نہ ہوگا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نص قرآنی میں لفظ اطعام
If he feeds them morning and evening, it is valid, whether they ate little or much. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not valid except with tamlik (transfer of ownership), by analogy with zakah and sadaqat al-fitr. This is because tamlik is more effective in meeting the need, so ibahah (permitting use) does not stand in its place. Our proof is that the text (Quran) states 'it'am' (feeding), which literally means enabling to eat, and ibahah achieves that as tamlik does. As for what is obligatory in zakah, it is 'ita' (giving), and in sadaqat al-fitr, it is 'ada' (payment), and both literally mean tamlik. Translation: Then if (the zihar-doer) fed the sixty poor in the morning or fed them in the evening, it is valid, whether they ate little or much. Imam al-Shafi'i said: This is not sufficient; only making them owners (tamlik) is valid, by analogy with zakah and sadaqat al-fitr. This is because tamlik removes the need more effectively; therefore, ibahah (making permissible) does not stand in its place. And our proof is that the Quranic text uses the word 'it'am' (feeding), which literally means enabling to eat, and ibahah achieves that just as tamlik does.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the manner of fulfilling the kaffarah of zihar. The issue: If the person liable for kaffarah invites the poor to eat (e.g., arranges a meal) rather than giving them ownership of the food, does it suffice? The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that it suffices. The Shafi'i objection, presented here, is that only tamlik (transfer of ownership) is valid, analogizing to zakah and sadaqat al-fitr where the poor must own the item. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that tamlik is more effective in satisfying need. The Hanafi response (lana) is that the Quranic text for zihar uses 'it'am' (feeding), which is literally enabling to eat (tamkin min al-ta'am), and this is achieved through ibahah (making the food permissible for the poor to eat) just as it is achieved through tamlik. They distinguish zakah and sadaqat al-fitr, where the texts use 'ita'' or 'ada'' which imply tamlik, whereas zihar specifically uses 'it'am'. The commentary emphasizes that the purpose is to feed and satisfy hunger, which can be done by inviting to eat.

Key Terms
اطعام (it'am): Feeding, enabling someone to eat; in zihar, the Quranic command to feed the poor.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; making the poor person the owner of the food.
اباحہ (ibahah): Making permissible; here, allowing the poor to eat the food without transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof that feeding (it'am) suffices without tamlik in zihar kaffarah?
A) Analogy with zakah
B) The Prophet's practice
C) The literal meaning of 'it'am' in the Quran
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
In zihar kaffarah, the Hanafi school accepts feeding via ibahah (inviting to eat) as valid, based on the literal meaning of 'it'am' in the Quran, distinguishing it from zakah which uses terms implying tamlik.

It'am in Zihar Kaffarah: Ibahah vs Tamlik
Inter-madhhab dispute on it'am in zihar kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the meaning of it'am in zihar kaffarah, identify the Shafi'i qiyas argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on textual literalism.

Core Idea
It'am means giving control over eating; ibahah fulfills it just as tamlik does.

When performing kaffarah for zihar, the Quran commands feeding sixty poor people. But what does 'feeding' (it'am) actually require? In this passage, the Hanafi school argues that making food available (ibahah) is sufficient, while Imam al-Shafi'i insists on transferring ownership (tamlik). The debate hinges on the literal meaning of the Quranic word and the validity of qiyas. Let us walk through the arguments on both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school says about the meaning and fulfillment of it'am in zihar kaffarah. Note that ibahah (making food permissible) is sufficient.
The text explicitly says it'am's real meaning is 'giving control over eating' and that ibahah achieves this.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State Imam al-Shafi'i's view: tamlik (transfer of ownership) is necessary, and ibahah does not suffice. Understand his basis for this claim.
He analogizes to zakat and sadaqat al-fitr.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof (qiyas)
Identify the Shafi'i argument: qiyas to zakat and sadaqat al-fitr, where terms ita' and ada' imply ownership. Understand why he draws this analogy.
This is a qiyas from one act of worship to another.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reject the qiyas. Identify their two-part response: (1) the literal meaning of 'it'am' includes ibahah; (2) zakat and sadaqat al-fitr use different terms (ita', ada') that specifically require ownership, so the analogy fails.
The response is based on the difference in textual wording.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Work out the thamarah al-khilaf: if a person feeds sixty poor people by inviting them to a meal (ibahah) without giving ownership, is the kaffarah valid? Hanafi: yes; Shafi'i: no.
This is the key outcome of the dispute.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم (مذکور ) ہے اور اطعام کے حقیقی معنی ہیں کھا لینے پر قابو دینا اور مباح کرنے میں یہ بات ( حاصل ہو جاتی ) ہے۔ جیسے مالک کر دینے میں (حاصل ہوتی ہے ) اور رہی زکوۃ تو مباح کرنا اس کا قائم مقام نہ ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نص قرآنی میں لفظ اطعام آیا ہے اور اطعام کے حقیقی معنی ہیں کھا لینے پر قابو دینا ( قدرت دینا ) اور یہ بات کھانے کو مباح کرنے میں اسی طرح حاصل
