درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ زکوۃ میں ایتاء ( دینا) فرض ہے اسلئے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے تو الزکوۃ یعنی زکوۃ دو اور صدقۃ الفطر میں ادا کرنا واجب ہے اسلئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے ادوا عمن تمونون یعنی جن کی تم کفالت کرتے ہو ان کی طرف سے ادا کرو اور دینا اور ادا کرنا ان دونوں کے حقیقی معنی مالک کر دینے کے ہیں نہ کہ صرف قدرت دینے کے۔
Chapter of Zihar. 132. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary on al-Hidaya, volume five: The real meaning of it'am (feeding) is to give control over eating, and this is achieved by making food permissible (ibahah) just as it is achieved by giving ownership (tamlik). As for zakat, giving (ita') is fard, and for sadaqat al-fitr, paying (ada') is wajib. The real meaning of both 'giving' and 'paying' is giving ownership. Explanation: If the person who performed zihar fed sixty poor people two full meals, the expiation is fulfilled regardless of whether they ate little or much. But if he fed them one meal for two days, it does not suffice because the need of one day must be satisfied, which is achieved by feeding morning and evening. It is also narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that if he fed sixty poor people in the morning and another sixty in the evening, the expiation is not fulfilled. Imam al-Shafi'i says that feeding morning and evening is not sufficient in expiation; rather, giving ownership is necessary, i.e., he must say, 'I have given this food into your ownership,' whether they eat it or not, as in zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. Thus, Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes expiation to zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. The reason ibahah is not valid is that giving ownership fully satisfies the poor person's need. Therefore, merely making food permissible to eat does not stand in its place. Our evidence is that the Qur'anic text uses the word 'it'am', and its real meaning is to give control over eating (enablement). This is achieved by making food permissible just as it is achieved by giving ownership. So the obligation is fulfilled by either method: by giving control over eating, because it observes the exact text; and by giving ownership, because ownership includes the textual meaning, since when the poor person becomes owner, he will eat it or use it for other needs. Thus, giving ownership is also a substitute for what is textually prescribed. As for zakat and sadaqat al-fitr, it is not correct to analogize zihar expiation to them because in zakat, 'giving' (ita') is fard due to Allah's command, 'Give zakat,' and in sadaqat al-fitr, 'paying' (ada') is wajib due to the Prophet's ﷺ saying, 'Pay on behalf of those you support.' The real meanings of 'giving' and 'paying' are giving ownership, not merely giving ability.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the nature of 'it'am' (feeding) in the kaffarah (expiation) for zihar. The Hanafi school, based on the literal meaning of the Quranic word 'it'am', holds that the obligation is fulfilled by enabling the poor to eat (ibahah), such as by inviting them to a meal, without requiring that ownership of the food be transferred to them. The Shafi'i school argues that giving ownership (tamlik) is necessary, analogizing to zakat and sadaqat al-fitr where the Quran and Sunnah use terms (ita' and ada') that imply transfer of ownership. The text first presents the Hanafi position, then the Shafi'i objection, and then the Hanafi response. The Hanafi response is that the word 'it'am' in the Quran (for zihar) literally means giving control over eating, which is achieved by ibahah. Ownership is not required but is also valid because it includes the meaning of it'am. The Hanafi response further distinguishes zakat and sadaqat al-fitr from zihar kaffarah on the grounds that those acts of worship have specific texts using 'ita'' and 'ada'' which inherently imply ownership, whereas the text for zihar uses 'it'am' which has a broader meaning. Thus, the qiyas (analogy) of the Shafi'is is rejected. The passage also mentions an intra-Hanafi narration from Abu Hanifa regarding feeding morning and evening separately.

Key Terms
اطعام (it'am): In this text, it'am means to give control over eating, enabling a person to eat, whether by making food available (ibahah) or by giving ownership (tamlik).
اباحة (ibahah): Making food permissible for the poor to eat without transferring ownership, e.g., inviting them to a meal.
تمليك (tamlik): Transferring ownership of the food to the poor person, so they can dispose of it as they wish.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum requirement for fulfilling the 'it'am' in zihar kaffarah?
A) Transferring ownership of the food to the poor.
B) Making the food available for the poor to eat (ibahah).
C) Both A and B are required.
D) Feeding the poor twice a day for two days.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school follows the literal meaning of 'it'am', rejecting qiyas to zakat, thus ibahah suffices for zihar kaffarah.

Conditions for Feeding in Zihar Kaffarah
Stating conditions for feeding validity in zihar kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid feeding in zihar kaffarah and apply them to determine validity.

Core Idea
A suckling child cannot be a recipient; barley bread needs gravy to achieve satiation.

This passage from al-Hidayah discusses two critical conditions for the feeding (it'am) expiation in zihar. First, each recipient must be able to consume a full solid meal; a suckling child does not qualify. Second, if barley bread is given, it must be accompanied by gravy (idam) to enable satiety, whereas wheat bread does not require this. These rules ensure the expiation truly fulfills its purpose of satisfying hunger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
Recognize that this is from the chapter on zihar kaffarah. The ruling addresses two separate conditions: the eligibility of recipients and the requirement of gravy with barley bread.
Zihar is a form of divorce-like declaration requiring expiation.
2
Analyze the first condition: recipient must be able to consume fully
The text states that if a suckling child is among the sixty recipients, the expiation is not valid. Understand the rationale: the child cannot eat a full meal of solid food; his diet includes milk. Therefore, feeding him does not constitute a full it'am.
The term 'fatim' here means a child still dependent on milk, not necessarily weaned.
3
Analyze the second condition: idam with barley bread
Gravy (idam) is required only when bread is made from barley. Barley bread is dry and difficult to eat to satiety without accompaniment. Wheat bread is more filling and does not require gravy.
This is based on customary practice and the goal of satiation.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a hypothetical case: a person feeds sixty poor people, one of whom is a one-year-old child who cannot eat bread. Also, he gives barley bread without gravy. Determine validity: both conditions are violated, so the expiation is not fulfilled.

Source Text

ولوكان فيمن عشاهم صبى فطيم لا يجزيه لانه لا يستوفى كاملا ولابد من الإدام في خبز الشعير ليمكنه استيفاء الى الشبع وفى خبز الحنطة لا يشترط الادام
ترجمہ اور اگر ان لوگوں میں جن کو شام کا کھانا کھلایا ہے کوئی شیر خوار بچہ ہوتو کفارہ ادا نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ پور اطعام نہیں کھا سکتا ہے اور جو کی روٹی کے ساتھے سالن کا ہونا ضروری ہے تاکہ سیر ہو کر روٹی کھانا ممکن ہو اور گیہوں کی روٹی کے ساتھ سالن کا ہونا شرط نہیں ۔ تشریح مسلہ یہ ہے کہ وہ ساٹھ مساکین جن کو شام میں کھانا کھلایا ہے اگر ان میں کوئی شیر خوار بچہ ہوتو یہ کفارہ ادا نہیں ہو گا دلیل یہ ہے
کہ شیر خوار بچہ پور اطعام نہیں کھا سکتا ہے یعنی اس کی غذا صرف طعام نہیں بلکہ کچھ طعام اور کچھ دودھ پیتا ہے۔ لہذا اس کو پور الطعام. کھلانا صادق نہیں آئے گا۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر روٹی جو کی ہے تو اس کے ساتھ سالن کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ تا کہ میر ہو کر کھا سکے اور اگر گیہوں کی روٹی ہے تو اس کے ساتھ سالن کی شرط نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ گیہوں کی روٹی بغیر سالن کے بھی سیر ہو کر کھائی جاسکتی ہے۔
And if among those whom he fed in the evening there is a weaned child, it does not suffice because he does not consume fully. And gravy (idam) is necessary with barley bread so that he can eat to satiety, but with wheat bread gravy is not required. Translation: And if among those whom he fed in the evening there is a suckling child, the expiation is not fulfilled, because he cannot eat a full meal. With barley bread, gravy is necessary so that he can eat to satiety, but with wheat bread, gravy is not a condition. Explanation: The issue is that if among the sixty poor people fed in the evening there is a suckling child, the expiation is not performed, the proof being that a suckling child cannot eat a full meal; his diet is not solely food but partly milk. Therefore, feeding him a full meal is not considered valid. It is said that if the bread is barley, gravy is necessary so that he can eat to satiety, but if the bread is wheat, gravy is not a condition because wheat bread can be eaten to satiety without gravy.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the validity of feeding in zihar kaffarah when a suckling child is among the recipients. The text states that if among the sixty poor people fed in the evening there is a weaned (or suckling) child, the expiation is not fulfilled. The reason is that a suckling child does not consume a full meal of solid food; he still relies partly on milk. Therefore, providing a full meal to him does not count as it'am for that recipient. Additionally, the text discusses the requirement of gravy (idam) with barley bread to ensure satiation, but not with wheat bread, as wheat bread is more filling. This ruling is based on the principle that it'am must fulfill the purpose of satisfying hunger, and a child who cannot eat fully defeats that purpose. The source of this ruling is the authoritative Hanafi texts (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it applies to the method of feeding by ibahah.

Key Terms
فطيم (fatim): A weaned child; in this context, a child who is still dependent on milk (suckling).
ادام (idam): Gravy or accompaniment to bread, such as curry or stew, necessary for satiation with barley bread.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The kaffarah is valid only if the child has been weaned.
D) The kaffarah is valid only if gravy is provided with barley bread.

Key Takeaway
In zihar kaffarah feeding, each recipient must be able to eat a full meal, and barley bread must be accompanied by gravy to achieve satiation.

Feeding One Poor Person over Sixty Days vs. Giving All at Once in Zihar Kaffarah
Clarifying the requirement of feeding sixty poor people each day vs. one person over sixty days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on feeding one poor person over sixty days vs. giving all at once in zihar kaffarah, and identify when tafriq (distribution) is achieved.

Core Idea
Feeding one poor person daily for sixty days fulfills zihar kaffarah because each day's need is fresh; a lump sum to one person does not.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a key practical issue in zihar expiation: how is the requirement to 'feed sixty poor people' satisfied? The text walks through three scenarios, distinguishing between ibahah (making food available) and tamlik (transfer of ownership), and highlights the mandatory condition of tafriq (distribution). Understanding these nuances ensures the kaffarah is validly performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The kaffarah of zihar requires feeding sixty poor people (Quran 58:4). The text discusses different methods to fulfill this.
2
Understand the objective
The purpose of kaffarah is to satisfy the daily need of the poor. Need renews each day, so each feeding addresses a fresh need.
3
Apply to scenarios
(a) Feeding one person over sixty days: each day's need is separate, so tafriq is achieved. (b) Feeding one person sixty times in one day via ibahah: no fresh need, fails tafriq unanimously. (c) Tamlik in installments to one person in one day: dispute over whether need for ownership can renew.
4
Note the unanimous and disputed cases
Ibahah case is unanimously invalid. Tamlik in installments is disputed among Hanafi scholars.
5
Conclude the relied-upon position
The mufta bihi is that tafriq is wajib. Feeding one person over sixty days is valid; giving all at once to one person is not.

And if he gave one poor person for sixty days, it suffices. But if he gave it in one day, it is only valid for that one day. Because the objective is to fulfill the need of the needy, and need renews every day. So giving to the same person on the second day is like giving to another. This is in ibahah without disagreement. As for tamlik to one poor person in one day in multiple installments, some say it does not suffice, and some say it suffices because the need for tamlik renews within a single day, unlike if he gives it in one lump sum because tafriq (distribution) is wajib by the text. Translation: And if he gave one poor person for sixty days, it suffices. And if he gave it in one day, it is only valid for that one day, because the objective is to fulfill the need of the needy, and need renews every day. So giving to the same person on the second day is like giving to another. This ruling in ibahah is without disagreement. As for tamlik to one poor person in one day in multiple installments, some say it does not suffice, and some say it suffices because the need for tamlik renews within a single day, unlike if he gives it in one lump sum because distribution is wajib by the text. Explanation: The issue is that if one poor person is fed for sixty days, the kaffarah is fulfilled. If given in one day, it only counts for one day. The proof is that the purpose of kaffarah is to remove the need of the needy, and need is renewed daily. So giving to the same person on the second day is like giving to another. Therefore, giving to one person for sixty days is like giving to sixty different people. Thus, in this case the kaffarah is fulfilled. 'Wa hadha fi al-ibahah' indicates the second form of the issue: if one poor person is fed sixty times in one day by way of ibahah, it is unanimously invalid because wajib is distribution among sixty, which is not achieved either in reality or in effect. In reality, it's one person; in effect, one person does not need to eat sixty times in one day. As for tamlik to one poor person in one day in sixty installments of the total amount, there is disagreement. Some scholars say it is invalid because the need is to fulfill hunger. Others say it is valid because the need for tamlik can renew within a day. In contrast, if he gives ownership of the entire amount to one person in a single lump sum, it is unanimously invalid because distribution is wajib by the text, as Allah says, 'Feed sixty poor people.' And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the method of feeding in zihar kaffarah. It addresses three scenarios: (1) Feeding one poor person over sixty days: valid because the need is renewed daily, so each day's feeding counts as a separate instance, equivalent to feeding sixty different people. (2) Feeding one person multiple times in one day by ibahah (making food available): invalid because distribution among sixty individuals is required, and a single person cannot need that many meals in one day. (3) Giving ownership (tamlik) of the total amount to one person in multiple installments within one day: there is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars; some consider it valid because the need for ownership can recur, while others say it is invalid because the purpose is to satisfy immediate hunger. However, giving ownership in one lump sum to one person is unanimously invalid because the Quran requires distribution among sixty. The text emphasizes the requirement of tafriq (distribution) as a textual obligation from the verse 'fa-it'am sittina miskinan' (feed sixty poor people).

Key Terms
تفرقة (tafriq): Distribution; the requirement that the kaffarah be given to sixty different poor individuals or spread over sixty days.
اباحة (ibahah): Making food available without transfer of ownership. In this context, feeding sixty poor people by inviting them to a meal.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership of food. In kaffarah, tamlik can also fulfill the obligation, but the same tafriq rules apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on feeding one poor person for sixty consecutive days for zihar kaffarah?
A) It is invalid because it must be given to sixty different people.
B) It is valid because each day's need is separate, equivalent to feeding sixty people.
C) It is valid only if done by tamlik.
D) It is invalid because it must be given in one day.

Key Takeaway
The validity of zihar kaffarah feeding depends on achieving distribution (tafriq) either across sixty individuals or across sixty days, because each day's need is distinct.

Feeding One Poor Person for Zihar Expiation: Ibaha vs Tamlik
Intra-Hanafi dispute on feeding one miskin for zihar expiation via ibaha and tamlik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ibaha and tamlik in feeding for zihar expiation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on tamlik.

Core Idea
Ibaha with one person over sixty days suffices; tamlik in one day splits scholars on validity.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah dives into a nuanced issue of zihar expiation: how exactly must the feeding of sixty poor persons be carried out? The text distinguishes between ibaha (permitting consumption without ownership) and tamlik (transferring ownership), and reveals an important internal Hanafi disagreement about whether tamlik can be fulfilled by giving multiple payments to the same person in a single day. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the Quranic command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
The act is feeding as expiation (kaffarah) for zihar. It is a wajib duty. The passage discusses the mode of distribution.
The overall expiation is wajib; the manner of feeding is the focus.
2
Distinguish ibaha from tamlik
Ibaha means giving food for consumption without transferring ownership; tamlik means transferring ownership of the food to the poor person. The ruling differs based on this distinction.
These two modes have different legal effects.
3
State the agreed ruling for ibaha
For ibaha, feeding one poor person over sixty days is unanimously valid because need renews daily. Giving all in one day only counts for that day.
The reason: the purpose is to remove need, which recurs each day.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on tamlik
For tamlik, there is a dispute: some Hanafi scholars permit giving one poor person sixty portions in multiple payments within one day; others forbid it.
The disputed point is whether the need for ownership can renew within a single day.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
If tamlik multiple payments are allowed, one can expiate quickly by giving all to one person in one day in small installments. If not, one must either give to sixty distinct persons or give over sixty days.
The practical consequence affects feasibility and speed of expiation.

Source Text

Chapter of Zihar. Ashraf al-Bidaya sharh Urdu Hidaya volume five: that a suckling child cannot eat full food, meaning his nutrition is not only food but some food and some milk. Therefore, feeding him full food is not valid. They say that if bread is of barley, then having curry is necessary so that he can be satisfied, and if bread is of wheat, then having curry is not a condition because wheat bread can be eaten to satisfaction without curry. Because the purpose is to fulfill the need of the needy, and the need renews every day, so giving to him on the second day is like giving to another. And this is in ibaha without disagreement. Explanation of the issue: If one gave food to one poor person for sixty days, the expiation is fulfilled, and if he gave it in one day, it only suffices for that day. The proof is that the purpose of expiation is to remove the need of the needy, and need arises every day. So giving to the same poor person on the second day is like giving to another poor person. Therefore, giving to one poor person for sixty days is like giving to sixty poor persons. So in this case, the expiation is fulfilled. And from 'this in ibaha' he is explaining the second scenario: that if one gave food to one poor person in one day by way of ibaha sixty times, then it is unanimously not valid, because the obligation is to distribute to sixty poor persons, and that is not achieved neither in reality nor in effect. In reality it is not achieved because he is one poor person, and in effect because one person cannot have the need to eat sixty times in one day. As for making one poor person the owner of the full amount in sixty installments in one day, there is disagreement. Some jurists say this scenario is also invalid, because the consideration is removing need. And some hold that it is valid, because the need for ownership can arise anew in one day. In contrast, if he made one poor person the owner of all in one lump sum, it is unanimously invalid, because distributing is obligatory by Quranic text, for He said: 'Then feed sixty poor persons.' And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah discusses the rulings on feeding for the expiation of zihar. It first addresses the quality of food: for a suckling child, full meals are not required; for barley bread, curry is needed for satiation, while wheat bread alone suffices. The main ruling differentiates between ibaha (permitting consumption) and tamlik (transferring ownership). In ibaha, feeding one poor person over sixty days is valid, but feeding all in one day only counts for that day. The reason is that need renews daily, so feeding the same person on different days is like feeding different individuals. For tamlik, there is a dispute: some scholars say making one poor person the owner of sixty portions in one day via multiple payments is valid because the need for ownership can recur within a day, while others say it is invalid because the obligation is to distribute to sixty distinct individuals. All agree that giving the entire amount in one lump sum to one person is invalid due to the Quranic command to feed sixty poor persons.

Key Terms
اباحت (ibāḥah): Giving food to a poor person without transferring ownership, allowing them to consume it.
تملیک (tamlīk): Transferring ownership of food to a poor person, making them the owner of the items.
مسکین (miskīn): A poor person who is eligible to receive zakat or expiation payments.
کفارہ (kaffārah): Expiation for breaking an oath or committing a sin like zihar, requiring specific acts like freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding poor people.
ظہار (ẓihār): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a husband says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back', which requires expiation before resuming marital relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi scholars in this passage, what is the ruling if a person gives one poor person sixty portions of food by way of ibaha (permitting consumption) over sixty days?
A) It does not suffice because it is one person.
B) It suffices because the need renews daily so each day is like a different person.
C) It is not valid unless the food is given in a lump sum.
D) It is only valid if given as tamlik (ownership).

Key Takeaway
For zihar expiation, feeding one miskin for sixty days in ibaha suffices, but tamlik involves a disagreement among Hanafi scholars regarding multiple payments in one day.

Intercourse During Feeding for Zihar Expiation
Explains that intercourse during feeding does not require restarting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that intercourse during zihar feeding does not require restarting and explain the distinction between intrinsic and extrinsic prohibition.

Core Idea
Intercourse during zihar feeding does not invalidate the feeding because the prohibition is external, not intrinsic.

This passage addresses a practical question: if a husband who has chosen feeding as his zihar expiation has intercourse before completing the feeding, must he start over? The answer is no, but the reasoning hinges on a subtle usul distinction between prohibitions that affect validity and those that do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The scenario: a husband performing zihar expiation by feeding sixty poor people has intercourse with his wife during the feeding period. The ruling: he does not need to restart the feeding.
2
Understand the Quranic proof
The Quran (58:3-4) prescribes three expiation options: freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor. For the first two, intercourse must precede the expiation; for feeding, no such condition is stated. This absence of condition is key.
The proof is from 'dalil al-khitab' — the silence of the text on a condition indicates it is not required.
3
Grasp the distinction between intrinsic and extrinsic prohibition
Intercourse before or during feeding is prohibited (man'u li ghayrihi) because it may prevent the husband from switching to a superior expiation (freeing or fasting) if he later becomes able. This prohibition is external to the act of feeding itself, unlike a prohibition intrinsic to the act (man'u li dhatihi) which would invalidate it.
The feeding remains valid because the prohibition is for an external reason, not because the act is inherently forbidden.
4
Apply to the feeding case
Since the prohibition is external, the feeding already performed is valid and need not be restarted. The husband must still complete the remaining feeding, and he should avoid future intercourse until the expiation is fully discharged.

And if he had intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar during the period of feeding, he does not need to restart, because Allah Most High did not stipulate in the feeding that it should be before intercourse, but rather he is prohibited from intercourse before it because perhaps he may become capable of freeing a slave or fasting, and then those would occur after intercourse. And the prohibition due to an external reason does not negate the intrinsic validity. Translation: And if he had intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar during the feeding, he does not need to restart. Because Allah Most High did not make it a condition in the feeding that it be before intercourse, but he will be prevented from intercourse before it, because sometimes he may become able to free a slave or fast, and then those two would occur after intercourse. And the prohibition due to another meaning does not destroy the validity in itself. Explanation of the issue: If the person performing the expiation of zihar has intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar during the feeding, he does not need to restart the feeding. The proof is that Allah did not state the condition that feeding must be before intercourse, as He did for freeing a slave and fasting. However, the person should be prevented from intercourse before feeding, because it is possible that before completing the feeding, he becomes able to free a slave or fast, and then if he has already had intercourse, the freeing or fasting would have to occur after intercourse, whereas the Quranic text prohibits that. So it is better not to have intercourse before feeding. It should be clear that having intercourse before feeding is prohibited for an external reason (man'u li ghayrihi), and a prohibition for an external reason does not contradict the intrinsic validity of the feeding. Therefore, having intercourse before or during feeding does not necessitate the invalidity of the feeding. It is like praying at the time of adhan or during disliked times.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: if a husband who is performing the feeding-based expiation for zihar has intercourse with his wife before completing the feeding, does he need to start the feeding over? The ruling is clear: he does not need to restart. The reason is that the Quranic verse on feeding does not condition the validity of feeding on being before intercourse, unlike the conditions for freeing a slave or fasting (which must be before intercourse). However, it is still prohibited to have intercourse before completing the feeding, but this prohibition is for an external reason (man'u li ghayrihi): because the husband might later become able to free a slave or fast, which are superior forms of expiation, and if he has already had intercourse, those alternatives would occur after intercourse, which is prohibited. Since the prohibition is not intrinsic to the act of feeding, it does not invalidate the feeding. The commentator draws an analogy with praying during disliked times—the prayer is still valid despite the prohibition.

Key Terms
استئناف (isti'nāf): Starting the feeding from the beginning; restarting the expiation.
ممنوع لغیرہ (man'u li ghayrihi): A prohibition that exists due to an external reason, not because the act itself is intrinsically forbidden.
ممنوع لذاتہ (man'u li dhātihī): A prohibition intrinsic to the act itself; such an act is invalid and sinful.
عتاق ('itāq): Freeing a slave as a form of expiation for zihar.
صوم (ṣawm): Fasting for two consecutive months as expiation for zihar if one cannot free a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The feeding becomes invalid and must be restarted.
B) The feeding remains valid, and no restart is needed.
C) The expiation is nullified entirely, and a different form of expiation must be chosen.
D) The husband must add an additional feeding to compensate.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse during zihar feeding does not invalidate the feeding because the prohibition is external (man'u li ghayrihi), not intrinsic.

Intercourse During Zihar Feeding: Validity of Kaffarah
Ruling on validity of zihar feeding if intercourse occurs during process

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a prohibition due to an external reason does not invalidate the act, specifically in the context of zihar kaffarah feeding.

Core Idea
Feeding for zihar remains valid even if intercourse occurs during it; the prohibition is external, not intrinsic.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the kaffarah of zihar. If a man begins feeding sixty poor people but has intercourse with his wife before completing the feeding, does he need to restart? The Hanafi answer is no, based on the wording of the Quran and a crucial usul principle about the nature of prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being judged? (Feeding during zihar kaffarah). What is the ruling? (It remains valid even if intercourse occurs during the process; no restart required.)
The ruling is from al-Hidayah and is the relied-upon position.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? Quran 58:4 conditions feeding before intercourse only for emancipation and fasting, not for feeding itself.
The verse: '...fasting for two consecutive months before they touch'. It does not repeat the condition for feeding.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the ruling? The absence of the condition for feeding indicates that feeding's validity is not tied to prior abstinence.
This is a 'dalala zanni' (non-definitive indication) but sufficient for the ruling.
4
Note the principle
Why does the prohibition not invalidate? Because it is a prohibition due to an external reason (mamnu' li ghayrihi), not a condition of validity.
The Hanafi maxim: 'Al-man'u li ghayrihi la yunafi al-mashru'iyyah'.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require sequence in all kaffarah steps, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The practical difference: Hanafi allows continuation; others may require restart.

Source Text

If he approaches the woman from whom he made zihar during the feeding, he does not start anew because Allah Almighty did not stipulate that the feeding must occur before intercourse. However, he is prevented from intercourse before it because perhaps he becomes able to emancipate or fast, so they could occur after intercourse. And prohibition due to an external reason does not negate the validity in itself. Translation: And if during the feeding he has intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar, then he does not restart. Because Allah Almighty did not stipulate that feeding must be before intercourse, but he will be prevented from intercourse before feeding because sometimes he becomes able to emancipate or fast, so those two would occur after intercourse. And a prohibition due to an external reason does not negate the validity in itself. Explanation: The issue is that if the one performing the kaffarah of zihar had intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar during the feeding, then restarting the feeding is not necessary. The proof is that Allah Almighty stated the condition that feeding be before intercourse, just as in emancipation and fasting this condition is stated. However, it is necessary to prevent him from intercourse before feeding because it is possible that he becomes able to emancipate or fast before completing the feeding, so in that case if he had intercourse before or during the feeding, then emancipation or fasting would necessarily occur after intercourse, which is prohibited by the Quranic text. Therefore, it is better not to have intercourse before feeding. It is clear that intercourse before feeding is prohibited due to an external reason, and that which is prohibited due to an external reason does not contradict the validity in itself, so intercourse before or during feeding does not necessitate the invalidity of the feeding.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. It addresses whether a man who makes zihar (a form of pre-Islamic divorce-like oath) and begins the kaffarah of feeding sixty poor people must restart the feeding if he has intercourse with his wife during the process. The ruling is that he does not restart. The proof is that the Quranic condition (Surah Mujadila 58:4) requires feeding before intercourse only for emancipation and fasting; for feeding, no such condition is stated. However, it is prohibited to have intercourse before completing the kaffarah because the husband might later be unable to feed and need to switch to emancipation or fasting, which would then occur after intercourse—contradicting the Quranic condition. But this prohibition is due to an external reason, not affecting the validity of the feeding already given. Therefore, the feeding remains valid and no repetition is needed. This principle—that a prohibition due to an external reason does not negate the intrinsic validity of an act—is a key Hanafi legal maxim.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A husband saying to his wife 'You are to me like my mother's back,' making her forbidden to him until he performs kaffarah.
مسيس (masis): Sexual intercourse.
ممنوع لغیرہ (mamnu' li ghayrihi): Prohibited due to an external factor, not because the act itself is evil; such prohibition does not invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The feeding is invalid and must be repeated after intercourse.
C) He does not restart; the feeding remains valid.
D) He must also perform a separate kaffarah for intercourse.

Key Takeaway
The feeding for zihar kaffarah remains valid even if intercourse occurs during the process because the prohibition is external, not intrinsic to the act.

Two Zihar Expiations with Same Sixty Poor People
Intra-madhhab dispute on merging two zihar expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that a single feeding of sixty poor people discharges only one of two zihar expiations, and apply the principle that intention in a single genus is futile.

Core Idea
Intention in a single genus is futile; a single feeding discharges only one of two identical zihar expiations.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person who owes two zihar expiations (kaffarah). He feeds sixty poor people each one sa' of wheat—double the required half-sa' per person for one expiation. The question: does this single act discharge both expiations or only one? The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say only one; Imam Muhammad says both. Understanding their reasoning reveals key principles about intention and sufficiency in acts of expiation.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A man has two zihar expiations (same genus). He feeds sixty poor people, each one sa' of wheat. Each expiation requires feeding 60 poor people half a sa' each, so he gives double the required amount for one expiation.
2
Identify the dispute
The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that only one expiation is discharged. Imam Muhammad holds that both are discharged.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
Intention in a single genus is futile: he cannot intend two expiations of the same type separately. The act is sufficient for only one expiation because the minimum per poor person is half a sa'; giving more does not create a second expiation without separate intention or distinct payment.
They compare to a case where causes differ (e.g., zihar and breaking fast), where intention distinguishes and both are discharged.
4
Analyze Muhammad's reasoning
The total amount (60 sa') suffices for both expiations (each requires 30 sa'). The recipients are valid for both; thus both are discharged, by analogy with different causes or separate payments.
Muhammad also uses analogy: if the causes were different, there is consensus that both are discharged.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical outcome: According to the Sahibayn, the man still owes one expiation; according to Muhammad, he owes nothing. The later fatwa often prefers the Sahibayn's view for caution.

جائیں گے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گندم کی جو مقدار ادا کی گئی ہے وہ دونوں کفاروں کے لئے کافی ہے اس لئے کہ ہر ایک ظہار میں ہر ایک مسکین کے لئے نصف صاع واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس ہر ایک مسکین کو ایک ایک صاع گندم دینے میں یقیناً دونوں کفاروں کی کفایت ہو سکتی ہے اور جن کو دیا گیا ہے وہ دونوں کفاروں کا محل بھی ہیں اس لئے کہ فقیر احد الحقین لے کر مصرف ہونے سے خارج نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا دونوں کفارے ادا ہو جائیں گے۔ جیسے اگر کفارہ کا سبب مختلف ہو مثلاً ایک کفارہ افطار کا ہے اور ایک ظہار کا اور ساٹھ مسکینوں کو ایک ایک صاع گندم دیا ہے تو دونوں کفارے ادا ہو جائیں گے۔ یا جیسے متفرق کر کے دیا مثلا ایک مسکین کو پہلے ایک کفارہ میں نصف صاع دیا پھر نصف آخر دوسرے کفارے میں دے دیا تو بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک جنس میں نیت لغو ہوتی ہے کیوں کہ نیت اجناس مختلفہ کے درمیان امتیاز کرنے کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور جنس واحد میں یہ بات پائی نہیں جاتی اس وجہ سے ایک جنس میں نیت لغو ہوگی اور نیت دو جنسوں میں معتبر ہوتی ہے۔ مثلاً ایک شخص پر رمضان کے چند روزوں کی قضا واجب ہے پس اس نے قضا کے روزے کی نیت کی تو کافی ہو جائے گا اور اس پر تعین کی نیت واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ تمام روزوں کی جنس ایک ہے اور اگر کسی پر رمضان کی قضا اور نذر کی قضا واجب ہے تو یہ شخص تعیین نیت کا محتاج ہے کیونکہ دونوں روزوں کی جنس مختلف ہو گئی ہے۔ پس جب مسئلہ مذکورہ میں کفارہ دینے والے کی نیت لغو ہو گئی اور جو مقدار ادا کی گئی ہے وہ ایک کفارہ کی صلاحیت بھی رکھتی ہے کیونکہ آدھا صاع گندم سب سے کم مقدار ہے اور مقدار تو مانع نقصان تو ہوتی ہے مگر زیادتی کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتی حاصل یہ کہ ایک مسکین کو نصف صاع سے کم نہ دیا جائے البتہ زیادہ دیا جا سکتا ہے لہذا اس ادائیگی سے ایک کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا جیسے یہ شخص اصل کفارہ کی نیت کرتا تو بالاتفاق ایک کفارہ ادا ہوتا پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی۔
And if he fed for two zihars sixty poor people, each poor person one sa' of wheat, it does not suffice except for one of them according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said it suffices for both. And if he fed that for breaking fast and zihar, it suffices for both. For Muhammad: the performed act suffices for both, and the recipients are the place for both, so it occurs for both, just as if the cause differed or he paid separately. For the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): intention in a single genus is futile, and in two genera it is considered. When intention is futile, and the performed act suffices for one expiation because half a sa' is the minimum amount—it prevents deficiency but not excess—so it occurs for one, as if he intended the original expiation, unlike if he paid separately because in the second payment it is in the status of another poor person. Translation and detailed commentary follow...
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who has two zihar expiations (kaffarahs) and feeds sixty poor people each one sa' of wheat—this is double the required amount per person (since each expiation requires half a sa' per poor person). The question: does this single feeding discharge both expiations or only one? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) hold that it discharges only one expiation. Their reasoning: when the cause (the kaffarah) is of the same type (both zihar), the intention cannot differentiate between them; the payment is effectively for one kaffarah because the minimum per person is half a sa', and giving more does not count as separate payments. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it discharges both expiations. His reasoning: the total amount given suffices for both (each poor person receives one sa', which covers both the half-sa' obligations from each expiation), and the recipients are valid recipients for both. He analogizes to cases where the causes are different (e.g., fasting expiation and zihar expiation)—in that case, it discharges both by consensus—or if the payments are made separately to the same poor person over two times. The text also notes that the Sahibayn's position relies on the principle that intention in a single genus is futile; if you intend two obligations of the same type, the act counts for only one, whereas if the obligations are of different types, intention distinguishes and both are discharged. This is illustrated with the example of qada (make-up) fasts: if only Ramadan qada is owed, no specific intention needed; but if both Ramadan qada and nazr (vow) qada are owed, specific intention is required because they are different genera.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship or expiation.
جنس (jins): Genus or category of an obligation. Multiple expiations of the same type (e.g., both zihar) are same jins; different types (zihar and iftar) are different ajnas.
نصف صاع (nisf sa'): Half a sa', the minimum amount of wheat to be given to each poor person in zihar expiation. One sa' is approximately 2.5-3 kg.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, if a man has two zihar expiations and feeds sixty poor people one sa' each (instead of half a sa' each for one expiation), how many expiations are discharged?
A) Both expiations are discharged.
B) Only one expiation is discharged.
C) None, because he must feed exactly half a sa' each.
D) He must feed 120 poor people.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when two obligations of the same genus are merged in a single act without distinct intention or separate payments, only one obligation is considered fulfilled, even if the quantity is sufficient for both.

Multiple Zihar Expiations: Intention and Species in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on multiple zihar expiations with single or multiple acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention of specification (niyyat al-ta'yin) is not required when discharging multiple expiations of the same species, and identify when it is required for different species.

Core Idea
If the species of expiation is the same, intention is not needed; if different, it is required.

This lesson explores a nuanced Hanafi dispute concerning multiple zihar expiations. The core issue is whether a person who owes multiple kaffarat of the same type can discharge them with a single sufficient act without specifying which is which. The Hanafi school, led by Imam Muhammad, holds that no intention of specification is needed when the species (jins) is the same, because the act applies automatically. However, when the species differ, such as between zihar and qatl, intention becomes necessary. We will examine the reasoning behind this position and contrast it with the views of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and ruling
Read the passage starting from 'ومن وجبت عليه كفارتا ظهار' and identify the scenario: a person owes two zihar expiations. Note the ruling: if he frees two slaves without specific intention, it suffices for both. Also note the parallel cases: fasting 4 months or feeding 120 poor.
Focus on the condition that the act must be complete per kaffarah.
2
Understand the principle behind the ruling
The passage states 'لأن الجنس متحد فلا حاجة إلى نية معينة' – because the species is one, no specific intention is needed. Explain in your own words what 'species' means: the type of expiation based on its cause (both are zihar kaffarat). Contrast this with the case of mixed species (zihar and qatl) where intention is required.
The species determines the need for specification.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Identify the difference between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn regarding feeding 60 poor. The Shaykhayn hold that when feeding 60 poor with one sa' each, only one kaffarah is discharged because the quantity suffices for only one. Understand why – the act must be sufficient per kaffarah.
This is a subtle point: the ruling depends on whether the act is sufficient in quantity per kaffarah.
4
Examine the external objections
The passage mentions Zufar and al-Shafi'i. Zufar claims a single act cannot discharge two because it would be like freeing half a slave for each. Al-Shafi'i argues all expiations are one species due to unity of purpose. Understand the Hanafi response to each.
The Hanafi response relies on species distinction and analogy with qada and nadhr.
5
Apply the principle to the analogy
The passage provides two analogies: (1) fasting one day for two qada days suffices for one; (2) fasting for qada and nadhr requires specification. Relate these to the principle: same species (both qada) vs different species (qada vs nadhr).
The analogy demonstrates that the need for specification depends on species, not on the number of obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن وجبت عليه كفارتا ظهار فاعتق رقبتين لا ينوى عن احدهما بعينها جاز عنهما وكذا اذا صام اربعة اشهر او اطعم مائة وعشرين مسكينا جاز لأن الجنس متحد فلا حاجة الى نية معينة وان اعتق عنهما رقبة واحدة أو صام شهرين كان له ان يجعل ذلك عن ايهما شاء وان اعتق عن ظهار وقتل لم يجز عن واحد منهما وقال زفر لا يجزيه عن احدهما فى الفصلين وقال الشافعى له ان يجعل ذلك عن احدهما في الفصلين لان الكفارات كلها باعتبار اتحاد المقصود جنس واحد وجه قول زفر انه اعتق عن كل ظهار نصف العبد وليس له ان يجعل عن احدهما بعد ما اعتق عنهما لخروج الأمر من يده ولنا ان نية التعيين فى الجنس المتحد غير مفيد فتلغو و فى الجنس المختلف مفيد و اختلاف الجنس في الحكم و هو الكفارة ههنا باختلاف السبب نظير الاول اذا صام يوما في قضاء رمضان عن يومين يجزيه عن قضاء يوم واحد ونظير الثانى اذا كان عليه صوم القضاء والنذر فانه لا بد فيه من التمييز والله اعلم
And whoever owes two expiations for zihar and frees two slaves without intending which one specifically, it suffices for both. Similarly, if he fasts four months or feeds one hundred and twenty poor people, it suffices because the species is one, so there is no need for a specific intention. And if he frees one slave for them (i.e., for both) or fasts two months, he has the option to assign that to whichever he wishes. And if he frees (a slave) for zihar and for murder, it does not suffice for either. Zufar said: it does not suffice for either in the two cases. Al-Shafi'i said: he has the option to assign it to either in the two cases, because all expiations, considering the unity of the intended purpose, are of one species. The proof of Zufar's statement: he freed half a slave for each zihar, and he does not have the option to assign it to one after having freed for both, because the matter has left his hand. And our proof: intention of specification in a single species is not beneficial, so it is invalid, and in different species it is beneficial. The difference in species in the ruling—and it is the expiation here—is due to the difference in cause. The analogy of the first: if he fasts one day for two days of qada of Ramadan, it suffices for one day of qada. And the analogy of the second: if he owes fasting of qada and nadhr, then he must distinguish. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah presents a complex intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the necessity of specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) in discharging multiple kaffarat (expiation for zihar). The passage begins with the core ruling: a person who owes two zihar expiations and frees two slaves without specifying which slave is for which expiation—both expiations are discharged. Similarly, fasting four months or feeding 120 poor people, without specific intention, suffices for both because the jins (species) of the expiation is the same. However, if a person performs a lesser act—freeing only one slave or fasting only two months—he may choose which of the two expiations it applies to. This is the position of Imam Muhammad. The passage then contrasts with a different scenario: if the person owes expiations for two different reasons (zihar and qatl/murder) and performs a single act, it does not suffice for either. The commentator then records the opinions of Zufar (who says in both scenarios regardless of species, a single act suffices for none) and al-Shafi'i (who allows the person to assign it to any one, arguing all kaffarat share a single purpose). The Hanafi response is that in a single species (jins muttahid), intention of specification is useless because the act is inherently applicable to all; in different species (jins mukhtalif), intention is necessary for validity. This is proven by an analogy: if someone owes two days of qada of Ramadan (same species: both qada) and fasts one day, it counts for one day without specifying which (the first analogy). But if someone owes both qada of Ramadan and a vow (nadhr) (different species), then specification is mandatory (the second analogy). The passage thus establishes that the need for specific intention depends on the unity or diversity of the species of the expiation, not on the difference in causes alone.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiation or atonement required for certain sins or invalid acts, such as zihar, breaking an oath, or accidental killing. In this passage, it refers specifically to the expiation for zihar.
ظهار (zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a husband says to his wife 'you are like my mother's back.' It is considered sinful and requires expiation before the husband can return to his wife.
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): The intention to specify which particular expiation (e.g., which zihar or which cause) the act applies to.
جنس (jins): Legally, the category or type of an obligation based on its cause and ruling. In this context, 'same species' means the type of expiation (e.g., both are kaffarat for zihar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person owes two zihar expiations and frees two slaves without specifying which slave is for which expiation, what is the Hanafi ruling according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Only one expiation is discharged, and he must specify for the other.
B) Both expiations are discharged.
C) Neither expiation is discharged until he specifies.
D) He may choose which expiation to apply the slaves to.

Key Takeaway
The need for intention of specification in expiations depends on whether the species (jins) is the same; if the same, no intention needed; if different, intention is required.

Ruling on Multiple Kaffarah: Same vs Different Genus
Dispute over single expiation act for multiple kaffarat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on fulfilling multiple kaffarah with a single act of expiation, and evaluate the opposing views of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i.

Core Idea
When two expiations share a genus, a single act suffices for one; when they differ, intention is needed and the act fails.

This passage addresses a practical and legally important question: if a person owes two expiations (kaffarat) and performs a single act of expiation, such as freeing one slave, does that fulfill one, both, or neither of the obligations? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on whether the expiations are of the same genus (jins wahid) or different genera (jins mukhtalif). This ruling illustrates key principles of intention (niyyah) and legal causation (sabab) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling for both scenarios: same genus and different genus. Note that within the same genus, intention to specify is not effective, so the act is valid for one at the doer's discretion. For different genera, intention is required; without it, the act is invalid for both.
2
Identify the opposing views
Recognize that Imam Zufar holds the act is invalid for both in all cases, while Imam Shafi'i allows the doer to choose which expiation is fulfilled in both cases.
Imam Zufar is a Hanafi scholar who differed from Abu Hanifa on this point.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the reasoning of each school. The Hanafi proof hinges on the principle that intention within the same genus is ineffective, making the act automatically assigned to one expiation. For different genera, intention is necessary because the acts are distinct.
The Hanafi response to Zufar is that within the same genus, freeing is not split. To Shafi'i, the genus differs because the causes differ.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: the real-world difference in ruling. For example, if a man owes two zihar expiations and frees one slave, the Hanafi school says it counts for one, Zufar says none, Shafi'i says he can choose which one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بات الظهار 
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم اختلاف سے ہے اول کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ (ایک شخص ) نے دو دن قضاء رمضان کی طرف سے ایک دن روزہ رکھا۔ تو یہ ایک دن کی قضاء سے کافی ہوگا اور ثانی کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ جب اس پر قضاء اور نذر کا روزہ ہو تو اس میں تمیز دینا ضروری ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب تشریح عبادت میں مسئلہ کی دو صورتیں زیر بحث ہیں ایک یہ کہ ایک شخص پر ظہار کے دو کفارے واجب ہیں اس نے دونوں کی طرف سے ایک غلام آزاد کیا یا دوماہ کے پے در پے روزے رکھے تو اس شخص کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہے کہ ان دونوں کفاروں میں سے جس ایک کی طرف سے چاہے مقرر کر دے دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اس پر ایک ظہار کا کفارہ واجب ہے اور ایک قتل کا پھر اس نے ایک غلام آزاد کیا تو اس صورت میں دونوں کفاروں میں سے کوئی ادا نہیں ہوگا یہ حکم ہمارے نزدیک ہے اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں کسی ایک کی طرف سے ادا نہیں ہوگا اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں اس کو اختیار ہے جس کے لئے چاہے قرار دیدے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تمام کفارات کا مقصود ایک ہے یعنی ستر اور اس گناہ کے اثر کو زائل کرنا۔ لہذا تمام کفارات کی جنس بھی ایک ہے اور جنس واحد میں نیت غیر مفید ہے اس وجہ سے اصل کفارہ کی نیت باقی رہی اور یہ شخص اگر اصل کفارہ کی نیت کرتا تو اس کو ان دونوں کفاروں میں سے ایک کے لئے مقرر کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی دونوں کفاروں میں سے جس ایک کے لیے چاہے مقرر کر دے۔
اور امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے دونوں کفاروں میں سے ہر ایک کی طرف سے آدھا غلام آزاد کیا ہے اور کفارے میں آدھا غلام آزاد کر نا صحیح نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ آزاد کر نا تبرع شمار ہوگا اور چونکہ دونوں کفاروں کی طرف سے آزاد کرنے کے بعد اس کے ہاتھ سے معاملہ بھی نکل گیا اس وجہ سے کسی ایک کے واسطے مقرر کرنے کا بھی اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔
اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد میں متعین کرنے کی نیت کرنا غیر مقید ہے لہذا نیت لغو ہوگی اور جب نیت لغو ہوگئی تو ایسا ہو گیا کردیا اس نے ظہار کے دو کفاروں میں ایک غلام آزاد اور دونوں کی طرف سے نیت نہیں کی ہے تو یہ جائز ہے اور اس کو اختیار ہے کہ دونوں ظہار میں سے جس کی طرف چاہے پھیر دے پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی جائز ہوگا۔
اور اگر دو کفارے مختلف الا جناس ہیں تو ان میں متعین کرنے کی نیت مفید ہوتی ہے لہذا معتبر ہوگی۔ پس جب اس شخص نے کفار قبل اور کفارہ ظہار میں بالا رادہ ایک غلام آزاد کیا ہے تو یہ غلام کسی ایک طرف سے آزاد نہیں ہو گا۔ و اختلاف الجنس سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ قتل اور ظہار دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے۔ یعنی کفارہ بالا عتاق ۔ پس جب دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے تو یہ دونوں مختلف الا جناس کیسے ہوں گے ۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ حکم یعنی کفارے میں جنس کا مختلف ہونا سبب کے اختلاف سے ہے۔ اسلئے کہ قتل یقیناً ظہارت مختلف ہے اور اختلاف سبب دلالت کرتا ہے اختلاف حکم پر کیونکہ حکم ملزوم ہوتا ہے اور سبب لازم اور اختلاف لوازم دلالت کرتا ہے ملزومات کے اختلاف پر۔ پس دوسرے مسئلہ میں جب جنس مختلف ہو گئی تو اس کی نیت درست ہوئی اور جب نیت درست ہوئی تو ایک غلام آزاد کرنا مختلف دو کفاروں کی طرف سے ہوگا پس ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے آدھا غلام ہوگا اور یہ جائز نہیں کیونکہ ایک کفارہ میں ایک غلام آزاد ہوتا ہے نہ کہ آدھا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے جنس واحد اور جنس مختلف دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی نظیر بیان کی ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ جنس واحد کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ جب کسی نے رمضان کی قضاء کے دوروزوں کی طرف سے ایک دن روزہ رکھا تو اس سے ایک روزہ کی قضاء صحیح ہو جائے گی اور جنس مختلف کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ جب کسی شخص پر ایک روزہ قضا کا واجب ہو اور ایک روزہ نذر کا تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو متعین کرے تا کہ دونوں روزں کے درمیان امتیاز ہو جائے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Explanation of Zihar. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Five. The difference is: first example: (a person) fasted one day for two days of Ramadan make-up. So that will suffice for one day's make-up. Second example: when he owes a make-up fast and a vow fast, then distinguishing between them is necessary. And Allah knows best. Commentary: In worship, two scenarios are under discussion: one is that a person owes two expiations for zihar, so he freed one slave or fasted two consecutive months for both. Then this person has the option to assign it to whichever of the two expiations he wishes. The second scenario is that he owes one expiation for zihar and one for killing, then he freed one slave. Then in this case, neither expiation is fulfilled. This is our ruling. Imam Zufar says that in both cases, neither is fulfilled. Imam Shafi'i says that in both cases, he has the option to assign it to whichever he wishes. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the purpose of all expiations is one, i.e., covering and removing the effect of sin. Hence the genus of all expiations is one, and intention is not effective within a single genus. Therefore the intention of the original expiation remains, and if this person intended the original expiation, he would have the option to assign it to one of the two expiations. Similarly here, he may assign it to whichever of the two expiations he wishes. Imam Zufar's proof is that this person freed half a slave for each of the two expiations, and freeing half a slave in expiation is not valid. Therefore this freeing is considered a gift, and since after freeing for both expiations the matter is out of his hands, he has no option to assign it to one. Our proof is that intending to specify within a single genus is unqualified, so the intention is irrelevant. When the intention is irrelevant, it is as if he freed one slave for the two zihar expiations and did not intend either. Then it is permissible, and he has the option to assign it to whichever of the two zihar he wishes. Similarly here, it will be permissible. If the two expiations are of different genera, then intending to specify is beneficial and thus valid. So when this person freed one slave for the expiation of killing and the expiation of zihar without specification, then this slave is not freed on behalf of either. This is the answer to the question about difference of genus. The question: the ruling of killing and zihar is the same, i.e., expiation by freeing a slave. So when the ruling is the same, how are they different in genus? The answer: the genus in the ruling (i.e., expiation) differs due to the difference of cause. Because killing is definitely different from zihar, and difference in cause indicates difference in ruling since the ruling is the consequent and the cause is the necessary condition. Difference in necessary conditions indicates difference in consequents. So in the second issue, when the genus differed, his intention was correct, and when the intention was correct, freeing one slave will be on behalf of two different expiations, so each will get half a slave, and that is not permissible because one expiation requires one slave, not half. The author of Hidayah gave an example of each of the single genus and different genus. Thus he said: the example of single genus is when someone fasted one day for two days of Ramadan make-up, then that will suffice for one day's make-up. The example of different genus is when a person owes one make-up fast and one vow fast, then it is obligatory for him to specify one of them so that distinction is made between the two fasts. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of a single act of expiation (kaffarah) when multiple expiations are due. It presents three positions: the Hanafi school, Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar), and Imam Shafi'i. The Hanafi position distinguishes between expiations of the same genus (jins wahid) and different genera (jins mukhtalif). If two expiations are of the same genus (e.g., both for zihar), performing one act (e.g., freeing one slave) suffices for one of them at the person's choice, because intention within a single genus is not effective for specification. But if they are of different genera (e.g., one for zihar and one for killing), the act does not fulfill either because intention is necessary to specify, and without specification the act is divided between both, rendering it invalid (half a slave for each). Imam Zufar holds that even for same genus, the act is divided between both and valid for neither. Imam Shafi'i holds that in both cases the person may choose which one to fulfill. The passage then provides reasoning: Shafi'i argues all expiations share the same purpose, hence same genus; Zufar argues that freeing without specification implies freeing half for each, which is invalid; the Hanafis argue that within same genus, specification is not required, so the act is valid for one at the person's discretion. The author then gives examples from fasting to illustrate the principle. This is a classic Hanafi usul al-fiqh application of the rule that intention (niyyah) is only required to distinguish acts of different legal categories (jins), not within the same category.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A form of divorce in which a husband says to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' which makes her unlawful to him until expiation.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for certain sins or violations, such as in zihar, breaking an oath, or accidental killing, usually by freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding the poor.
جنس واحد (jins wahid): Same genus or category, meaning expiations that are of the same type (e.g., both for zihar).
جنس مختلف (jins mukhtalif): Different genus, meaning expiations arising from different causes (e.g., zihar and killing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person owes two zihar expiations and frees one slave without specifying intention, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The act is invalid for both.
B) It is valid for one of them at his choice.
C) It is valid for both simultaneously.
D) It becomes a voluntary act (tatawwu').

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between expiations of the same genus and different genera: within the same genus, a single act suffices for one at the doer's choice; across different genera, intention is required and without it the act is invalid for both.

Li'an: Definition, Pillar, Cause, Condition, and Ruling
Defines li'an and lists its cause, condition, and ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define li'an, identify its pillar, cause, condition, and ruling, and explain the Hanafi requirement of eligibility for testimony (ahl al-shahada) compared to the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Li'an is a procedure of mutual oaths replacing hadd; its pillar is testimony emphasized by oath.

In this lesson, we explore the chapter on li'an—a unique procedure in Islamic law that allows a husband to accuse his wife of adultery or deny paternity without having to produce witnesses, avoiding the hadd punishment for false accusation. The passage defines li'an linguistically and legally, explains its components, and highlights the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on who may perform it.

Guided Path
1
Define li'an linguistically and technically
Understand why the whole procedure is named after the curse (la'n) despite including wrath (ghadab). The term is of the category 'naming the whole after a part'.
Linguistically li'an means curse/driving away; technically it is the four testimonies, curse, and wrath exchanged between spouses.
2
Identify the components of li'an: pillar, cause, condition, ruling
The pillar (rukn) is testimony emphasized by oath (shahadah mu'akkadah bil-yamin). The cause (sabab) is the husband's accusation that would necessitate hadd (qadhf). The condition (shart) is a valid marriage. The ruling (hukm) is that after li'an, intercourse becomes haram permanently.
These are the four structural elements of li'an as per the passage.
3
Understand the Hanafi qualification: ahl al-shahada
Hanafis require both spouses to be eligible to give testimony (ahl al-shahada), i.e., free, Muslim, just (adil). This is because the pillar of li'an is testimony (shahadah).
The Shafi'i condition is eligibility for oath (ahl al-yamin).
4
Compare with Shafi'i: ahl al-yamin
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the pillar is the oath (yamin) itself, so the person must be qualified to take an oath. This leads to practical differences in who can perform li'an.
The difference stems from analyzing the Quranic verse (24:6).

باب اللعان
ترجمہ ( یہ ) باب احکام لعان کے بیان میں ) ہے
تشریح .. لعان، مفاعلت کا مصدر ہے ، لغوی معنی ہیں دھتکارنا اور رحمت سے دور کرنا اور شریعت میں لعان ان چار شہادتوں اور لعن اور غضب کو کہتے ہیں جو میاں بیوی کے درمیان جاری ہوں اور مجموعہ کا نام لعان اس وجہ سے رکھا گیا کہ اس میں لعن مذکور ہوتا ہے جیسے رکوع پر مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے نماز کا نام رکوع رکھ دیا گیا اور تشہد پر مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے التحیات کا نام تشہد رکھ دیا گیا ہے پس لعان کا نام رکھنا تسمیۃ الکل باسم الجزء کے قبیل سے ہوگا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ لعان نام کیوں رکھا جب کہ اس میں غضب بھی مذکور ہوتا ہے۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لعن مرد کی جانب سے ہوتا ہے اور مخضب عورت کی جانب سے اور ظاہر ہے کہ جو چیز مرد کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتی ہے وہ مقدم ہوتی ہے اس لئے نام رکھنے میں لعن کو ترجیح دی گئی نہ کہ غضب کو ۔ اور لعان کا رکن شہادت موکدہ بالیمین ہے اور اس کا سب مرد کا اپنی بیوی کو ایسی تہمت لگا نا جوا جانب میں موجب حد ہو اور اس کی شرط قیام نکاح ہے اور اس کا حکم لعان سے فارغ ہوتے ہی وطی اور استمتاع کا حرام ہونا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک لعان کا اہل وہ ہے جو شہادت کا اہل ہو اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک وہ ہے جو یمین کا اہل ہو۔
لعان کا موجب ، لعان کی تعریف
قال اذاقذف الرجل امرأته بالزناء وهما من اهل الشهادة و المرأة ممن يحد قاذفها اونفى نسب ولدها وطالبته بموجب القذف فعليه اللعان والاصل ان اللعان عند ناشهادات مؤكدات بالايمان مقرونة باللعن قائمة مقام حد القذف فى حقه و مقام حد الزناء فى حقها لقوله تعالى و لم يكن لهم شهداء الا انفسهم و الاستثناً انما يكون من الجنس وقال الله تعالى فشهادة احدهم اربع شهادات بالله نص على الشهادة واليمين فقلنا الركن هو الشهادة المؤكدة باليمين ثم قرن الركن فى جانبه باللعن لو كان كاذبا وهو قائم مقام حد القذف وفي جانبها با لغضب وهو قا ئم مقام حد الزناء اذا ثبت هذا نقول لا بد ان يكونا من اهل الشهادة لان الركن فيه الشهادة ولابد ان تكون هى ممن يحد قاذفها لانه قائم فى حقه مقام حد القذف فلا بد من احصانها ويجب بنفى الولد لانه لمانفى ولدها صار قاذفا لها ظاهرا ولا يعتبر احتمال ان يكون الولد من غیره بالوطى من شبهة كما اذا نفى اجنبى نسبه عن ابيه المعروف وهذا لان الاصل في النسب الفراش
Chapter of Li'an. Translation: This chapter is about the rulings of li'an. Commentary: Li'an is a verbal noun from mufa'ala. Its lexical meaning is to curse and drive away from mercy. In Sharia, li'an refers to the four testimonies, curse, and wrath that occur between husband and wife. The whole set is called li'an because it includes the curse (la'n), just as prayer is named ruku' because it includes ruku', and al-Tahiyyat is named tashahhud because it includes tashahhud. So naming li'an is of the category of naming the whole after a part. As for why it is named li'an when it also includes wrath (ghadab), the answer is that the curse comes from the husband and the wrath from the wife, and what pertains to the husband is given precedence. So in naming, la'n is preferred over ghadab. The pillar (rukn) of li'an is testimony emphasized by oath (shahadah mu'akkadah bil-yamin). Its cause (sabab) is the husband accusing his wife of something that would necessitate hadd punishment. Its condition (shart) is the existence of marriage. Its ruling is that after completing li'an, intercourse and enjoyment become forbidden. In our view, the person qualified for li'an is one who is qualified to give testimony (shahadah). According to Imam Shafi'i, it is one qualified to take an oath (yamin). The requirement for li'an, the definition of li'an. He said: When a man accuses his wife of adultery and both are qualified to give testimony, and the woman is one whose accuser would be subject to hadd, or he denies the paternity of her child and she demands the consequence of the accusation, then li'an is required. The basis is that li'an consists of four testimonies emphasized by oaths, accompanied by curses, standing in the place of hadd for qadhf (false accusation) against him and in the place of hadd for zina against her, due to the verse: 'And they have no witnesses except themselves' (Quran 24:6). The exception (istithna') must be from the same genus. And Allah said: 'For the testimony of one of them is four testimonies by Allah' (Quran 24:6) – this explicitly mentions testimony and oath. So we say the pillar is testimony emphasized by oath. Then he attached the curse to his side if he is lying, which stands in place of hadd for qadhf, and on her side the wrath, which stands in place of hadd for zina. Once this is established, we say: They must be qualified to give testimony because the pillar is testimony. And she must be one whose accuser would be subject to hadd, because it stands in place of hadd for qadhf against him, so she must be muhsanah (free, Muslim, chaste, etc.). And it is obligatory due to denial of the child, because by denying her child, he effectively accuses her of zina outwardly. The possibility that the child might be from someone else due to sexual intercourse under a doubtful contract (shubhah) is not considered, just as if a stranger denies the lineage of a child from his known father. This is because the basis for lineage is the marital bed (firash).
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on li'an (mutual cursing) in Islamic law. It begins with a linguistic definition: li'an comes from the root la'n (curse). In Sharia, it is a specific procedure involving four testimonies, a curse, and a wrath, performed by spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity. The author explains that the term 'li'an' is used for the whole process even though it contains elements like ghadab (wrath), because the curse (from the husband) is considered primary. The pillar (rukn) of li'an is testimony emphasized by an oath (shahadah mu'akkadah bil-yamin). The cause (sabab) is the husband's accusation that would normally subject him to hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf). The condition (shart) is a valid marriage. The ruling is that after li'an, the couple becomes haram to each other permanently. There is a difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is: Hanafis require both spouses to be eligible to give testimony (ahl al-shahada), i.e., they must be free, Muslim, and just. Shafi'is require eligibility to take an oath (ahl al-yamin). The passage then cites Quranic verses (24:6-7) as proof, stating that the four testimonies stand in place of the hadd punishment for both parties. It also clarifies that the possibility of a child being born from a doubtful intercourse is not considered in denying paternity; the default principle is the marital bed (al-walad li'l-firash).

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): A legal procedure where a husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity, and both take oaths and curses to avoid hadd punishment.
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony or bearing witness, which in li'an takes the form of four oaths by Allah.
یمین (yamin): Oath, which in li'an is taken by the husband and wife to affirm the truth of their statements.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of adultery, which carries a hadd punishment of eighty lashes if unproven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on li'an according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Mubah
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a wajib procedure that substitutes for hadd when a husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity, and its validity depends on both spouses being qualified to give testimony (ahl al-shahada) according to the Hanafi school.

The Definition and Ruling of Li'an (Mutual Imprecation)
Defines Li'an, its Quranic proof, and the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Li'an, identify its proof from the Quran, and explain the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
Li'an is testimony strengthened by oaths, replacing hadd punishments for spouses.

The Quranic verse on Li'an was revealed after a Companion's dilemma. This lesson unpacks the nature of Li'an, its ruling, and the key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over whether it is primarily testimony or oaths.

Guided Path
1
Understand the cause of revelation
Review the narrations from Ibn Mas'ud and Hilal ibn Umayyah to see why the Li'an verse was revealed: a husband finds another man with his wife but lacks witnesses.
The original ruling of hadd for qadhf was abrogated for spouses by this verse.
2
Extract the Hanafi principle
From the verse, the Hanafis deduce that Li'an consists of testimonies (shahadat) strengthened by oaths, connected with the word 'la'n'.
The husband is made a witness by the exception 'except themselves'.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Examine verse 24:6-9: the phrase 'and they have no witnesses except themselves' establishes the husband as a witness, hence testimony is the pillar.
The combination of 'shahadah' and 'billah' indicates testimony plus oath.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i interprets 'shahadah' as oath, making Li'an essentially an exchange of oaths. This leads to different conditions: Hanafis require eligibility for testimony; Shafi'is require eligibility for oaths.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) affects who can perform Li'an.
