باب اللعان
وعبد اللہ بن مسعودؓ سے روایت ہے قال كنا جلو سافی المسجد ليلة الجمعة اذ دخل انصاری فقال يا رسول الله ارايتم الرجل يجد مع امراته رجلاً فان قتل قتلتموه وان تكلم جلد تموه و ان سكت، سكت على غيظ ثم قال اللهم أفتح فنزلت آية اللعان یعنی فرمایا ابن مسعودؓ نے کہ ہم شب جمعہ میں مسجد میں بیٹھے ہوئے تھے۔ اچانک ایک انصاری آیا اور کہنے لگا کہ اے اللہ کے رسول آپ کی کیا رائے ہے کہ ایک شخص اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ ایک (اجنبی ) آدمی کو پاتا ہے اگر وہ اس کو قتل کر دے تو آپ حضرات اس کو قتل کر دیں گے اور اگر وہ کچھ بولے آپ حضرات اس کو کوڑے لگاتے ہیں اور اگر وہ خاموش رہے تو اس کو خون کے گھونٹ پینے پڑتے ہیں ۔ پھر اس نے کہا ۔ ائے میرے خدا تو (اس معاملہ ) کوکھول دے۔ پس آیت لعان نازل ہوئی۔ اور ایک مرتبہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ہلال بن امیہ سے کہا جب کہ اس نے اپنی بیوی کو شریک بن شما ء کے ساتھ زنا کی تہمت لگادی تھی تم اپنی بات کی صداقت پر چار گواہ پیش کرو۔ ورنہ تمھاری پیٹھ پر کوڑے مارے جائیں گے ۔ صحابہ نے کہا کہ اب ہلال بن امیہ کوکوڑے مارے جائیں گے اور اس کی شہادت مسلمانوں میں باطل ہو جائے گی۔ (عنایه )
اس آیت اور دونوں روایت سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ موجب قذف حد قذف تھی مگر آیت لعان سے یہ حکم منسوخ ہو گیا ۔ پھر ہم نے آیت لعان میں غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ ہمارے نزدیک لعان میں اصل یہ ہے کہ گواہیاں قسموں کے ساتھ مؤکد کی گئیں ہوں اور لفظ لعن کے ساتھ مقترن ہوں اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک لعان وہ قسمیں ہیں جو لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ موکد ہوں ۔ پس ہمارے نزدیک لعان کا اہل وہ شخص ہوگا ، جو شہادت کا اہل ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک لعان کا وہ اہل ہے جو یمین کا اہل ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ لعان شو ہر کے حق میں حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اس کی بیوی کے حق میں حد زنا کے قائم مقام ہے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ والذين يرمون ازواجهم ولم يكن لهم شهداء الا نفسهم فشهادة احدهم اربع شهادات بالله انه لمن الصادقين والخامسة ان لعنت الله عليه ان كان من الكذبين ويدرؤ اعنها العذاب ان تشهد أربع شهادات بالله انه لمن الكذبين والخامسة ان غضب الله عليها ان كان من الصادقين - یعنی جو لوگ اپنی (منکوحہ بیویوں کو ( زنا) کی تہمت لگائیں اور ان کے پاس بجز اپنے دعوی کے اور کوئی گواہ نہ ہوں ۔ ( جن کو عدد میں چار ہونا چاہیے ) تو ان کی شہادت (جو کہ دافع جبس یا حد قذف ہو ) یہی ہے کہ چار بار اللہ کی قسم کھا کر کہہ دے کہ بے شک میں سچا ہوں اور پانچویں بار یہ کہے کہ مجھ پر خدا کی لعنت ہو اگر میں جھوٹا ہوں اور اس کے بعد اس عورت سے پیز ائے جبس یا حد زنا) اس طرح مل سکتی ہے کہ وہ چار بار تم کھا کر کہے کہ بے شک یہ مرد جھوٹا ہے اور پانچویں بار یہ کہے کہ مجھ پر خدا کا غضب ہوا گر یہ سچا ہو۔ (بیان القرآن ) اس آیت سے استدلال اس طرح ہوگا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے شهداء سے ازواج کا استثناء فرمایا ہے پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ زوج شاہد ہے اس لئے استثناء میں اصل یہ ہے کہ مستی مستثنی منہ کا ہم جنس ہوتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ زوج شاہد ہے اور شاہد بغیر شہادت کے نہیں ہو سکتا اور اس مسئلہ میں شہادت نام ہے حکایت لعان کا ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ لعان وہ شہادتیں ہیں جو قسموں کے ساتھ مضبوط کی گئیں ہیں ۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک لعان و قسمیں ہیں جو لفظ شہادت کیسا تھ موکد کی گئی ہوں دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فشهادة احدهم اربع شهادات باللہ ہے۔ اس آیت میں قول باری باللہ یمین کے معنی میں محکم ہے اور شہادت بھی یمین کے معنی کا احتمال رکھی ہے کیونکہ اگر کسی نے اشھد کہا تو یہ یمین ہو گی۔ پس ہم نے محتمل کو محکم پر محمول کیا ہے لیکن احناف کی طرف سے جواب ہوگا کہ اس آیت میں شہادت اور یمین دونوں کی تصریح کی گئی ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ لعان کا رکن وہ شہادت ہے جو یمین کے ساتھ موکد کی گئی ہو۔ پھر شوہر کی جانب میں لعان کے رکن کو لفظ لعان کے ساتھ ملایا گیا ہے اگر شوہر اپنی قسم میں جھوٹا ہو اور یہ شوہر کے حق میں حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے اور عورت کی جانب میں لعان کے رکن یعنی شہادت کو لفظ غضب کے ساتھ ملایا ہے اور یہ عورت کے حق میں حد زنا کے قائم مقام ہے۔
-
رہی یہ بات کہ عورت کی شہادت کو لفظ لعن کے بجائے لفظ غضب کے ساتھ مقترن کیوں کیا گیا ہے۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عورتیں اپنے کلام میں بکثرت لعنت کا لفظ استعمال کرتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ حدیث میں مروی ہے کہ انھن یكثون اللعن ويكفرن العشير يعني عورتيں بکثرت لعنت کرتی ہیں اور اپنے شوہر کی نعمتوں کا کفران کرتی ہیں۔ پس بکثرت لعنت کرنے کی وجہ سے ان کی نظروں کی قباحت ہی جاتی رہی۔ اس لئے ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ لعنت کے اقدام پر جری ہو جائیں ۔ پس اس مصلحت کے پیش نظر عورت کی شہادت کولفظ غضب کے ساتھ ملایا گیا ہے تا کہ وہ جھوٹی قسم کا اقدام کرنے سے باز رہے۔ یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ شہادت (لعان) زوجین کے حق میں حد کے قائم مقام ہے پس سوال یہ ہے کہ شہادت اور حد کے درمیان مناسبت کیا ہے جس کی وجہ سے شہادت کو حد کے قائم مقام کیا گیا ہے۔ جواب ان دونوں میں مناسبت یہ ہے کہ جس طرح حدزا جبر اور معاصی سے روکنے والی ہے۔ اس طرح اللہ کی جھوٹی قسم کھلانا در انحالیکہ وہ لعنت پر مشتمل ہے یہ بھی زاجر ہے بایں طور کہ اس قسم اور شہادت کے سبب پر اقدام کرنے سے باز رہے گا۔ صاحب بدا یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب ضابطہ ثابت ہو چکا کہ ہمارے نزدیک لعان وہ شہادتیں ہیں جو قسموں کے ساتھ موکد کی گئیں ہیں۔ تو میاں بیوی دونوں کا شہادت کی لیاقت رکھنا ضروری ہے، اس لئے کہ لعان میں شہادت رکن ہے اور یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ عورت ایسی ہو جس کے تہمت لگانے والے کو حد ماری جاتی ہے کیونکہ احان شوہر کے حق میں حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے عورت کا محصنہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کر دینے سے بھی لعان واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جب شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کے بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کی اور کہا کہ یہ بچہ میرے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے تو یہ اس عورت کو تہمت لگانے والا ہو گیا۔ جیسے کسی اجنبی نے بچہ کے معروف باپ سے اس کے نسب کی نفی کی تو یہ اجنبی عورت کو تہمت لگانے والا شمار ہو گا اسی طرح یہاں بھی۔
ولا يعتبر احتمال سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر اپنی بیوی کے والد کی نفی کر دے تو اس سے لعان واجب نہ ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ یہ بچہ اس کا بیٹا نہ ہو اور اس کی بیوی زانیہ بھی نہ ہو اس طرح پر کہ اس کے ساتھ ولی بالشبہ کی گئی ہو۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ شبہ معتبر نہیں ہے۔ کیوں کہ اس بات پر اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے کہ اگر کسی اجنبی نے کسی بچہ کی اس کے مشہور باپ سے نفی کی ہے تو یہ اجنبی شخص قاذف ( تہمت لگانے والا) ہوگا ۔ اگر چہ وہ احتمال یہاں بھی موجود ہے۔
Chapter of Li'an. And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: We were sitting in the mosque on Friday night when an Ansari entered and said: O Messenger of Allah, what is your opinion regarding a man who finds a (strange) man with his wife? If he kills him, you kill him; if he speaks, you flog him; and if he remains silent, he drinks a cup of anger. Then he said: O Allah, open (this matter). So the verse of Li'an was revealed. That is, Ibn Mas'ud said: We were sitting in the mosque on Friday night. Suddenly an Ansari came and said: O Messenger of Allah, what is your opinion? A man finds a (strange) man with his wife; if he kills him, you will kill him; if he says something, you will flog him; and if he remains silent, he must drink the cup of blood. Then he said: O my Lord, open this matter. So the verse of Li'an was revealed. And once the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Hilal ibn Umayyah when he accused his wife of zina with Sharik ibn Samha': Bring four witnesses to the truth of your statement, otherwise your back will be flogged. The Companions said: Now Hilal ibn Umayyah will be flogged and his testimony among the Muslims will be invalid. (From Inayah) From this verse and the two narrations it is established that the cause of qadhf was the hadd of qadhf, but this ruling was abrogated by the verse of Li'an. Then we pondered over the verse of Li'an and learned that according to us the principle in Li'an is that testimonies are strengthened with oaths and are connected with the word 'la'n'. And according to Imam Shafi'i, Li'an are oaths that are strengthened with the word 'shahadah'. Therefore, in our view, the person eligible for Li'an is one who is eligible for testimony, and according to Imam Shafi'i, the one eligible for Li'an is one who is eligible for oath. The summary is that Li'an takes the place of hadd of qadhf for the husband and takes the place of hadd of zina for the wife. The proof is that Allah Most High said: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves, then the testimony of one of them is four testimonies by Allah that he is among the truthful, and the fifth that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars. And it will avert the punishment from her if she testifies four testimonies by Allah that he is among the liars, and the fifth that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful.' That is, those people who accuse their (married) wives (of zina) and have no witnesses except their own claim (which must be four in number), then their testimony (which is a deterrent against punishment or hadd of qadhf) is that they swear by Allah four times saying: 'Indeed I am truthful', and the fifth time say: 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am a liar.' After that, the woman can avert punishment (or hadd of zina) by swearing four times saying: 'Indeed this man is a liar', and the fifth time say: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is truthful.' (Bayan al-Qur'an) The inference from this verse is that Allah Most High excepted wives from witnesses, so it is established that the husband is a witness because the principle in exception is that the excepted thing is of the same kind as that from which it is excepted. The conclusion is that the husband is a witness, and a witness cannot be without testimony, and in this matter testimony means the recitation of Li'an. So it is established that Li'an are testimonies that are strengthened with oaths. And according to Imam Shafi'i, Li'an are oaths that are strengthened with the word testimony. His proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'the testimony of one of them is four testimonies by Allah.' In this verse, the saying of Allah 'by Allah' is decisive in the meaning of oath, and testimony also has the possibility of meaning oath, because if someone says 'ashhadu' it will be an oath. So we have carried the probable (testimony) on the decisive (oath). But from the Hanafis the answer is that in this verse both testimony and oath are explicitly mentioned, so we say that the pillar of Li'an is testimony that is strengthened with an oath. Then on the husband's side, the pillar of Li'an is connected with the word 'curse'; if the husband is lying in his oath, it takes the place of hadd of qadhf for the husband. And on the wife's side, the pillar of Li'an (i.e. testimony) is connected with the word 'wrath', and it takes the place of hadd of zina for the wife. As for why the wife's testimony is connected with the word 'wrath' instead of the word 'curse', the answer is that women frequently use the word curse in their speech. As narrated in hadith: 'They frequently curse and are ungrateful to their spouses.' That is, women curse a lot and are ungrateful for their husbands' favors. So due to their frequent cursing, the repulsiveness of cursing has disappeared from their eyes. Therefore it is possible that they may become bold in pronouncing curses. So for this wisdom, the woman's testimony is connected with the word 'wrath' so that she refrains from embarking on a false oath. Here there is a question: You said that testimony (of Li'an) takes the place of hadd for the spouses. So the question is: What is the connection between testimony and hadd that testimony is made a substitute for hadd? The answer: The connection between them is that just as hadd prevents (sin and transgression), similarly, swearing a false oath by Allah while it contains cursing is also a deterrent, because one will refrain from proceeding due to the fear of this oath and testimony. The author of Bada'i' says: When it is established as a principle that according to us Li'an are testimonies strengthened with oaths, then it is necessary that both the husband and wife possess the capacity for testimony, because testimony is a pillar in Li'an. And it is also necessary that the woman be such that her accuser is subject to hadd, because Li'an takes the place of hadd of qadhf for the husband, so it is necessary that the woman be muhsanah (chaste and married). And also, denying the lineage of a child makes Li'an obligatory. Because when the husband denies the lineage of his wife's child and says that this child is not from my sperm, he becomes an accuser of that woman. Just as if a stranger denies a child's lineage from its known father, that stranger will be considered an accuser of the woman, similarly here. (The phrase) 'And possibility is not considered' is the answer to a question. The question is: If the husband denies the lineage of his wife's father, Li'an should not become obligatory, because it is possible that this child is not his son and his wife is not an adulteress, for example, if she had intercourse under a doubtful contract (shubha). The gist of the answer is that this doubt is not valid because there is consensus (ijma) that if a stranger denies a child's lineage from its known father, that stranger will be a qadhif (accuser), even if that possibility exists here as well.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof regarding the definition and conditions of Li'an (mutual imprecation). It begins by narrating the cause of revelation of the Li'an verse: a Companion asked the Prophet about a man who finds another man with his wife, facing a dilemma: if he kills him, he will be killed; if he speaks, he will be flogged (for qadhf); if he stays silent, he swallows his anger. The Prophet prayed, and the Li'an verse was revealed. Another narration mentions Hilal ibn Umayyah who accused his wife, and the Prophet demanded four witnesses. Thus, the original ruling for qadhf was the hadd punishment, but Li'an abrogated it for spouses. The text then contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions. According to the Hanafis, Li'an consists of testimonies (shahadat) strengthened by oaths, connected with the word 'curse'. According to Imam Shafi'i, Li'an are oaths strengthened by the word 'testimony'. The difference leads to different conditions: Hanafis require the spouses to be eligible for testimony (i.e., Muslim, adult, sane, just), while Shafi'is require eligibility for oaths. The proof for the Hanafi view is the Quranic verse: 'and they have no witnesses except themselves' – the husband is made a witness, so Li'an is testimony, not mere oaths. The Shafi'i inference from 'four testimonies by Allah' is that testimony here means oaths. The Hanafi response is that the verse explicitly mentions both testimony and oath, so the pillar is testimony supported by oath. The passage further explains why the wife's testimony uses 'wrath' instead of 'curse': women are prone to cursing, so using 'wrath' serves as a stronger deterrent. It then addresses the connection between Li'an and hadd: both serve as deterrents. Finally, it states conditions: both spouses must be capable of testimony, the wife must be muhsanah (chaste and married, so that false accusation would incur hadd), and denying a child's lineage triggers Li'an. A hypothetical objection about a possible shubha is rejected due to ijma that such denial makes one a qadhif.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses where each swears oaths invoking curse/wrath, replacing hadd punishment.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a chaste person, punishable by hadd.
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony; in Li'an, the recitation of the specific oaths.
يمين (yamin): Oath sworn by Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the pillar (rukn) of Li'an?
A) Oaths (yamin) strengthened by testimony
B) Testimony (shahadah) strengthened by oaths
C) Simply four oaths without testimony
D) A single testimony without oaths

Key Takeaway
Li'an is testimony strengthened by oaths, replacing hadd punishments, and requires both spouses to be eligible for testimony.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Husband's Refusal to Perform Li'an: Imprisonment or Hadd?
Ruling on husband's refusal with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a husband who refuses li'an, explain the inter-madhhab dispute, and distinguish between li'an as a substitution vs. exemption.

Core Idea
Hanafi: imprison until li'an or retraction; Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali: flog with hadd.

When a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses, Islamic law offers li'an as a remedy. But what if he refuses? The Hanafi school holds that the judge imprisons him until he complies or retracts, while other schools insist on immediate hadd punishment. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and the basis of disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State that the husband is imprisoned until he performs li'an or retracts his accusation.
2
Understand the proof
The right of li'an is wajib on the husband and he is capable of fulfilling it, so imprisonment enforces that right.
This is a rational proof (istihsan) based on enforcing a right.
3
Contrast opposing schools
Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali view li'an as an exemption; refusal triggers the default hadd of qadhf.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi imprisonment vs. other school's flogging.
5
Recognize consensus on retraction
If the husband retracts, he is subject to hadd by consensus.
Retraction removes the cause of li'an.

شوہر لعان کرنے سے رک جائے تو حاکم اسے قید کر دے حتی کہ لعان کرے یا اپنے نفس کی تکذیب کرے
فان امتنع منه حبسه الحاكم حتى يلاعن او يكذب نفسه لانه حق مستحق عليه و هو قادر على ايفائه فيحبس به حتى ياتى بما هو عليه او يكذب نفسه ليرتفع السبب ولولا عن وجب عليها اللعان لماتلونا من النص الا انه يبتدأ بالزوج لانه هو المدعى
ترجمہ پھر اگر شوہر نے لعان کرنے سے انکار کر دیا تو حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ لعان کرے یا اپنے آپ کو جھوٹا بنا دے کیونکہ شوہر پر یہ حق واجب ہے اور وہ اس کو پورا کرنے پر قادر بھی ہے پس اس کے عوض قید کیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ شوہر ( یا ) تو اس کو پورا کرے جو اس پر واجب ہے یا اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے تا کہ سبب ہی دور ہو جائے اور اگر شوہر نے لعان کیا تو عورت پر بھی لعان کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ اس نص کی وجہ سے جو ہم تلاوت کر چکے ہیں مگر ابتداء شوہر سے کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہ مدعی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے لعان کرنے سے انکار کر دیا تو حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ لعان کرے یہ ہمارا مذ ہب ہے اور امام شافعی ، امام مالک، اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر حد جاری کی جائے گی ۔ بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک موجب قذف حد ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک لعان ہے یا وہ اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے پس اگر اس شخص نے اپنی تکذیب کر دی تو بالا تفاق اس پر حد قذف جاری کی جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر یہ حق یعنی لعان واجب ہے درانحالیکہ وہ اس کو پورا کر دینے پر قادر ہے۔ لہذا اس حق کی وجہ سے اس کو محبوس کر دیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ شوہر اس حق کو ادا کر دے یا اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے تا کہ لعان کا سبب مرتفع ہو جائے اور لعان کا سبب زوجین میں سے ایک کا دوسرے کی تکذیب کرنا ہے کیونکہ لعان اس وقت واجب ہو گا جب کہ شوہر اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگا دے اور پھر دونوں باہم ایک دوسرے کی تکذیب کریں ہاں اگر شوہر نے اپنی تکذیب کی تو تکاذب باقی نہ رہا بلکہ شوہر عورت کے موافق ہو گیا کہ اس نے زنا نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور اگر شوہر نے لعان کیا تو عورت پر بھی لعان کرنا واجب ہو گا دلیل وہ آیت ہے جو ہم تلاوت کر چکے یعنی فشهادة احد هم اربع الآية[؟] لیکن لعان کی ابتداء شوہر سے کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ شوہر ہی مدعی ہے اور لعان نام ہے شہادت کا اور شہادت کا مطالبہ مدعی سے ہوتا ہے
If the husband refrains from li'an, the judge should imprison him until he performs li'an or retracts his accusation. [Arabic matn] Then if he refrains from it, the judge imprisons him until he performs li'an or retracts, because it is a right owed to him [the wife] and he is capable of fulfilling it, so he is imprisoned for it until he does what is upon him or retracts so that the cause is removed. And if he performs li'an, then li'an becomes obligatory upon her due to the text we have recited, but the beginning is by the husband because he is the claimant. [Translation] Then if the husband refrained from li'an, the judge will imprison him until he performs li'an or makes himself false. Because this right is obligatory upon the husband and he is capable of fulfilling it, so he is imprisoned in lieu of it until the husband either fulfills what is upon him or retracts so that the cause is removed. And if the husband performed li'an, then li'an becomes obligatory upon the woman as well, due to this text we have recited, but the beginning is by the husband because he is the claimant. Explanation: The matter is that if the husband refrained from li'an, the judge will imprison him until he performs li'an. This is our madhhab. Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad say that hadd should be applied to him. The basis of difference is that with them, the consequence of qadhf is hadd, and with us it is li'an. Or he retracts; then if that person retracts, then by consensus the hadd of qadhf is applied to him. The proof is that this right, i.e., li'an, is obligatory upon the husband while he is capable of fulfilling it, so he is imprisoned for this right until the husband fulfills it or retracts so that the cause of li'an is removed. The cause of li'an is that one of the spouses accuses the other, because li'an becomes obligatory when the husband accuses his wife of zina and then both mutually accuse each other. Yes, if the husband retracts, then mutual accusation does not remain; rather the husband agrees with the woman that she did not commit zina. And if the husband performed li'an, then li'an becomes obligatory upon the woman as well; the proof is the verse we have recited: 'fa shahadatu ahadihim arba'a shahadatin...' But li'an begins by the husband because he is the claimant, and li'an is a type of testimony, and testimony is demanded from the claimant.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute regarding the consequence for a husband who refuses to perform li'an after accusing his wife of zina. The Hanafi ruling is clear: the judge imprisons the husband until he either performs li'an or retracts his accusation. The reasoning is that li'an is a right owed to the wife—it clears her from the stigma of adultery—and since the husband is capable of fulfilling it, he is compelled through imprisonment. The text also notes that if the husband retracts, he becomes subject to the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes) by consensus. The inter-madhhab dispute here is with the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools, who hold that the husband should be flogged with the hadd of qadhf immediately, because in their view the original punishment for qadhf is hadd, and li'an is merely an exemption for the husband; if he refuses, the default applies. The Hanafi counter is that li'an is a distinct substitution (khalaf) for hadd in the case of spouses, and it is a right of the wife, not a mere exemption. The passage also explains that if the husband does perform li'an, then li'an becomes obligatory on the wife as well, but the husband initiates because he is the claimant. All rulings here are from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of zina without witnesses, involving oaths and curses to establish the truth.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a married person (muhsan), punishable by hadd of 80 lashes.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shariah for certain crimes, e.g., 80 lashes for qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a husband who refuses to perform li'an after accusing his wife of zina?
A) He is imprisoned until he performs li'an or retracts his accusation.
B) He is flogged 80 lashes immediately.
C) His marriage is automatically annulled.
D) He is exiled from the community.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school enforces li'an through imprisonment to protect the wife's right, whereas other schools revert to hadd punishment.

Imprisoning the Wife Who Refuses Li'an: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Maliki Views
Ruling on wife's refusal with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a wife who refuses li'an, distinguish it from the Shafi'i/Maliki position, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) supporting the Hanafi view.

Core Idea
Imprisonment compels the wife to exercise her right of li'an—it does not presume guilt.

When a husband accuses his wife of zina and initiates li'an, the wife must also perform li'an to defend herself. If she refuses, the Hanafi school rules that she is imprisoned until she either performs li'an or confirms the accusation. This lesson examines the proof for this ruling and contrasts it with the Shafi'i/Maliki position, which would apply the hadd penalty for zina. Understanding the underlying rationale—that li'an is a wajib right she is capable of fulfilling—clarifies why imprisonment is the chosen compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage rules on the wife who refuses to perform li'an after the husband has performed his. The Hanafi ruling: the judge imprisons her until she performs li'an or confirms the husband's accusation.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is that li'an is a right (haqq) wajib upon the wife, and she is capable of fulfilling it. Therefore, imprisonment is a legitimate means to compel performance of a wajib act.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on legal obligation and capacity.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The link: Since li'an is wajib, the state has authority to enforce it. The wife's refusal does not invalidate the obligation; imprisonment pressures her to choose either li'an (clearing her) or tasdiq (confirming guilt, which then incurs hadd).
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Dispute)
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that the wife should not be imprisoned; rather, her refusal implies admission of zina, so the hadd of zina (flogging) is applied directly.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) because refusal could stem from various reasons; automatic hadd would be premature without giving the wife a chance to exercise her right of li'an.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر عورت لعان سے رک جائے حاکم اسے قید میں ڈال دے حتی کہ لعان کرے یا مرد کی تصدیق کرے
فان امتنعت حبسها الحاكم حتى تلاعن او تصدقه لانه حق مستحق عليها وهي قادرة على ايفائه فتحبس فيه ترجمہ پھر اگر عورت نے انکار کیا تو حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ لعان کرے یا مرد کے قول کو سچاہتا دے کیونکہ عورت پر یہ حق واجب ہے اور وہ اس کو پورا کرنے پر قادر بھی ہے تو اس کو اس حق میں قید کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح اگر عورت نے لعان کرنے سے انکار کر دیا تو حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ لعان کرے یا اپنے شوہر کی تصدیق کرے دلیل یہ ہے کہ لعان عورت پر بھی واجب ہے اور وہ اس کو پورا کرنے پر بھی قادر ہے اس وجہ سے اس حق میں اس کو قید کیا جائے گا امام شافعی اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ عورت کو قید نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ اس پر حد زنا جاری کی جائے گی۔
If the woman refrains from li'an, the judge puts her in prison until she performs li'an or confirms the man's statement. [Arabic matn] Then if she refrains, the judge imprisons her until she performs li'an or confirms him, because it is a right owed to her [the husband] and she is capable of fulfilling it, so she is imprisoned for it. [Translation] Then if the woman refused, the judge will imprison her until she performs li'an or confirms the man's statement, because this right is obligatory upon the woman and she is capable of fulfilling it, so she is imprisoned for this right. Explanation: If the woman refused to perform li'an, the judge will imprison her until she performs li'an or confirms her husband's statement. The proof is that li'an is also obligatory upon the woman, and she is capable of fulfilling it, so she is imprisoned for this right. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik said that the woman should not be imprisoned, but rather the hadd of zina should be applied to her.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling for when the wife refuses to perform li'an after the husband has initiated it. The Hanafi position is symmetrical: the wife is imprisoned until she either performs her part of li'an or confirms the husband's accusation (i.e., retracts her denial). The reasoning matches that for the husband: li'an is a right that is wajib upon her, and she is capable of fulfilling it, so imprisonment is the means of compulsion. The passage then notes a dispute with Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, who hold that the wife should not be imprisoned but rather flogged with the hadd of zina. This is because, in their view, the wife's refusal to perform li'an implies acceptance of the accusation, so she is liable for zina. The Hanafi school, however, does not jump to that conclusion; the wife may refuse for various reasons, and imprisonment is used to compel her to either swear (li'an) or admit guilt by confirming the husband. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
تصدیق (tasdiq): The wife confirming her husband's accusation, which ends the li'an process and subjects her to penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a wife who refuses to perform li'an after her husband has done so?
A) She is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms the accusation.
B) She is immediately flogged for zina.
C) She is divorced automatically.
D) She is given a monetary fine.

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment is not punishment but compulsion to fulfill the wajib right of li'an; the wife retains the option to clear herself via li'an or admit guilt.

Husband Unfit for Li'an: Slave, Kafir, or Previous Qadhf
Ruling when husband cannot perform li'an due to legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases where a husband cannot perform li'an and explain why hadd of qadhf applies instead.

Core Idea
When the husband lacks testimonial capacity, li'an is impossible and the original hadd of qadhf revives.

Li'an is a special procedure that allows a husband to accuse his wife of zina without the usual burden of four witnesses. However, li'an requires the husband to be eligible for testimony (shahada). This lesson examines three categories of husbands who lack that eligibility, leading to the application of the original punishment for qadhf: eighty lashes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three exceptional husbands
Note that all three categories (slave, disbeliever, mahrur) share a common feature: they lack full testimonial capacity as per Hanafi law.
Testimonial capacity is a condition for li'an.
2
Locate the original ruling on qadhf
The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nur, 24:4) establishes the hadd of 80 lashes for false accusation. This is the original consequence (mu'jib asli).
The imperative 'fajlidoohum' indicates obligation.
3
Understand the relationship between li'an and hadd
Li'an is a substitute (khalaf) for the hadd specifically for spouses, but it requires the husband to be eligible for testimony. When that condition is absent, the original hadd applies.
Substitute operates only when its conditions are met.
4
Apply the principle: revert to the original
If li'an is impossible due to a deficiency in the husband (lack of testimonial capacity), recourse is made to the original ruling of hadd.
The deficiency is from his side, not the wife's.
5
Consider why testimonial capacity is necessary
Li'an involves swearing oaths akin to testimony; hence the husband must be legally eligible to testify. Slaves, disbelievers, and those punished for qadhf are disqualified.
This is based on general principles of shahada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر اگر غلام ہو یا کافر یا محدود فی القذف ہوا اپنی عورت پر تہمت لگائے اس پر حد ہے
واذا كان الزوج عبدا او كافرا او محدودا في قذف فقذف امرأته فعليه الحد لانه تعذر اللعان لمعنى من جهته فيصار الى الموجب الاصلى و هو الثابت بقوله تعالى والذين يرمون المحصنت الآية واللعان خلف عنه
ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر غلام ہو یا کافر ہو یا وہ کسی کو تہمت لگانے میں مارا گیا ہو پس اس نے اپنی بیوی کو تہمت لگائی تو اس پر حد واجب ہوگی کیونکہ لعان متعذر ہو گیا ایک معنی کی وجہ سے جو اسی کی طرف سے ہے پس موجب اصلی کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور وہ اللہ تعالی کے قول والذين يرمون المحصنت سے ثابت ہے اور لعان اس کا خلیفہ ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر غلام ہو یا کافر ہو اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ زوجین دونوں کافر ہیں ۔ پھر عورت مسلمان ہو گئی اور شوہر پر اسلام پیش کرنے سے پہلے شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگادی۔ یا شوہر ایسا ہے کہ تہمت لگانے کی وجہ سے اس کو حد قذف ماری گئی ہے۔ ان تینوں صورتوں میں اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگا دی تو اس پر لعان واجب نہیں ہوگا بلکہ حد قذف واجب ہوگی۔ لعان کا واجب کرنا تو اس لئے ممتنع ہو گیا کہ یہ شخص شہادت کا اہل نہیں رہا حالانکہ لعان کرنے والے کے لئے شہادت کا اہل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پس جب لعان کرنا ممتنع ہو گیا تو موجب اصلی یعنی حد قذف کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور حد قذف باری تعالیٰ کے قول
الذين يرمون المحصنات ثم لم ياتوا باربعة شهداء فاجلدو هم ثمانين جلدة ولا تقبلو الهم شهادة ابدا سے ثابت ہے یعنی اس آیت کی وجہ سے اولا تو حد قذف ہی مشروع کی گئی تھی پھر شوہر کے اپنی بیوی کو تہمت لگانے کی صورت میں لعان حد قذف کا نائب اور خلیفہ ہو گیا ہے پس اگر شرط لعان کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے لعان متعذر ہو جائے تو موجب اصلی یعنی حد قذف کی طرف رجوع
کیا جائے گا۔
If the husband is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf, and he accuses his wife, then hadd is upon him. [Arabic matn] And if the husband is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf, then he accuses his wife, then hadd is upon him because li'an is prevented due to a meaning from his side, so recourse is made to the original consequence, which is established by Allah's saying: 'And those who accuse chaste women...' and li'an is a substitute for it. [Translation] And if the husband is a slave, or a disbeliever, or he has been flogged for accusing someone, then he accused his wife, then hadd is obligatory upon him because li'an became impossible due to a meaning from his side, so recourse is made to the original consequence, which is established by Allah's saying: 'And those who accuse chaste women...' and li'an is a substitute for it. Explanation: The situation is that if the husband is a slave, or a disbeliever—this occurs when both spouses are disbelievers, then the woman became Muslim and before presenting Islam to the husband, he accused his wife of zina—or the husband is one who has been flogged for qadhf. In these three situations, if the husband accuses his wife of zina, li'an is not wajib upon him, but rather hadd of qadhf is wajib. The obligation of li'an becomes impossible because this person is no longer eligible for testimony (shahada), while it is necessary for the one performing li'an to be eligible for testimony. So when li'an becomes impossible, recourse is made to the original consequence, i.e., hadd of qadhf. And the hadd of qadhf is established by Allah's saying: 'Those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony...' This means that originally hadd of qadhf was legislated, then in the case of a husband accusing his wife, li'an became the deputy and substitute for hadd of qadhf. So if the condition of li'an is absent, causing li'an to be impossible, then recourse is made to the original consequence, i.e., hadd of qadhf.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining when the husband's accusation of his wife results in hadd of qadhf rather than li'an. The key principle is that li'an is a substitute (khalaf) for the hadd of qadhf, but it requires the husband to be eligible for testimony (shahada). Three categories of husbands are ineligible for testimony: slaves, disbelievers, and those previously punished for qadhf (who have lost their testimonial capacity). In these cases, li'an is not possible, so the original punishment of 80 lashes applies. The proof cited is the Quranic verse on qadhf (Surah al-Nur, ayah 4), which establishes the hadd, and the rule that li'an is a substitution legislated specifically for spouses. The passage clarifies that the ruling applies in specific scenarios: e.g., both spouses were originally kafir, then the wife became Muslim, and the husband accused her before he was given the option to accept Islam; or the husband is a slave; or he has been punished for qadhf (mahrur). All these individuals lack the testimonial capacity required for li'an. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
محدود فی القذف (mahrur fi al-qadhf): A person who has already been punished with the hadd of qadhf, thus losing testimonial capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which husband cannot perform li'an and instead faces hadd of qadhf according to the Hanafi school?
A) A husband who is a slave.
B) A husband who is a minor child.
C) A husband who is blind.
D) A husband who is poor.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a substitute for hadd of qadhf, but requires testimonial capacity; without it, the original hadd applies.

Hadd Applies When Husband is Unqualified for Li'an
Ruling that hadd for qadhf applies when husband is slave, kafir, or previously punished for qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios where a husband cannot perform li'an and explain why hadd for qadhf becomes wajib instead, citing Quran 24:4 as the original dalil.

Core Idea
Li'an is a substitute; if the husband is unfit for testimony, the original hadd for qadhf revives.

The institution of li'an provides a special procedure for a husband who accuses his wife of zina, allowing the couple to avoid the hadd penalty. However, this alternative is not available to every husband. This passage from the Hanafi tradition outlines three cases where the husband's personal status disqualifies him from performing li'an, causing the original penalty for false accusation (hadd al-qadhf) to become binding. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly applying the law of hudud in marital accusations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exceptions
The passage states that normally li'an replaces hadd for a husband's accusation, but in three specific cases, hadd applies instead. Identify these cases.
2
Determine the underlying condition
All three cases share a common deficiency: the husband is not qualified for shahada (testimony). Explain why shahada qualification is necessary for li'an.
Li'an involves swearing oaths that serve as testimony; thus ahl al-shahada is required.
3
Locate the original dalil
The Quranic verse 24:4 establishes the original hadd for qadhf. Recognize that li'an is a substitute (khalaf) for this rule.
This verse gives the general penalty for false accusation.
4
Apply the principle of substitution
When the substitute (li'an) is impossible due to a defect in the husband, the original ruling (hadd) is reintroduced. This is the core legal reasoning.
The principle is that the original obligation revives when the exceptional alternative fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر اگر غلام ہو یا کا فریا محدود فی القذف ہوا اپنی عورت پر تہمت لگائے اس پر حد ہے واذا كان الزوج عبدا او كافرا او محدودا في قذف فقذف امرأته فعليه الحد لانه تعذر اللعان لمعنى من جهته فيصار الى الموجب الاصلى و هو الثابت بقوله تعالى والذين يرمون المحصنت الآية واللعان خلف عنه ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر غلام ہو یا کافر ہو یا وہ کسی کو تہت دینے میں مارا گیا ہو پس اس نے اپنی بیوی کو تہمت لگائی تو اس پر حد واجب ہوگی کیونکہ لعان متعذر ہو گیا ایک معنی کی وجہ سے جو اسی کی طرف سے ہے پس موجب اصلی کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور وہ اللہ تعالی کے قول والذين يرمون المحصنت سے ثابت ہے اور لعان اس کا خلیفہ ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر غلام ہو یا کافر ہو اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ زوجین دونوں کا فر ہیں ۔ پھر عورت مسلمان ہو گئی اور شوہر پر اسلام پیش کرنے سے پہلے شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگادی۔ یا شوہر ایسا ہے کہ تہمت لگانے کی وجہ سے اس کو حد قذف ماری گئی ہے۔ ان تینوں صورتوں میں اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگا دی تو اس پر لعان واجب نہیں ہوگا بلکہ حد قذف واجب ہوگی۔ لعان کا واجب کرنا تو اس لئے ممتنع ہو گیا کہ یہ شخص شہادت کا اہل نہیں رہا حالانکہ لعان کرنے والے کے لئے شہادت کا اہل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پس جب لعان کرنا ممتنع ہو گیا تو موجب اصلی یعنی حد قذف کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور حد قذف باری تعالیٰ کے قول الذين يرمون المحصنات ثم لم ياتوا باربعة شهداء فاجلدو هم ثمانين جلدة ولا تقبلو الهم شهادة ابدا سے ثابت ہے یعنی اس آیت کی وجہ سے اولا تو حد قذف ہی مشروع کی گئی تھی پھر شوہر کے اپنی بیوی کو تہمت لگانے کی صورت میں لعان حد قذف کا نائب اور خلیفہ ہو گیا ہے پس اگر شر ط لعان کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے لعان مستعد رہو جائے تو موجب اصلی یعنی حد قذف کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
If the husband is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf (false accusation), and he accuses his wife, then hadd is obligatory upon him. The Arabic: 'If the husband is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf, and he accuses his wife, then he is subject to hadd, because li'an is prevented due to a cause from his side, so recourse is had to the original cause (hadd), which is established by Allah's statement: 'And those who accuse chaste women...' and li'an is a substitute for it.' Translation: And if the husband is a slave, or a disbeliever, or he has been flogged for false accusation, then he accused his wife, so hadd is obligatory upon him, because li'an has become prevented due to a meaning from his side, so recourse is had to the original obligation, which is established by Allah's statement 'And those who accuse chaste women...' and li'an is its deputy. Explanation: The scenario: If the husband is a slave or a disbeliever – the case is that both spouses are disbelievers, then the wife became Muslim and before the husband was offered Islam, he accused her of zina. Or the husband is one who had been given hadd for qadhf. In these three cases, if the husband accuses his wife of zina, li'an is not wajib, rather hadd for qadhf is wajib. Li'an is prevented because this person is not qualified for shahada (witnessing), whereas for li'an, the performer must be qualified for shahada. So when li'an is prevented, recourse is had to the original cause, i.e., hadd for qadhf, and hadd for qadhf is established by Allah's statement: 'Those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony forever.' That is, by this verse, originally hadd for qadhf was legislated; then in the case of a husband accusing his wife, li'an became a substitute for hadd. So if li'an becomes prevented due to the absence of its condition, recourse is had to the original, i.e., hadd for qadhf.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage details three scenarios where a husband cannot perform li'an: if he is a slave, a disbeliever, or one who has already received the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf). In each case, the husband's accusation of his wife's zina does not lead to li'an; instead, he is subject to the hadd penalty for qadhf. The reason is that li'an requires the husband to be qualified to give testimony (shahada), and these individuals lack that qualification. Since li'an is a substitute for the original hadd (which is established by Quran 24:4), when the substitute cannot be applied due to a deficiency in the husband, the original ruling (hadd) is implemented. The commentary explains the specific scenarios: a slave husband with a non-Muslim wife who later converts, a non-Muslim husband before his conversion, and a husband who had previously been punished for qadhf. In all, the principle is that alternative procedures (li'an) only apply when the conditions for them are met; otherwise, the default ruling remains.

Key Terms
حد قذف (hadd al-qadhf): Eighty lashes for falsely accusing a chaste person of adultery without four witnesses.
شہادت کا اہل (ahl al-shahada): Legally qualified to give testimony; for li'an, the husband must be a free Muslim not previously punished for qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases does a husband who accuses his wife of zina face hadd for qadhf instead of performing li'an?
A) Husband is a free Muslim and wife is a slave.
B) Husband is a slave or a disbeliever or previously punished for qadhf.
C) Husband is a minor or insane.
D) Wife is a minor or insane.

Key Takeaway
When a husband is unqualified for li'an due to slavery, disbelief, or prior qadhf, the original hadd for false accusation becomes obligatory, demonstrating that procedural alternatives do not eliminate the underlying penal obligation.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
No Hadd nor Li'an When Wife is Unqualified
Ruling that hadd and li'an drop when wife lacks ihsan or shahada qualification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which hadd for qadhf and li'an are lifted, and apply the Hanafi reasoning using the hadith of the four women.

Core Idea
If the wife is not muhsana, no hadd and no li'an — because both rely on her being a chaste, free Muslim.

In Hanafi fiqh, the hadd punishment for false accusation of zina (qadhf) and the procedure of li'an are strict protections for the chaste. But what if the wife herself does not qualify for that protection? This passage clarifies that when the wife is a slave, a non-Muslim, a known adulteress, a minor, or insane, the husband's accusation triggers neither hadd nor li'an. The Prophet himself listed four categories of women with whom li'an does not occur, and the reasoning extends to all similar cases where the wife lacks ihsan or the capacity for testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's legal capacity
First, assume the husband is qualified for shahada (free, adult Muslim, not previously punished for qadhf). This is the default in the text.
If the husband himself is not qualified (e.g., a slave or previously punished), different rulings apply.
2
Identify the wife's disqualifying attributes
The text lists several: being a slave, a disbeliever, one already punished for qadhf, a minor, insane, or an adulteress. Also included in the hadith: a free woman married to a slave.
These attributes make the wife lacking in ihsan (chastity or free status) or ahl al-shahada (competence to testify).
3
Understand the twin reasons for the ruling
Hadd for qadhf requires the accuser to have accused a muhsana (free, Muslim, chaste adult). Li'an requires both spouses to be competent for shahada. If the wife lacks either, the punishment/procedure drops.
The ruling is not about the husband's innocence but the wife's ineligibility to be the victim of qadhf.
4
Apply the hadith evidence
The Prophet explicitly said there is no li'an for four types of women: Jewess, Christian, slave, and free woman married to a slave. The text uses this hadith, transmitted by Abu Bakr al-Razi, as the primary dalil.
The hadith directly negates li'an. Since li'an replaces hadd when the wife could testify but refuses, removing li'an also removes hadd.
5
Note the exception when both are punished for qadhf
If both the husband and wife have previously been punished for qadhf, then hadd is imposed on the husband upon accusation, because the wife is no longer considered muhsana? Actually the text says 'and if both are from among those punished for qadhf, then hadd is upon him.' This is a specific exception.
This is a separate case where the ruling differs; ensure not to confuse with the main rule.

نکاح میں ہو۔ یہ حدیث حدیث کی مشہور کتابوں میں مذکور نہیں ہے مگر ابو بکر رازی نے اس کو مختصر الطحاوی کی اپنی شرط میں ذکر کیا ہے اور ابو بکر رازی عدات اللہ اور ضبط میں مقتدیل اور پیشوا کی حیثیت رکھتے If the husband is from among those qualified for shahada, and the wife is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf, or she is from among those whose accuser is not subjected to hadd, such as a minor, insane, or an adulteress, then there is no hadd upon the husband and no li'an. The Arabic: 'And if he is from among those qualified for shahada, and she is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one punished for qadhf, or she is from among those whose accuser is not punished with hadd, such as a minor, insane, or adulteress, then there is no hadd upon him and no li'an, because the qualification for shahada and ihsan are absent on her side, and li'an is prevented due to a cause from her side, so the hadd falls, just as if she confirmed him. The basis for this is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Four (women) between whom and their husbands there is no li'an: the Jewess under a Muslim, the Christian under a Muslim, the female slave under a free man, and the free woman under a slave.' And if both are from among those punished for qadhf, then hadd is upon him.' Translation: And if the husband is qualified for shahada, and the wife is a slave, or a disbeliever, or has been punished for qadhf, or is a woman whose accuser is not punished with hadd – such as a minor, insane woman, or adulteress – then there is no hadd upon the husband and no li'an. Because both qualification for shahada and ihsan are absent on her side, and li'an is prevented due to a cause from her side, so the hadd drops, just as if she confirmed his statement. And the basis in this is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Four (categories of women) there is no li'an between them and their husbands: the Jewess married to a Muslim, the Christian married to a Muslim, the slave woman married to a free man, and the free woman married to a slave.' ... This hadith is not mentioned in the famous books of hadith, but Abu Bakr al-Razi mentioned it in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, and Abu Bakr al-Razi is reliable and accurate, so this hadith can be used as evidence.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage discusses cases where the husband is qualified for shahada (free, Muslim, not previously punished for qadhf) but the wife is not legally protected. The wife may be a slave, a disbeliever, one who has already been punished for qadhf, or a woman against whom hadd is not applicable – such as a minor, insane woman, or an adulteress. In all these cases, neither hadd for qadhf nor li'an is imposed on the husband. The reasons are twofold: (1) the wife is not qualified to give testimony (ahl al-shahada), which is a requirement for li'an to be wajib on her, and (2) she is not muhsana (chaste and free), so the hadd for qadhf does not become obligatory on the accuser (since the verse specifies 'chaste women'). The result is similar to when the wife confirms the husband's accusation, which also drops the hadd. The author then cites a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) listing four types of women with whom li'an does not occur: Jewess, Christian, slave woman, and free woman married to a slave. This hadith is used as the primary evidence. The commentator notes that this hadith is not found in the major hadith collections but is mentioned by Abu Bakr al-Razi, a reliable scholar. Thus, the ruling stands that if the wife is in one of these categories, no hadd and no li'an apply.

Key Terms
محصنہ (muhsana): A chaste, free, Muslim woman; against false accusation of such a woman, hadd for qadhf is wajib.
قاذف (qadhdhif): One who accuses another of adultery; in this context, the husband is the qadhdhif of his wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, in which of the following cases does no hadd and no li'an occur?
A) Wife is a free Muslim woman, husband is a slave.
B) Wife is a Jewish woman married to a Muslim man.
C) Wife is a previously punished for qadhf, husband is a free Muslim.
D) Both husband and wife are free Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for qadhf and li'an both fall when the wife is not muhsana or not competent for shahada, as proven by the hadith of the four women.
